   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">Wikipedia:Manual of Style</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Style guide for all Wikipedia articles and editable reader-facing content
      </div> 
      <p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p> 
      <table class="plainlinks ombox ombox-notice" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Blue_check.svg/30px-Blue_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="30" height="30" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Blue_check.svg/45px-Blue_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Blue_check.svg/60px-Blue_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div style="padding-top: 6px; padding-bottom: 5px;">
           <b>This <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Policies_and_guidelines#guide" title="Wikipedia:Policies and guidelines">guideline</a> is a part of the English Wikipedia's Manual of Style</b>.
           <br>
           <div style="font-size: 90%;">
             It is a generally accepted standard that editors should attempt to follow, though it is best treated with <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:What_%22Ignore_all_rules%22_means#Use_common_sense" title="Wikipedia:What &quot;Ignore all rules&quot; means">common sense</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Ignore_all_rules" title="Wikipedia:Ignore all rules">occasional exceptions</a> may apply. Any <i>substantive</i> edit to this page should reflect <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Consensus" title="Wikipedia:Consensus">consensus</a>. When in doubt, discuss first on the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia_talk:Manual_of_Style" title="Wikipedia talk:Manual of Style">talk page</a>.
           </div>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-imageright"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1007196855">.mw-parser-output .module-shortcutboxplain{float:right;margin:0 0 0 1em;border:1px solid #aaa;background:#fff;padding:0.3em 0.6em 0.2em 0.6em;text-align:center;font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .module-shortcutboxleft{float:left;margin:0 1em 0 0}.mw-parser-output .module-shortcutlist{display:inline-block;border-bottom:1px solid #aaa;margin-bottom:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .module-shortcutboxplain>ul{font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .module-shortcutanchordiv{position:relative;top:-3em}.mw-parser-output li .module-shortcutanchordiv{float:right}.mw-parser-output .mbox-imageright .module-shortcutboxplain{padding:0.4em 1em 0.4em 1em;line-height:1.3}</style>
          <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
           <span id="WP:MOS"></span>
          </div>
          <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
           <div class="module-shortcutlist">
            <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
           </div>
           <ul>
            <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikipedia:MOS&amp;redirect=no">WP:MOS</a></span></li>
           </ul>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>

      <p>The <b>Manual of Style</b> (<b>MoS</b> or <b>MOS</b>) is the <a href="/wiki/Style_manual" class="mw-redirect" title="Style manual">style manual</a> for all English Wikipedia <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:What_is_an_article%3F" title="Wikipedia:What is an article?">articles</a>. However, accessibility guidelines apply across the entire project. This primary page is supported by further <a href="/wiki/Category:Wikipedia_Manual_of_Style" title="Category:Wikipedia Manual of Style">detail pages</a>, which are cross-referenced here and listed at <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Contents" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Contents">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Contents</a>. If any contradiction arises, <em>this page has precedence</em>.<sup id="cite_ref-CONLEVEL_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CONLEVEL-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Clarity"></span>MoS presents <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Style_guide" title="Style guide">house style</a> to assist <a href="/wiki/Wikipedians" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedians">its volunteer editors</a> write and maintain articles with precise and consistent language, layout, and formatting. Since using <a href="/wiki/Plain_English" title="Plain English">plain English</a> makes the encyclopedia easier and more intuitive to read, editors should avoid <a href="/wiki/Ambiguity" title="Ambiguity">ambiguity</a>, <a href="#Technical_language">jargon</a>, and vague or unnecessarily complex wording. </p>
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Stability"></span>Where more than one style or format is acceptable under MoS, one should be used consistently within an article and <a href="#Retaining_existing_styles">should not be changed</a> without good reason. <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Edit_warring" title="Wikipedia:Edit warring">Edit warring</a> over optional styles is unacceptable.<sup id="cite_ref-ew_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ew-2">[2]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>New content added to this page should directly address a <em>persistently recurring</em> style issue. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Retaining_existing_styles">Retaining existing styles</span></h2> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:VAR"></span><span id="MOS:STYLEVAR"></span><span id="MOS:STYLERET"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:VAR&amp;redirect=no">MOS:VAR</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:STYLEVAR&amp;redirect=no">MOS:STYLEVAR</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:STYLERET&amp;redirect=no">MOS:STYLERET</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>Sometimes the MoS provides more than one acceptable style or gives no specific guidance. The <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Arbitration_Committee" title="Wikipedia:Arbitration Committee">Arbitration Committee</a> has expressed the principle that "When either of two styles are acceptable it is inappropriate for a Wikipedia editor to change from one style to another unless there is some substantial reason for the change."<sup id="cite_ref-ArbCom_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArbCom-3">[3]</a></sup> If you believe an alternative style would be more appropriate for a particular article, discuss this at the article's talk page or&nbsp; if it raises an issue of more general application or with the MoS itself&nbsp; at <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia_talk:Manual_of_Style" title="Wikipedia talk:Manual of Style">Wikipedia talk:Manual of Style</a>. </p>
      <p>Edit-warring over style, or enforcing optional style in a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Bot_policy#Assisted_editing_guidelines" title="Wikipedia:Bot policy">bot-like</a> fashion without prior consensus, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Disruptive_editing" title="Wikipedia:Disruptive editing">is never acceptable</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ew_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ew-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bot-like_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bot-like-4">[4]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1015928993">.mw-parser-output div.crossreference{padding-left:0}</style><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">For retention of an article's established dialect of English (and potential reasons to change it), see <a href="#National_varieties_of_English">&nbsp;National varieties of English</a>.</span> </p> 
      <h2><span id="Article_titles.2C_headings.2C_and_sections"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Article_titles,_headings,_and_sections">Article titles, headings, and sections</span></h2> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:AT"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:AT&amp;redirect=no">MOS:AT</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Article_titles">Article titles</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Article_titles" title="Wikipedia:Article titles">Wikipedia:Article titles</a>
      </div> 
      <p>A title should be a recognizable name or description of the topic that is natural, sufficiently precise, concise, and consistent with those of related articles. If these criteria are in conflict, they should be <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Common_sense" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Common sense">balanced</a> against one another. </p>
      <p>For formatting guidance see the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Article_titles#Article_title_format" title="Wikipedia:Article titles">Wikipedia:Article titles &nbsp;Article title format</a> section, noting the following: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Capitalize the initial letter (except in rare cases, such as <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">eBay</span>), but otherwise follow <a href="/wiki/Sentence_case" class="mw-redirect" title="Sentence case">sentence case</a><sup id="cite_ref-Sentence_case_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sentence_case-5">[a]</a></sup> (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Funding of UNESCO projects</span>), not title case (<span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Funding of UNESCO Projects</span>), except where title case would be expected were the title to occur in ordinary prose. See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(capitalization)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (capitalization)">Wikipedia:Naming conventions (capitalization)</a>.</li> 
       <li>To italicize, add <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Italic_title" title="Template:Italic title">italic title</a>}}</code> near the top of the article. For mixed situations, use, e.g., <code>{{DISPLAYTITLE:?Interpretations of ''2001: A Space Odyssey''}}</code>, instead. Use of italics should conform to <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Text_formatting#Italic_type" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting &nbsp;Italic type</a>.</li> 
       <li>Do not use <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">A</span>, <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">An</span>, or <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">The</span> as the first word (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Economy of the Second Empire</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">The economy of the Second Empire</span>), unless it is an inseparable part of a name (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The Hague</span>) or title of a work (<i><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">A Clockwork Orange</span></i>, <i><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The Simpsons</span></i>).</li> 
       <li>Normally use <a href="/wiki/Noun" title="Noun">nouns</a> or <a href="/wiki/Noun_phrase" title="Noun phrase">noun phrases</a>: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Early life</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">In early life</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[b]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>The final character should not be punctuation unless it is an inseparable part of a name (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><a href="/wiki/Saint-Louis-du-Ha!_Ha!" title="Saint-Louis-du-Ha! Ha!">Saint-Louis-du-Ha! Ha!</a></span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i><a href="/wiki/Do_Androids_Dream_of_Electric_Sheep%3F" title="Do Androids Dream of Electric Sheep?">Do Androids Dream of Electric Sheep?</a></i></span>) or an abbreviation (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><a href="/wiki/Inverness_City_F.C." title="Inverness City F.C.">Inverness City F.C.</a></span>), or when a closing round bracket or quotation mark is required (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><a href="/wiki/John_Palmer_(1814_schooner)" title="John Palmer (1814 schooner)"><i>John Palmer</i> (1814 schooner)</a></span>).</li> 
       <li>Whenever quotation marks or apostrophes appear, add a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Redirect" title="Wikipedia:Redirect">redirect</a> for the same title using apostrophes.<sup id="cite_ref-curlyq_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-curlyq-7">[c]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Subject both to the above and to <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Article_titles" title="Wikipedia:Article titles">Wikipedia:Article titles</a>, the rest of the MoS, particularly <a href="#Punctuation">&nbsp;Punctuation</a>, applies also to the title. </p>
      <p>
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">See also <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Titles" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Titles">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Titles</a>, for cases where a Wikipedia article about a published work has a title that coincides with the work's title.</span> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Section_organization">Section organization</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:SO"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:SO&amp;redirect=no">MOS:SO</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Layout" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Layout">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Layout</a>
      </div> 
      <p>An article's content should begin with an introductory <em>lead section</em>&nbsp; a concise summary of the article&nbsp; which is never divided into sections 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Lead_section" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Lead section">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Lead section</a>)</span>. The remainder of the article is typically divided into <a href="/wiki/Help:Section" title="Help:Section">sections</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Infoboxes" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Infoboxes">Infoboxes</a>, images, and related content in the lead section must be right-aligned. </p>
      <p>Certain standardized elements that are not sections go at the very top of the article, before the content of the lead section, and in the following order: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>A <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Short_description" title="Wikipedia:Short description">Wikipedia:Short description</a>, with the <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Short_description" title="Template:Short description">Short description</a>}}</code> template.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Hatnote" title="Wikipedia:Hatnote">disambiguation hatnotes</a></li> 
       <li>No-output templates that indicate the article's established date format and English-language variety, if any (e.g., <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Use_DMY_dates" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Use DMY dates">Use DMY dates</a>}}</code>, <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Use_Canadian_English" title="Template:Use Canadian English">Use Canadian English</a>}}</code>)</li> 
       <li>Banner-type <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Template_index/Disputes" title="Wikipedia:Template index/Disputes">Dispute</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Template_index/Cleanup" title="Wikipedia:Template index/Cleanup">Cleanup templates</a> for article-wide issues that have been flagged (otherwise used at the top of a specific section, after any sectional hatnote such as <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Main" title="Template:Main">main</a>}}</code>)</li> 
       <li>An <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Infoboxes" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Infoboxes">infobox</a>, which is optional (except in special cases like <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Taxobox" title="Template:Taxobox">Taxobox</a>}}</code> and <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Chembox" title="Template:Chembox">Chembox</a>}}</code>, or a variant thereof, at applicable articles); usually also includes the first image</li> 
       <li>An introductory image, when an infobox is not used, or an additional image is desired for the lead section (for unusually long leads, a second image might be mid-way through the lead text)</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>If an article has at least four section headings, a navigable <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Table_of_contents" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Table of contents">table of contents</a> appears automatically, just after the lead. </p>
      <p>If the topic of a section is covered in more detail in a dedicated article 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Summary_style" title="Wikipedia:Summary style">Wikipedia:Summary style</a>)</span>, insert <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Main" title="Template:Main">main</a>|<var style="padding-right: 1px;">Article name</var>}}</code> immediately under the section heading. </p>
      <p>As explained in detail in <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Layout#Standard_appendices_and_footers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Layout">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Layout &nbsp;Standard appendices and footers</a>, several kinds of material (mostly optional) may appear after the main body of the article, in the following order: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Books or other works created by the subject of the article, under a section heading "Works", "Publications", "Discography", "Filmography", etc. as appropriate (avoid "Bibliography", confusable with reference citations)</li> 
       <li>Internal links to related English Wikipedia articles, with section heading "See also"</li> 
       <li>Notes and references, with a section heading "Notes" or "References" (usually the latter), or a separate section for each in this order 
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">Wikipedia:Citing sources</a>)</span>; avoid "Bibliography", confusable with the subject's works</li> 
       <li>Relevant books, articles, or other publications that have not been used as sources; use the section heading "Further reading"; be highly selective, as <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOT#DIRECTORY" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOT">Wikipedia is not a bibliographic directory</a></li> 
       <li>Relevant <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:External_links" title="Wikipedia:External links">and appropriate</a> websites that have not been used as sources and do not appear in the earlier appendices, using the heading "External links", which may be made a subsection of "Further reading" (or such links can be integrated directly into the "Further reading" list instead); <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Layout#Links_to_sister_projects" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Layout">link templates for sister-project content</a> also usually go at the top of this section when it is present (otherwise in the last section on the page)</li> 
       <li>The following final items never take section headings 
        <ul>
         <li>Internal links organized into <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NAVBOX" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NAVBOX">navigational boxes</a></li> 
         <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Stub_sorting" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Stub sorting">Stub templates</a>, if needed</li> 
         <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Authority_control" title="Wikipedia:Authority control">Wikipedia:Authority control</a> metadata, if needed, using <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Authority_control" title="Template:Authority control">Authority control</a>}}</code> (distinguishes uses of the same name for two subjects, or multiple names for one subject)</li> 
         <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Categorization" title="Wikipedia:Categorization">Categories</a>, which should be the very last material in the article's source code.</li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Stand-alone_lists" title="Wikipedia:Stand-alone lists">Stand-alone list articles</a> have some additional layout considerations. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Section_headings">Section headings</span></h3> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Section_management"></span>
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855"></p>
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:HEAD"></span><span id="MOS:HEADINGS"></span><span id="MOS:SECTIONS"></span><span id="WP:SECTIONHEAD"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:HEAD&amp;redirect=no">MOS:HEAD</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:HEADINGS&amp;redirect=no">MOS:HEADINGS</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:SECTIONS&amp;redirect=no">MOS:SECTIONS</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikipedia:SECTIONHEAD&amp;redirect=no">WP:SECTIONHEAD</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Help:Section" title="Help:Section">Help:Section</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Accessibility#Headings" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility &nbsp;Headings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Layout#Order_of_article_elements" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Layout">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Layout &nbsp;Order of article elements</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Capital_letters#Section_headings" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters &nbsp;Section headings</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Section headings should follow all the guidance for <a href="#Article_titles">article titles</a> (above), and should be presented in <a href="/wiki/Sentence_case" class="mw-redirect" title="Sentence case">sentence case</a> (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Funding of UNESCO projects in developing countries</span>), not title case (<span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Funding of UNESCO Projects in Developing Countries</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-Sentence_case_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sentence_case-5">[a]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Use equals signs around a section heading: <code>==Title==</code> for a primary section, <code>===Title===</code> for a subsection, and so on to <code>======Title======</code>, with <a href="/wiki/MOS:GOODHEAD" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:GOODHEAD">no level skipped</a>. <code>=Title=</code> is never used.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[d]</a></sup> Spaces around the title <span class="nowrap">(<code>== Title ==</code>)</span> are optional and ignored. </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:BLANKLINE"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:BLANKLINE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:BLANKLINE</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>The heading must be on its own line, with one blank line just before it; a blank line just <i>after</i> is optional and ignored (but do not use <i>two</i> blank lines, before or after, because that will add unwanted visible space). </p>
      <p>Section headings should: </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:NOSECTIONLINKS"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:NOSECTIONLINKS&amp;redirect=no">MOS:NOSECTIONLINKS</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>Be unique within a page, so that section links lead to the right place.</li> 
       <li>Not contain links, especially where only part of a heading is linked.</li> 
       <li>Not contain images or <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Icons#Encyclopedic_purpose" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Icons">icons</a>.</li> 
       <li>Not contain <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Mathematics#Typesetting_of_mathematical_formulae" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Mathematics"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;math&gt;</code></a> markup.</li> 
       <li>Not contain citations or footnotes.</li> 
       <li>Not misuse <a href="/wiki/MOS:DLIST" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:DLIST">description list</a> markup ("<code>;</code>") to create <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Accessibility#Pseudo-headings" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility">pseudo-headings</a>.</li> 
       <li>Not contain template transclusions.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>These restrictions are necessary to avoid technical complications, and are not subject to override by local consensus. </p>
      <p><span class="anchor" id="SECTIONSTYLE"></span>In addition, as a matter of consistent style, section headings should: </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:SECTIONSTYLE"></span><span id="MOS:NOBACKREF"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:SECTIONSTYLE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:SECTIONSTYLE</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:NOBACKREF&amp;redirect=no">MOS:NOBACKREF</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>Not redundantly refer back to the subject of the article, e.g., <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Early life</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Smith's early life</span> or <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">His early life</span>.</li> 
       <li>Not refer to a higher-level heading, unless doing so is shorter or clearer.</li> 
       <li>Not be numbered or lettered as an outline.</li> 
       <li>Not be phrased as a question, e.g., <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Languages</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">What languages are spoken in Mexico?</span>.</li> 
       <li>Not use color or unusual fonts that might cause <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Accessibility#Headings" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility">accessibility problems</a>.</li> 
       <li>Not wrap headings in markup, which may break their display and also cause additional accessibility issues.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>These are broadly accepted community preferences. </p>
      <p>An <a href="#Invisible_comments">invisible comment</a> on the same line must be <em>inside</em> the <code>==&nbsp;==</code> markup:<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[e]</a></sup> </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996643573">.mw-parser-output .block-indent{padding-left:3em;padding-right:0;overflow:hidden}</style>
      <div class="block-indent">
       <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code>==Implications&lt;!--This comment works fine.--&gt;== </code></span>
       <br> 
       <p><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code>==&lt;!--This comment works fine.--&gt;Implications== </code></span><br> <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;"><code>==Implications==&lt;!--This comment causes problems.--&gt; </code></span><br> </p> <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;"><code>&lt;!--This comment breaks the heading completely.--&gt;==Implications== </code></span>
      </div> 
      <p>It is more usual practice to put such comments <em>below</em> the heading. </p>
      <p>Before changing a heading, consider whether you might be breaking existing links to it. If there are many <a href="/wiki/Help:Link#To_a_section" title="Help:Link">links to the old</a> title, create an <a href="/wiki/Help:Anchor" class="mw-redirect" title="Help:Anchor">anchor</a> with that title to ensure that these still work. Similarly, when linking to a section, leave an invisible comment at the heading of the target section, naming the linking articles, so that if the heading is later altered these can be fixed. Combined example: </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996643573">
      <div class="block-indent">
       <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code>=={{subst:<a href="/wiki/Template:Anchor" title="Template:Anchor">Anchor</a>|Consequences|reason=Old section name.}}Implications==<br>&lt;!-- Section linked from [[Richard Dawkins]], [[Daniel Dennett]]. --&gt;</code></span>
      </div> 
      <p>which will be saved in the article as: </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996643573">
      <div class="block-indent">
       <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code>==<code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr">&lt;span class="anchor" id="Consequences"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;</code>Implications==<br>&lt;!-- Section linked from [[Richard Dawkins]], [[Daniel Dennett]]. --&gt;</code></span>
      </div> 
      <p>The advantage of using <code>{{subst:Anchor}}</code>, or simply inserting the <code>&lt;span&gt;</code> tags directly, is that when edits are made to the section in the future, the anchor will not be included in page history entries as part of the section name. When <code>{{Anchor}}</code> is used directly, that undesirable behavior <i>does</i> occur. Note: if electing to insert the span directly, do not abbreviate it by using a self-closing tag, as in <code>==&lt;span id="Consequences" /&gt;Implications==</code>, since in HTML5 that XML-style syntax is valid only for certain tags, such as <span class="nowrap"><code>&lt;br /&gt;</code></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[5]</a></sup> See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Linking#Avoiding_broken_section_links" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Linking">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Linking &nbsp;Avoiding broken section links</a> for further discussion of this. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Heading-like_material">Heading-like material</span></h4> 
      <p>The above guidance about sentence case, redundancy, images, and questions also applies to <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Tables#Captions_and_headers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Tables">headers of tables</a> (and of table columns and rows). However, table headings can incorporate citations and may begin with, or be, numbers. Unlike page headings, table headers do not automatically generate link anchors. Aside from sentence case in glossaries, the heading advice also applies to the <i>term</i> entries in <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Lists#DLIST" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Lists">description lists</a>. If using <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Glossaries#Linking" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Glossaries">template-structured glossaries</a>, terms will automatically have link anchors, but will not otherwise. Citations for description-list content go in the <i>term</i> or <i>definition</i> element, as needed. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="National_varieties_of_English">National varieties of English</span></h2> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="WP:ENGVAR"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikipedia:ENGVAR&amp;redirect=no">WP:ENGVAR</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Article_titles#National_varieties_of_English" title="Wikipedia:Article titles">Wikipedia:Article titles &nbsp;National varieties of English</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Spelling" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Spelling">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Spelling</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The English Wikipedia prefers no national variety of English over any other. These varieties (for example <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American English</a> or <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a>) differ in vocabulary (<i>elevator</i> vs. <i>lift</i>), spelling (<i>center</i> vs. <i>centre</i>), and occasionally grammar 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="#Plurals">&nbsp;Plurals</a>, below)</span>. Articles such as <a href="/wiki/English_plurals" title="English plurals">English plurals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_American_and_British_English" title="Comparison of American and British English">Comparison of American and British English</a> provide information about such differences. </p>
      <p>An article's date formatting (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">June 6, 2021</span> vs. <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">6 June 2021</span>) is also related to national varieties of English&nbsp; see <a href="/wiki/MOS:DATEFORMAT" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:DATEFORMAT">MOS:DATEFORMAT</a> and especially <a href="/wiki/MOS:DATETIES" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:DATETIES">MOS:DATETIES</a> and <a href="/wiki/MOS:DATEVAR" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:DATEVAR">MOS:DATEVAR</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consistency_within_articles">Consistency within articles</span></h3> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Internal_consistency"></span> </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:ARTCON"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:ARTCON&amp;redirect=no">MOS:ARTCON</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Consistency" class="mw-disambig" title="Wikipedia:Consistency">Wikipedia:Consistency</a> for additional policies and guidelines on consistency.
      </div> 
      <p><em>Within a given article</em> the conventions of one particular variety of English should be followed consistently. Exceptions include: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><b>quotations, titles of works (books, films, etc.)</b> should be as given in the source (but see <a href="#Typographic_conformity">&nbsp;Typographic conformity</a>, below);</li> 
       <li><b>proper names</b> use the subject's own spelling, e.g., <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">joint project of the United States Department of Defense and the Australian Defence Force</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">International Labour Organization</span>;</li> 
       <li>For articles about <b>chemistry</b>-related topics, the international standard spellings <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">aluminium</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">sulfur</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">caesium</span> (and derivative terms) should be used, regardless of the national English variant employed in the article generally. See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(chemistry)#Element_names" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (chemistry)">Wikipedia:Naming conventions (chemistry) &nbsp;Element names</a>.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opportunities_for_commonality">Opportunities for commonality</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:COMMONALITY"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:COMMONALITY&amp;redirect=no">MOS:COMMONALITY</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>For an international encyclopedia, using vocabulary common to all varieties of English is preferable. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Use universally accepted terms rather than those less widely distributed, especially in titles. For example, <a href="/wiki/Glasses" title="Glasses"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">glasses</span></a> is preferred to the national varieties <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">spectacles</span> (<a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a>) and <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">eyeglasses</span> (<a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American English</a>); <a href="/wiki/Ten_million" class="mw-redirect" title="Ten million"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">ten million</span></a> is preferable to <a href="/wiki/Crore" title="Crore"><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">one crore</span></a> (<a href="/wiki/Indian_English" title="Indian English">Indian English</a>).</li> 
       <li>If one variant spelling appears in a title, make a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Redirect" title="Wikipedia:Redirect">redirect</a> page to accommodate the others, as with <a href="/wiki/Artefact" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Artefact">artefact</a> and <a href="/wiki/Artifact" class="mw-disambig" title="Artifact">artifact</a>, so that all variants can be used in searches and linking.</li> 
       <li>Terms that differ between varieties of English, or that have divergent meanings, may be <a href="/wiki/Gloss_(annotation)#In_linguistics" title="Gloss (annotation)">glossed</a> to prevent confusion, for example, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the trunk (American English) or boot (British English) of a car ...</span>.</li> 
       <li>Use a commonly understood word or phrase in preference to one that has a different meaning because of national differences (rather than <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">alternate</span>, use <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">alternative</span> or <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">alternating</span>, as appropriate).</li> 
       <li>When more than one variant spelling exists within a national variety of English, the most commonly used current variant should usually be preferred, except where the less common spelling has a specific usage in a specialized context, e.g., <i>connexion</i> in <a href="/wiki/Connexionalism" title="Connexionalism">Methodist connexionalism</a>.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference selfref">For assistance with specific terms, see <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_American_and_British_English#Vocabulary" title="Comparison of American and British English">Comparison of American and British English &nbsp;Vocabulary</a>, and <a href="/wiki/American_and_British_English_spelling_differences" title="American and British English spelling differences">American and British English spelling differences</a>; most dictionaries also indicate regional terms.</span> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Strong_national_ties_to_a_topic">Strong national ties to a topic</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:TIES"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:TIES&amp;redirect=no">MOS:TIES</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Strong_national_ties_to_a_topic" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers &nbsp;Strong national ties to a topic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>An article on a topic that has strong ties to a particular English-speaking nation should use the (formal, not colloquial) English of that nation. For example: </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style>
      <div class="div-col" style="column-width: 22em;"> 
       <ul>
        <li><a href="/wiki/Afrikaners" title="Afrikaners">Afrikaners</a> (<a href="/wiki/South_African_English" title="South African English">South African English</a>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> (<a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American English</a>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Australian_Defence_Force" title="Australian Defence Force">Australian Defence Force</a> (<a href="/wiki/Australian_English" title="Australian English">Australian English</a>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Christchurch" title="Christchurch">Christchurch</a> (<a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_English" title="New Zealand English">New Zealand English</a>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> (<a href="/wiki/Irish_English" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish English">Irish English</a>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Great_Fire_of_London" title="Great Fire of London">Great Fire of London</a> (<a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Mayon" title="Mayon">Mayon</a> (<a href="/wiki/Philippine_English" title="Philippine English">Philippine English</a>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_Jinnah" title="Muhammad Ali Jinnah">Muhammad Ali Jinnah</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pakistani_English" title="Pakistani English">Pakistani English</a>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a> (<a href="/wiki/Indian_English" title="Indian English">Indian English</a>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a> (<a href="/wiki/Canadian_English" title="Canadian English">Canadian English</a>)</li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>For topics with strong ties to <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> countries and other <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">former British territories</a>, use <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_English" class="mw-redirect" title="Commonwealth English">Commonwealth English</a> orthography, largely indistinguishable from British English in encyclopedic writing (excepting Canada, which uses <a href="/wiki/Canadian_spelling" class="mw-redirect" title="Canadian spelling">a different orthography</a>). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retaining_the_existing_variety">Retaining the existing variety</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:RETAIN"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:RETAIN&amp;redirect=no">MOS:RETAIN</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="#Retaining_existing_styles">&nbsp;Retaining existing styles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Retaining_the_existing_format" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers &nbsp;Retaining the existing format</a>
      </div> 
      <p>When an English variety's <a href="#Consistency_within_articles">consistent usage</a> has been established in an article, maintain it in the absence of consensus to the contrary. With few exceptions (e.g., when a topic has <a href="#Strong_national_ties_to_a_topic">strong national ties</a> or the change reduces ambiguity), there is no valid reason for changing from one acceptable option to another. </p>
      <p><span class="anchor" id="FPSR"></span><span class="anchor" id="FMC"></span>When no English variety has been established and discussion does not resolve the issue, use the variety found in the first post-<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Stub" title="Wikipedia:Stub">stub</a> revision that introduced an identifiable variety. The established variety in a given article can be documented by placing the appropriate <a href="/wiki/Category:Varieties_of_English_templates" title="Category:Varieties of English templates"><i>Varieties of English</i> template</a> on its talk page. </p>
      <p>An article should not be edited or renamed simply to switch from one variety of English to another. The <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Uw-engvar" title="Template:Uw-engvar">uw-engvar</a>}}</code> template may be placed on an editor's talk page to explain this. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Capital_letters">Capital letters</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Capital_letters" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Wikipedia article titles and section headings use sentence case, not title case; see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Article_titles" title="Wikipedia:Article titles">Wikipedia:Article titles</a> and <a href="#Section_headings">&nbsp;Section headings</a>. For capitalization of list items, see <a href="#Bulleted_and_numbered_lists">&nbsp;Bulleted and numbered lists</a>. Other points concerning capitalization are summarized below; full information can be found at <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Capital_letters" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters</a>. The central point is that Wikipedia does not capitalize something unless it is consistently capitalized in a substantial majority of independent, reliable sources. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Capitalization_of_The">Capitalization of <i>The</i></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Capital_letters#Capitalization_of_The" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters &nbsp;Capitalization of The</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Generally, do not capitalize the word <i>the</i> in mid-sentence: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">throughout the United Kingdom</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">throughout The United Kingdom</span>. Conventional exceptions include certain proper names (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">he visited The Hague</span>) and most titles of creative works (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Tolkien wrote <i>The Lord of the Rings</i></span>&nbsp; but be aware that <i>the</i> may not be part of the title itself, e.g., <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Homer composed the <i>Odyssey</i></span>). </p>
      <p>There are special considerations for: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Music#Names_(definite_article)" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Music">band names</a> &nbsp;<a href="/wiki/MOS:THEINST" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:THEINST">institution names</a> &nbsp;<a href="/wiki/MOS:NICKNAMETHE" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:NICKNAMETHE">nicknames</a> &nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Titles#Indefinite_and_definite_articles" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Titles">titles of works</a> &nbsp;<a href="/wiki/MOS:TMTHE" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:TMTHE">trademarks</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles_of_works"><span id="Capitalization-Titles"></span>Titles of works</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For complete guidance on the handling of titles of works, see (until the material is better consolidated): 
       <ul>
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Titles" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Titles">WP:Manual of Style/Titles</a> (overview and details)</li> 
        <li class="mw-empty-elt"></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style#Titles" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style">WP:Manual of Style ?Italics ?Titles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Text_formatting#Names_and_titles" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting">WP:Manual of Style/Text formatting &nbsp;Names and titles</a> (both summarize details at WP:Manual of Style/Titles)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style#Names_and_titles" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style">WP:Manual of Style ?Punctuation ?Quotation marks ?Names and titles</a> (summarizes details at WP:Manual of Style/Titles)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Lists_of_works" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Lists of works">WP:Manual of Style/Lists of works</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Music#Capitalization" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Music">WP:Manual of Style/Music &nbsp;Capitalization</a></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>The English-language titles of compositions (books and other print works, songs and other audio works, films and other visual media works, paintings and other artworks, etc.) are given in <em><a href="/wiki/Title_case" title="Title case">title case</a></em>, in which every word is given an initial capital except for certain less important words (as detailed at <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Capital_letters#Composition_titles" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters &nbsp;Composition titles</a>). The first and last words in an English-language title are always capitalized. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><em>Correct</em>: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>An Eye for an Eye</i></span></li> 
       <li><em>Correct</em>: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Worth the Fighting For</i></span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Capitalization in foreign-language titles varies, even over time within the same language; generally, retain the style of the original for modern works, and follow the usage in current<sup id="cite_ref-recent_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recent-11">[f]</a></sup> English-language reliable sources for historical works. Many of these items should also be in <a href="#Italics">italics</a>, or enclosed in <a href="#Names_and_titles">quotation marks</a>. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><em>Correct</em>: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">"<i lang="de" title="German-language text">Hymnus an den heiligen Geist</i>"</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles_of_people">Titles of people</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Biography#Titles_of_people" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Biography">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Biography &nbsp;Titles of people</a>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li><b>In generic use</b>, apply lower case to words such as <i>president</i>, <i>king</i>, and <i>emperor</i> (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">De Gaulle was a French president</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Louis XVI was a French king</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Three prime ministers attended the conference</span>).</li> 
       <li><b>Directly juxtaposed with the person's name</b>, such words begin with a capital letter (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">President Obama</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">president Obama</span>). Standard or commonly used names of an office are treated as proper names (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">David Cameron was Prime Minister of the United Kingdom</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Hirohito was Emperor of Japan</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Louis XVI was King of France</span>). Royal styles are capitalized (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Her Majesty</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">His Highness</span>); exceptions may apply for particular offices.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span id="Religions.2C_deities.2C_philosophies.2C_doctrines"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Religions,_deities,_philosophies,_doctrines">Religions, deities, philosophies, doctrines</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Capital_letters#Religions,_deities,_philosophies,_doctrines,_and_their_adherents" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters &nbsp;Religions, deities, philosophies, doctrines, and their adherents</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Titles#Religious_Texts" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Titles">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Titles &nbsp;Religious Texts</a>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li><b>Religions, sects, and churches</b> and their followers (in noun or adjective form) start with a capital letter. Generally, "the" is not capitalized before such names (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Sh??a</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">The Sh??a</span>).</li> 
       <li><b><a href="/wiki/Religious_text" title="Religious text">Religious texts</a></b> are capitalized, but often not italicized (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Bhagavad Gita</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Quran</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Talmud</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Granth Sahib</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Bible</span>). Do not capitalize "the" when using it in this way. Some derived adjectives are capitalized by convention, and some are not (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">biblical</span>, but <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Quranic</span>); if unsure, check a dictionary.</li> 
       <li><b><a href="/wiki/Honorific" title="Honorific">Honorifics</a> for deities</b>, including proper names and titles, start with a capital letter (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">God</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Allah</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Lord</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Supreme Being</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Great Spirit</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Horned One</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Bhagavan</span>). Do not capitalize "the" in such cases or when referring to major religious figures or characters from mythology (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Prophet</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Messiah</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Virgin</span>). Common nouns for deities and religious figures are not capitalized (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">many gods</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the god Woden</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">saints and prophets</span>).</li> 
       <li><b>Pronouns for figures of veneration or worship</b> are not capitalized, even if capitalized in a religion's scriptures (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">God and his will</span>).</li> 
       <li><b>Broad categories of mythical or legendary beings</b> start with lower-case letters (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">elf</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">fairy</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">nymph</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">unicorn</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">angel</span>), although in works of fantasy, such as the novels of <a href="/wiki/J._R._R._Tolkien" title="J. R. R. Tolkien">J. R. R. Tolkien</a> and some video games, initial capitals are sometimes used to indicate that the beings form a culture or race in a <a href="/wiki/Fictional_universe" title="Fictional universe">fictional universe</a>. Capitalize the names or titles of individual creatures (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Minotaur</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Pegasus</span>) and of groups whose name and membership are fixed (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Magi, or the Three Wise Men</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Nephilim</span>). Generalized references are not capitalized (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">these priests</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">several wise men</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">cherub-like</span>).</li> 
       <li><b>Spiritual or religious events</b> are capitalized only when referring to specific incidents or periods (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Great Flood</span> and <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Exodus</span>; but <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">annual flooding</span> and <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">an exodus of refugees</span>).</li> 
       <li><b>Philosophies, theories, movements, and doctrines</b> use lower case unless the name derives from a proper name (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">capitalism versus Marxism</span>) or has become a proper name (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">republican</span>, a system of political thought; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Republican</span>, a political party). Use lower case for doctrinal topics or canonical religious ideas (as opposed to specific events), even if they are capitalized by some religious adherents (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">virgin birth</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">original sin</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">transubstantiation</span>).</li> 
       <li><b><a href="/wiki/Platonic_idealism" title="Platonic idealism">Platonic</a> or transcendent ideals</b> are capitalized in the context of philosophical doctrine (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Truth</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Good</span>); used more broadly, they are in lower case (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Superman represents American ideals of truth and justice</span>). Use capitals for personifications represented in art (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the guidebook mentioned statues of Justice and Liberty</span>).</li> 
       <li><span class="anchor" id="Eponyms"></span><span class="anchor" id="EPONYM"></span><span class="anchor" id="EPONYMS"></span> <b><a href="/wiki/Eponym" title="Eponym">Eponyms</a></b> are capitalized (<a href="/wiki/Edwardian_era" title="Edwardian era"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Edwardian</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/De_Morgan%27s_laws" title="De Morgan's laws"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">De Morgan's laws</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland_syndrome" title="Alice in Wonderland syndrome"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Alice in Wonderland syndrome</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Plaster_of_Paris" class="mw-redirect" title="Plaster of Paris"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">plaster of Paris</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Platonic_idealism" title="Platonic idealism"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Platonic idealism</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Draconian_constitution" title="Draconian constitution"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Draconian constitution of Athens</span></a>), except in idiomatic uses disconnected from the original context and usually lower-cased in sources (<a href="/wiki/Platonic_relationship" class="mw-redirect" title="Platonic relationship"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">a platonic relationship</span></a>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">complained of draconian workplace policies</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-eponyms_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eponyms-12">[g]</a></sup> An entire phrase in which an eponym is an adjective <a href="/wiki/MOS:DOCTCAPS" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:DOCTCAPS">is not capitalized</a> except when the phrase is itself a proper name (e.g., the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Titles" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Titles">title of a published work</a>: <a href="/wiki/The_China_Syndrome" title="The China Syndrome"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>The China Syndrome</i></span></a>).</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Calendar_items">Calendar items</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Capital_letters#Calendar_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters &nbsp;Calendar items</a>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li><b>Months, days of the week, and holidays</b> start with a capital letter (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">June</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Monday</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Fourth of July</span> refers only to the US Independence Day&nbsp; otherwise <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">July 4</span> or <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">4 July</span>).</li> 
       <li><b>Seasons</b> are in lower case (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">her last summer</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the winter solstice</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">spring fever</span>), except in personifications or in proper names for periods or events (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Old Man Winter</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">competed on the Spring Circuit</span>).</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span id="Animals.2C_plants.2C_and_other_organisms"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Animals,_plants,_and_other_organisms">Animals, plants, and other organisms</span></h3> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="People,_animals,_plants,_and_other_organisms"></span> </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:LIFE"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:LIFE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:LIFE</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For more detail on capitalization, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Capital_letters#Animals,_plants,_and_other_organisms" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters &nbsp;Animals, plants, and other organisms</a>; on italicization, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Text_formatting#Italic_face" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting &nbsp;Italic face</a>. See also <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Lead_section#Organisms" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Lead section">Wikipedia:Lead section &nbsp;Organisms</a> for handling of first sentence. See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(fauna)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (fauna)">Wikipedia:Naming conventions (fauna)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(flora)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (flora)">Wikipedia:Naming conventions (flora)</a> for article title guidelines.
      </div> 
      <p>When using <b><a href="/wiki/Taxonomy_(biology)" title="Taxonomy (biology)">taxonomic ("scientific") names</a></b>, capitalize and italicize the genus: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Berberis</i></span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Erithacus</i></span>. (Supergenus and subgenus, when applicable, are treated the same way.) Italicize but do not capitalize taxonomic ranks at the level of species and below: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Berberis darwinii</i></span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Erithacus rubecula superbus</i></span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Acacia coriacea</i> subsp. <i>sericophylla</i></span>; no exception is made for proper names forming part of scientific names. Higher taxa (order, family, etc.) are capitalized in Latin (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Carnivora</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Felidae</span>) but not in their English equivalents (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">carnivorans</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">felids</span>); they are not italicized in either form, except for viruses, where all names accepted by the <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_on_Taxonomy_of_Viruses" title="International Committee on Taxonomy of Viruses">ICTV</a> are italicized (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Retroviridae</i></span>). </p>
      <p><b><a href="/wiki/Cultivar" title="Cultivar">Cultivar</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Cultivar_group" title="Cultivar group">cultivar group</a></b> names of plants are not italicized, and are capitalized (including the word <i>Group</i> in the name); cultivar names appear within single quotes (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Malus domestica</i> 'Red Delicious'</span>), while cultivar groups do not (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Cynara cardunculus</i> Scolymus Group</span>). </p>
