      <p><b>English <a href="/wiki/Common_name" title="Common name">vernacular ("common") names</a></b> are given in lower case in article prose (<a href="/wiki/Plains_zebra" title="Plains zebra"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">plains zebra</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountain_maple" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountain maple"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">mountain&nbsp;maple</span></a>, and <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_red-tailed_hawk" title="Southwestern red-tailed hawk"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">southwestern red-tailed hawk</span></a>) and in sentence case at the start of sentences and in other places where the first letter of the first word is capitalized.<sup id="cite_ref-Sentence_case_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sentence_case-5">[a]</a></sup> They are additionally capitalized where they contain proper names: <a href="/wiki/Przewalski%27s_horse" title="Przewalski's horse"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Przewalski's&nbsp;horse</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/California_condor" title="California condor"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">California&nbsp;condor</span></a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fair-maid-of-France" class="mw-redirect" title="Fair-maid-of-France"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">fair-maid-of-France</span></a>. This applies to species and subspecies, as in the previous examples, as well as to general names for groups or types of organism: <a href="/wiki/Bird_of_prey" title="Bird of prey"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">bird&nbsp;of&nbsp;prey</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">oak</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_apes" class="mw-redirect" title="Great apes"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">great&nbsp;apes</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Bryde%27s_whales" class="mw-redirect" title="Bryde's whales"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Bryde's&nbsp;whales</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Livestock_guardian_dog" title="Livestock guardian dog"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">livestock&nbsp;guardian&nbsp;dog</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Poodle" title="Poodle"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">poodle</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Van_cat" title="Van cat"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Van&nbsp;cat</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolfdog" title="Wolfdog"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">wolfdog</span></a>. When the common name coincides with a scientific taxon, do not capitalize or italicize, except where addressing the organism taxonomically: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">A lynx is any of the four medium-sized wild cat species within the genus <i>Lynx</i>.</span> Non-English vernacular names, when relevant to include, are handled like any other foreign-language terms: italicized as such, and capitalized only if the rules of the native language require it. Non-English names that have become English-assimilated are treated as English (<a href="/wiki/Ayahuasca" title="Ayahuasca"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">ayahuasca</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Okapi" title="Okapi"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">okapi</span></a>). </p>
      <p><b><a href="/wiki/Breed_standard" title="Breed standard">Standardized breeds</a></b> should generally retain the capitalization used in the breed standards.<sup id="cite_ref-Standardized_breeds_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Standardized_breeds-13">[h]</a></sup> Examples: <a href="/wiki/German_Shepherd_dog" class="mw-redirect" title="German Shepherd dog"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">German Shepherd dog</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_White_goat" title="Russian White goat"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Russian White goat</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Short-faced_Tumbler" title="Berlin Short-faced Tumbler"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Berlin Short-faced Tumbler</span></a>. As with plant cultivars, this applies whether or not the included noun is a proper name, in contrast to how vernacular names of species are written. However, unlike cultivars, breeds are never put in single quotation marks, and their names are never part of a scientific name. A species term appended at the end for disambiguation ("cat", "hound", "horse", "swine", etc.) should not be capitalized, unless it is a part of the breed name itself and is consistently presented that way in the breed standard(s) (rare cases include <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Forest_Cat" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwegian Forest Cat"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Norwegian Forest Cat</span></a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Quarter_Horse" title="American Quarter Horse"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">American Quarter Horse</span></a>). </p>
      <p>Create <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Redirect" title="Wikipedia:Redirect">redirects</a> from alternative capitalization and spelling forms of article titles, and from alternative names, e.g., <a href="/wiki/Ad%C3%A9lie_Penguin" class="mw-redirect" title="Adlie Penguin">Adlie Penguin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adelie_penguin" class="mw-redirect" title="Adelie penguin">Adelie penguin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adelie_Penguin" class="mw-redirect" title="Adelie Penguin">Adelie Penguin</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Pygoscelis_adeliae" class="mw-redirect" title="Pygoscelis adeliae">Pygoscelis adeliae</a></i> should all redirect to <a href="/wiki/Ad%C3%A9lie_penguin" title="Adlie penguin">Adlie penguin</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Celestial_bodies">Celestial bodies</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Capital_letters#Celestial_bodies" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters &nbsp;Celestial bodies</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(astronomical_objects)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (astronomical objects)">Wikipedia:Naming conventions (astronomical objects)</a>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>The words <i>sun</i>, <i>earth</i>, <i>moon</i> and <i>solar system</i> do not take capitals in general use (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The sun was over the mountain top</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The tribal people thought of the whole earth as their home</span>). They are capitalized when the entity is personified (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Sol Invictus ('Unconquered Sun') was the Roman sun god</span>) or when used as the name of a specific body in a scientific or astronomical context (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The Moon orbits the Earth</span>; but <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Io is a moon of Jupiter</span>).</li> 
       <li>Names of planets, moons, asteroids, comets, stars, constellations, and galaxies are proper names, and therefore capitalized (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The planet Mars is in the constellation Gemini, near the star Pollux</span>). The first letter of every word in such a name is capitalized (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Alpha Centauri</span> and not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Alpha centauri</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Milky Way</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Milky way</span>). Words such as <i>comet</i> and <i>galaxy</i> should be capitalized when they form part of a proper name, but not when they are used as a generic term (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Halley's Comet is the most famous of the comets</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The Andromeda Galaxy is a spiral galaxy</span>).</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Compass_points">Compass points</span></h3> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Compass"></span> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Capital_letters#Compass_points" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters &nbsp;Compass points</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Do not capitalize <b>directions</b> such as <i>north</i>, or their related forms (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">We took the northern road</span>), except where they are parts of proper names (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Great North Road</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Great Western Drive</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">South Pole</span>). </p>
      <p>Capitalize <b>names of regions</b> if they have attained proper-name status, including informal conventional names (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Southern California</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Western Desert</span>), and derived terms for people (e.g., a <i>Southerner</i> as someone from the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">Southern United States</a>). Do not capitalize descriptive names for regions that have not attained the status of proper names, such as <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">southern Poland</span>. </p>
      <p>Composite directions may or may not be hyphenated, depending on the <a href="#National_varieties_of_English">variety of English adopted</a> in the article. <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Southeast Asia</span> and <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">northwest</span> are more common in American English; but <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">South-East Asia</span> and <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">north-west</span> in British English. In cases such as <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">northsouth dialogue</span> and <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">eastwest orientation</span>, use an en dash; see <a href="#En_dashes:_other_uses">&nbsp;En dashes: other uses</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Proper_names_versus_generic_terms"><span id="Institutions"></span> Proper names versus generic terms</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main pages: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Capital_letters#Institutions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters &nbsp;Institutions</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Capital_letters#Capitalization_of_''The''" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters &nbsp;Capitalization of <i>The</i></a>
      </div> 
      <p>Capitalize names of particular institutions (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the founding of the University of Delhi</span>;<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span> <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the history of Stanford University</span>) but not generic words for institutions (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the high school is near the university</span>). Do not capitalize <i>the</i> at the start of an institution's name, regardless of the institution's preferred style. There are rare exceptions, when a leading <i>The</i> is represented by a <i>T</i> in the organization's acronym: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The International Cat Association (TICA)</span>. </p>
      <p>Treat political or geographic units similarly: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The city has a population of 55,000</span>;<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span> <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The two towns merged to become the City of Smithville</span>. Do not mimic the style of local newspapers which refer to their municipality as <i>the City</i> or <i>The City</i>; an exception is the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">City of London</a>, referred to as <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the City</span> in a context that already makes the subject clear, as distinct from <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greater_London" title="Greater London">Greater London</a>. When in doubt, use the full name for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Accessibility" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility">accessibility</a> reasons; users of screen readers for the blind cannot hear a difference between <i>city</i> and <i>City</i>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ligatures">Ligatures</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(use_English)#Modified_letters" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (use English)">Wikipedia:Naming conventions (use English) &nbsp;Modified letters</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:LIGATURE"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:LIGATURE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:LIGATURE</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Typographic_ligature" class="mw-redirect" title="Typographic ligature">Ligatures</a> should be used in languages in which they are standard (hence <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Moreau's last words were <i>clin d'il</i></span> is preferable to <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Moreau's last words were <i>clin d'oeil</i></span>) but not in English (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">encyclopedia</span> or <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">encyclopaedia</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">encyclopdia</span>), except in proper names (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">thelstan</span> not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Aethelstan</span>). </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Abbreviations">Abbreviations</span></h2> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Acronyms_and_abbreviations"></span><span class="anchor" id="Acronyms"></span><span class="anchor" id="Initialisms"></span><span class="anchor" id="Shortenings"></span> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Abbreviations" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Abbreviations">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Abbreviations</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Biography#Initials" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Biography">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Biography &nbsp;Initials</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Abbreviations are shortened forms of words or phrases. In strict analysis, they are distinct from <a href="/wiki/Contraction_(grammar)" title="Contraction (grammar)">contractions</a>, which use an <a href="/wiki/Apostrophe" title="Apostrophe">apostrophe</a> (e.g., <i>won't</i>, see <a href="#Contractions">&nbsp;Contractions</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Initialism" class="mw-redirect" title="Initialism">initialisms</a>. An initialism is formed from some or all of the initial letters of words in a phrase. Below, references to abbreviations should be taken to include acronyms, and the term <i>acronym</i> to apply also to initialisms. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Write_out_both_the_full_version_and_the_abbreviation_at_first_occurrence">Write out both the full version and the abbreviation at first occurrence</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:1STOCC"></span><span id="MOS:1STABBR"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:1STOCC&amp;redirect=no">MOS:1STOCC</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:1STABBR&amp;redirect=no">MOS:1STABBR</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>When an abbreviation will be used in an article, first introduce it using the full expression: </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996643573">
      <div class="block-indent">
       <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">an early local area network (LAN) developed by Digital Equipment Corporation (DEC)<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>... DEC's later LAN products were<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>...</span>
      </div> 
      <p>Do not use capitals in the full version merely because capitals are used in the abbreviation: <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">an early Local Area Network (LAN)</span>. </p>
      <p>Except in special circumstances, common abbreviations (such as <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">PhD</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">DNA</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">USSR</span>) need not be expanded even on first use. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plural_forms">Plural forms</span></h3> 
      <p>Pluralize <a href="/wiki/Acronyms" class="mw-redirect" title="Acronyms">acronyms</a> by adding <i>-s</i> or <i>-es</i>: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Three CD-ROMs and two BIOSes were released</span>. (Do not use apostrophes to form plurals: <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Three CD-ROM's and two BIOS's were released</span>.) </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Punctuation_and_spacing">Punctuation and spacing</span></h3> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Periods_(full_stops)_and_spaces"></span><span class="anchor" id="Full_stops_and_spaces"></span><span class="anchor" id="op.cit."></span> </p>
      <p>An abbreviation may or may not be terminated with a full point (also called a <i>period</i> or <i>stop</i>). A consistent style should be maintained within an article. North American usage is typically to end all abbreviations with a period/point (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Dr. Smith of 42&nbsp;Drummond St.</span>) but in common British and Australian usage, no period/point is used if the abbreviation (contraction) ends in the last letter of the unabbreviated form (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Dr Smith of 42&nbsp;Drummond St</span>) unless confusion could result. This is also common practice in scientific writing. Regardless of punctuation, words that are abbreviated to more than one letter are spaced (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">op.&nbsp;cit.</span> not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">op.cit.</span> or <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">opcit</span>). There are some exceptions: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">PhD</span> 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see above)</span> for "Philosophiae Doctor"; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">BVetMed</span> for "Bachelor of Veterinary Medicine". In most situations, Wikipedia <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Abbreviations#Full_points_(periods)" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Abbreviations">uses no such punctuation inside acronyms and initialisms</a>: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">GDP</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">G.D.P.</span> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="US_and_U.S.">US and U.S.</span></h3> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="US"></span><span class="anchor" id="U.S."></span><span class="anchor" id="USA"></span><span class="anchor" id="U.S.A."></span> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "MOS:US" redirects here. For the use of the word "us", see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style#First-person_pronouns" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style">Wikipedia:Manual of Style &nbsp;First-person pronouns</a>.
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:US"></span><span id="MOS:USA"></span><span id="MOS:NOTUSA"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:US&amp;redirect=no">MOS:US</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:USA&amp;redirect=no">MOS:USA</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:NOTUSA&amp;redirect=no">MOS:NOTUSA</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>While, in principle, either <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">US</span> or <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">U.S.</span> may be used (with internal consistency) to abbreviate "United States" in any given article, the use or non-use of periods (full stops) should also be consistent with other country abbreviations in the same article (thus <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the US, UK, and USSR</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">the U.S., UK, and USSR</span>). In longer abbreviations (three letters or more) that incorporate the country's initials (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">USN</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">USAID</span>), do not use periods. When the United States is mentioned with one or more other countries in the same sentence, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">U.S.</span> or <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">US</span> may be too informal, especially at the first mention or as a noun instead of an adjective (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">France and the United States</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">France and the US</span>). Do not use the spaced <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">U.&nbsp;S.</span> or the archaic <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">U.S.&nbsp;of&nbsp;A.</span>, except when quoting; and do not use <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">U.S.A.</span> or <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">USA</span> except in a quotation, as part of a proper name (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Team USA</span>), or in certain technical or formal uses (e.g., the <a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-1_alpha-3" title="ISO 3166-1 alpha-3">ISO 3166-1 alpha-3</a> codes and <a href="/wiki/FIFA_country_codes" class="mw-redirect" title="FIFA country codes">FIFA country codes</a>). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Circa">Circa</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Uncertain,_incomplete,_or_approximate_dates" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers &nbsp;Uncertain, incomplete, or approximate dates</a> for examples.
      </div> 
      <p>To indicate <i>approximately</i>, the abbreviation <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">c.</span> (followed by a space and not italicized) is preferred over <i>circa</i>, <i>ca.</i>, or <i>approx.</i> The template <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Circa" title="Template:Circa">circa</a>}}</code> may be used. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Do_not_use_unwarranted_abbreviations">Do not use unwarranted abbreviations</span></h3> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="unwarranted_abbreviations"></span> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Units_of_measurement" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers &nbsp;Units of measurement</a> for when to abbreviate units of measurement.
      </div> 
      <p>Avoid abbreviations when they might confuse the reader, interrupt the flow, or appear informal. For example: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Do not use <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">approx.</span> for <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">approximate(ly)</span> except in an infobox or table (in which case use <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Abbr" title="Template:Abbr">abbr</a>|approx.|approximately}}</code> at first occurrence: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><abbr title="approximately">approx.</abbr></span>).</li> 
       <li>Do not use the legalism <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Smith J</span> for <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Justice Smith</span>.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Do_not_invent_abbreviations_or_acronyms">Do not invent abbreviations or acronyms</span></h3> 
      <p>Generally avoid devising <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Wikipedia_is_not_a_dictionary#Neologisms" title="Wikipedia:Wikipedia is not a dictionary">new abbreviations</a>, especially acronyms. For example, <span class="example example-neutral" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: initial;">World Union of Billiards</span> is good as a <em>translation</em> of <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><a href="/wiki/Union_Mondiale_de_Billard" title="Union Mondiale de Billard">Union Mondiale de Billard</a></span>, but neither it nor the reduction <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">WUB</span> is used by the organization or by independent sources; use the original name and its official abbreviation, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">UMB</span>. </p>
      <p>If it is necessary to abbreviate in a tight space, such as a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Tables#Captions_and_headers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Tables">column header in a table</a>, use widely recognized abbreviations. For example, for <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">New Zealand gross national product</span>, use <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">NZ</span> and <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">GNP</span>, with a link if the term has not already been written out in the article: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">NZ&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Measures_of_national_income_and_output" title="Measures of national income and output">GNP</a></span>. Do not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Wikipedia_is_not_for_things_made_up_one_day" title="Wikipedia:Wikipedia is not for things made up one day">make up</a> initialisms such as <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">NZGNP</span>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="HTML_tags_and_templates_for_abbreviations">HTML tags and templates for abbreviations</span></h3> 
      <p>Either the <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;abbr&gt;</code> element or the <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Abbr" title="Template:Abbr">abbr</a>}}</code> template can be used for abbreviations and acronyms: <code class="wrap" style="">&lt;abbr title="World Health Organization"&gt;WHO&lt;/abbr&gt;</code> or <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Abbr" title="Template:Abbr">abbr</a>|WHO|World Health Organization}}</code> will generate <abbr title="World Health Organization">WHO</abbr>; <a href="/wiki/Mouseover" title="Mouseover">hovering</a> over the rendered text causes a <a href="/wiki/Tooltip" title="Tooltip">tooltip</a> of the long form to pop up. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ampersand">Ampersand</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:AMP"></span><span id="MOS:&amp;amp;"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:AMP&amp;redirect=no">MOS:AMP</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:%26&amp;redirect=no">MOS:&amp;</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>In normal text and headings, use <i>and</i> instead of the <a href="/wiki/Ampersand" title="Ampersand">ampersand</a> (<i>&amp;</i>): <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">January 1&nbsp;and&nbsp;2</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">January 1&nbsp;&amp;&nbsp;2</span>. But retain an ampersand when it is a legitimate part of the style of a proper noun, such as in <i><a href="/wiki/Up_%26_Down_(album)" title="Up &amp; Down (album)">Up&nbsp;&amp;&nbsp;Down</a></i> or <a href="/wiki/AT%26T" title="AT&amp;T">AT&amp;T</a>. Elsewhere, ampersands may be used with consistency and discretion where space is extremely limited (e.g., tables and infoboxes). Quotations <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style#Typographic_conformity" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style">may be cautiously modified</a>, especially for consistency where different editions are quoted, as modern editions of old texts routinely replace ampersands with <i>and</i> (just as they replace other disused <a href="/wiki/Glyph" title="Glyph">glyphs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Typographic_ligature" class="mw-redirect" title="Typographic ligature">ligatures</a>, and abbreviations). Another frequent permissible but not required use is in short bibliographic references to works by multiple authors, e.g.: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">&nbsp;...a series of French and Belgian papers (Lubbers &amp; Scheepers, 2002; Van Hiel &amp; Mervielde, 2002; Swyngedouw &amp; Giles, 2007; Van Hiel, 2012)</span>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Italics">Italics</span></h2> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:IT"></span><span id="MOS:ITAL"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:IT&amp;redirect=no">MOS:IT</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:ITAL&amp;redirect=no">MOS:ITAL</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Text_formatting#Italic_type" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting &nbsp;Italic type</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emphasis">Emphasis<span id="Do_not_use_capitals_for_emphasis"></span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Text_formatting#Emphasis" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting &nbsp;Emphasis</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Italics are used for emphasis, rather than <a href="/wiki/MOS:BOLD" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:BOLD">boldface</a> or <a href="/wiki/MOS:ALLCAPS" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:ALLCAPS">capitals</a>. But overuse diminishes its effect; consider rewriting instead. </p>
      <p>Use <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;em&gt;...&lt;/em&gt;</code> or <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Em" title="Template:Em">em</a>|...}}</code> for emphasis. This allows <a href="/wiki/Help:User_style" title="Help:User style">user style sheets</a> to handle emphasis in a customized way, and helps reusers and translators.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[6]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Correct: <code><span class="example monospaced example-mono" style="font-family: monospace, monospace; color: #006400;">The meerkat is &lt;em&gt;not&lt;/em&gt; actually a cat.</span></code></li> 
       <li>Correct: <code><span class="example monospaced example-mono" style="font-family: monospace, monospace; color: #006400;">The meerkat is {{em|not}} actually a cat.</span></code></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles"><span id="Italics-Titles"></span>Titles</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For complete guidance on the handling of titles of works, see (until the material is better consolidated): 
       <ul>
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Titles" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Titles">WP:Manual of Style/Titles</a> (overview and details)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style#Titles_of_works" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style">WP:Manual of Style &nbsp;Titles of works</a> (which summarizes the key points)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Text_formatting#Names_and_titles" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting">WP:Manual of Style/Text formatting &nbsp;Names and titles</a> (provides greater detail than the section are you are reading now)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style#Names_and_titles" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style">WP:Manual of Style ?Punctuation ?Quotation marks ?Names and titles</a> (summarizes details at WP:Manual of Style/Titles)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Lists_of_works" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Lists of works">WP:Manual of Style/Lists of works</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Music#Capitalization" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Music">WP:Manual of Style/Music &nbsp;Capitalization</a></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>Use italics for the titles of works (such as books, films, television series, named exhibitions, computer games, music albums, and paintings). The titles of articles, chapters, songs, episodes, research papers and other short works instead take double quotation marks. Italics are not used for major religious works (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Bible</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Quran</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Talmud</span>). Many of these titles should also be in <a href="#Titles_of_works">title case</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Words_as_words">Words as words</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Text_formatting#Words_as_words" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting &nbsp;Words as words</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Use italics when <em>mentioning</em> a word or character 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="/wiki/Use%E2%80%93mention_distinction" title="Usemention distinction">Usemention distinction</a>)</span> or a string of words up to one sentence (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the term <i>panning</i> is derived from <i>panorama</i></span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the most common letter in English is <i>e</i></span>). When a whole sentence is mentioned, double quotation marks may be used instead, with consistency (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The preposition in <i>She sat on the chair</i> is <i>on</i></span>; or <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The preposition in "She sat on the chair" is "on"</span>). Quotation marks may also be used for shorter material to avoid confusion, such as when italics are already being heavily used in the page for some other purpose (e.g., many non-English words and phrases). <em>Mentioning</em> (to discuss grammar, wording, punctuation, etc.) is different from <em>quoting</em> (in which something is usually expressed on behalf of a quoted source). Quotation is done with quotation marks, never italics, nor both at once 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="#Quotations">&nbsp;Quotations</a> for details).</span> </p>
      <p>A closely related use of italics is when introducing or distinguishing terms: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The <i>natural numbers</i> are the integers greater than 0.</span> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_words">Foreign words</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Text_formatting#Foreign_terms" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting &nbsp;Foreign terms</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Use italics for phrases in other languages and for isolated foreign words that are not common in everyday English. However, proper names (such as place names) in other languages are not usually italicized, nor are terms in non-Latin scripts. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_names">Scientific names</span></h3> 
      <p>Use italics for the scientific names of plants, animals, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_(biology)" title="Kingdom (biology)">all other organisms</a> except viruses at the <a href="/wiki/Genus" title="Genus">genus</a> level and below (italicize <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Panthera leo</i></span> and <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Retroviridae</i></span>, but not <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Felidae</span>). The hybrid sign is not italicized (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Rosa</i>&nbsp;&nbsp;<i>damascena</i></span>), nor is the "connecting term" required in <a href="/wiki/Trinomial_nomenclature#In_botany" title="Trinomial nomenclature">three-part botanical names</a> (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Rosa gallica</i> subsp. <i>officinalis</i></span>). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Quotations_in_italics"><span id="Italics_and_quotations"></span>Quotations in italics</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:ITALQUOTE"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:ITALQUOTE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:ITALQUOTE</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div>
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="#Quotations">&nbsp;Quotations</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Do not use italics for quotations. Instead, use quotation marks for short quotations and <a href="#Block_quotations">block quoting</a> for long ones. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Italics_within_quotations">Italics within quotations</span></h3> 
      <p>Use italics within quotations to reproduce emphasis that exists in the source material. If it is not clear that the source already included italics (or some other styling) for emphasis, add the editorial note <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">[emphasis in original]</span> after the quotation. </p>
      <p>If adding emphasis that was not in the original, add the editorial note <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">[emphasis added]</span> after the quotation. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">"Now cracks a noble heart. Good night sweet prince: And <em>flights of angels</em> sing thee to thy rest." [emphasis added]</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Effect_on_nearby_punctuation">Effect on nearby punctuation</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:ITALPUNCT"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:ITALPUNCT&amp;redirect=no">MOS:ITALPUNCT</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>Italicize only the elements of the sentence affected by the emphasis. Do not italicize surrounding punctuation. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>
        <div style="text-indent: -1.6em; margin-left: 1.6em;">
         <em>Incorrect</em>: <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">What are we to make of <em>that?</em></span> (The question mark applies to the whole sentence, not just to the emphasized <i>that</i>, so it should not be italicized.)
        </div></li> 
       <li>
        <div style="text-indent: -1.6em; margin-left: 1.6em;">
         <em>Correct</em>: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">What are we to make of <em>that</em>?</span>
        </div></li> 
       <li>
        <div style="text-indent: -1.6em; margin-left: 1.6em;">
         <em>Correct</em>: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Four of Patrick White's most famous novels are <i>A Fringe of Leaves</i>, <i>The Aunt's Story</i>, <i>Voss</i>, and <i>The Tree of Man</i>.</span> (The commas, the period, and the word <i>and</i> are not italicized.)
        </div></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Quotations">Quotations</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Do_not_include_the_full_text_of_lengthy_primary_sources" title="Wikipedia:Do not include the full text of lengthy primary sources">Wikipedia:Do not include the full text of lengthy primary sources</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:QUOTE"></span><span id="MOS:QUOTATIONS"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:QUOTE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:QUOTE</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:QUOTATIONS&amp;redirect=no">MOS:QUOTATIONS</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="#Italics_and_quotations">&nbsp;Italics and quotations</a>, <a href="#Quotation_marks">&nbsp;Quotation marks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Quotations" title="Wikipedia:Quotations">Wikipedia:Quotations</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NFCCEG" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NFCCEG">Brief quotations of copyrighted text</a> may be used to illustrate a point, establish context, or attribute a point of view or idea. While quotations are an indispensable part of Wikipedia, try not to overuse them. Using too many quotes is incompatible with an encyclopedic writing style and may be a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Copyrights" title="Wikipedia:Copyrights">copyright infringement</a>. It is generally recommended that content be written in Wikipedia editors' own words. Consider paraphrasing quotations into plain and concise text when appropriate (while being aware that <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Close_paraphrasing" title="Wikipedia:Close paraphrasing">close paraphrasing</a> can still violate copyright). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Original_wording">Original wording</span></h3> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Principle_of_minimal_change"></span><span class="anchor" id="Minimal_change"></span><span class="anchor" id="PMC"></span><span class="anchor" id="PLC"></span><span class="anchor" id="MINIMALCHANGE"></span><span class="anchor" id="MINCHANGE"></span><span class="anchor" id="LEASTCHANGE"></span> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "WP:PLC" redirects here. For inclusion guidelines for organizations, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Notability_(organizations_and_companies)" title="Wikipedia:Notability (organizations and companies)">Wikipedia:Notability (organizations and companies)</a>. For the handling of the abbreviation "plc" in article titles, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(companies)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (companies)">Wikipedia:Naming conventions (companies)</a>.
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:PMC"></span><span id="MOS:SIC"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:PMC&amp;redirect=no">MOS:PMC</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:SIC&amp;redirect=no">MOS:SIC</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>Quotations must be <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verifiably</a> attributed, and the wording of the quoted text should be faithfully reproduced. This is referred to as the <strong>principle of minimal change</strong>. Where there is good reason to change the wording, bracket the changed text; for example, <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">"Ocyrhoe told him his fate"</span> might be quoted as <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">"Ocyrhoe told [her father] his fate"</span>. If there is a significant error in the original, follow it with the template <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Sic" title="Template:Sic">sic</a>}}</code> (producing <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"> [<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>]</span>?) to show that the error was not made by Wikipedia. However, insignificant spelling and typographic errors should simply be silently corrected (for example, correct <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">basicly</span> to <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">basically</span>). </p>
      <p>Use <a href="#Ellipses">ellipses</a> to indicate omissions from quoted text. Legitimate omissions include extraneous, irrelevant, or parenthetical words, and unintelligible speech (<span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">umm</span> and <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">hmm</span>). Do not omit text where doing so would remove important context or alter the meaning of the text. When a vulgarity or obscenity is quoted, it should appear exactly as it does in the cited source; Wikipedians should <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Offensive_material#How_to_treat_offensive_material_in_articles" title="Wikipedia:Offensive material">never bowdlerize words</a> by replacing letters with dashes, asterisks, or other symbols, except when faithfully reproducing quoted text that did so. In carrying over such an alteration from a quoted source, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>]</span> or the <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Sic" title="Template:Sic">sic</a>}}</code> template may be used to indicate that the transcription is exact. </p>
      <p>In direct quotations, retain dialectal and archaic spellings, including capitalization (but not archaic glyphs and ligatures, as detailed below). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Point_of_view">Point of view</span></h3> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Quotation_point_of_view"></span> </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:QUOTEPOV"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:QUOTEPOV&amp;redirect=no">MOS:QUOTEPOV</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view#Attributing_and_specifying_biased_statements" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">Wikipedia:Neutral point of view &nbsp;Attributing and specifying biased statements</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Expressions_of_doubt" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch &nbsp;Expressions of doubt</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Quotation should be used, with attribution, to present emotive opinions that cannot be expressed in Wikipedia's own voice, but never to present cultural norms as simply opinional: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Acceptable: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Siskel and Ebert called the film "unforgettable".</span></li> 
       <li>Unacceptable: <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">The site is considered "sacred" by the religion's scriptures.</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Concise opinions that are not overly emotive can often be reported with attribution instead of direct quotation. Use of quotation marks around simple descriptive terms can <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Expressions_of_doubt" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">imply something doubtful</a> regarding the material being quoted; sarcasm or <a href="/wiki/Weasel_words" class="mw-redirect" title="Weasel words">weasel words</a> such as <i>supposedly</i> or <i>so-called</i>, might be inferred. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Permissible: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Siskel and Ebert called the film interesting.</span></li> 
       <li>Unnecessary and may imply doubt: <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Siskel and Ebert called the film "interesting".</span></li> 
       <li>Should be quoted: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Siskel and Ebert called the film "interesting but heart-wrenching".</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typographic_conformity">Typographic conformity</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:CONFORM"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:CONFORM&amp;redirect=no">MOS:CONFORM</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>A quotation is not a <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/facsimile" class="extiw" title="wikt:facsimile">facsimile</a> and, in most cases, it is not a requirement that the original formatting be preserved. Formatting and other purely typographical elements of quoted text<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[i]</a></sup> should be adapted to English Wikipedia's conventions without comment provided that doing so will not change or obscure meaning or intent of the text. These are alterations which make no difference when the text is read aloud, for example: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Normalize dashes and hyphens: see <a href="#Dashes">&nbsp;Dashes</a>. Use the style chosen for the article: unspaced <a href="/wiki/Em_dash" class="mw-redirect" title="Em dash">em dash</a> or spaced <a href="/wiki/En_dash" class="mw-redirect" title="En dash">en dash</a>.</li> 
       <li>Convert apostrophes and quotation marks to Wikipedia's style: 
        <ul>
         <li>These should be straight, not curly or slanted. See <a href="#Quotation_marks">&nbsp;Quotation marks</a>.</li> 
         <li>When quoting a quotation that itself contains a quotation, alternate between using double and single quotes for each quotation. See <a href="#For_a_quotation_within_a_quotation">&nbsp;For a quotation within a quotation</a> for details.</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li>When quoting text from non-English languages, the outer punctuation should follow <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style#Quotation_marks" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style">the Manual of Style for English quote marks</a>. If there are nested quotations, follow the rules for correct punctuation in that language. If there are multiple styles for a language, the one used by the Wikipedia for that language is preferred unless the punctuation itself is under discussion. 
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The cynical response "L'auteur aurait d demander: &nbsp; quoi sert-il d'crire ceci?&nbsp; mais ne l'a pas fait" was all he wrote.</span>
         </dd>
        </dl></li> 
       <li>Remove spaces before punctuation such as periods and colons.</li> 
       <li>Generally preserve bold and italics 
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="#Italics">&nbsp;Italics</a>)</span>, but most other styling should be altered. <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;"><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Underlining</span></span>, <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">spac&nbsp;ing</span> within words, <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">co<span style="color:Goldenrod;">lor</span>s</span>, <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">ALL CAPS</span>, <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r920966791">.mw-parser-output span.smallcaps{font-variant:small-caps}.mw-parser-output span.smallcaps-smaller{font-size:85%}</style><span class="smallcaps"><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">small caps</span></span>, etc. should generally be normalized to plain text. If it <em>clearly</em> indicates emphasis, use italic <em>emphasis</em> (<code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Em" title="Template:Em">em</a>}}</code>) or, in an already-italic passage, boldface (with <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Strong" title="Template:Strong">strong</a>}}</code>). For titles of books, articles, poems, and so forth, use italics or quotation marks following <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Titles" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Titles">the guidance for titles</a>. Italics can also be added to mark up <a href="#Foreign_terms">non-English terms</a> (with the <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Lang" title="Template:Lang">lang</a>}}</code> template), for an <a href="#Animals,_plants,_and_other_organisms">organism's scientific name</a>, and to indicate a <a href="#Words_as_words">words-as-words</a> usage.</li> 
       <li>Expand an abbreviation (not already used in the content before the quotation) as a square-bracketed change, or explain it with the <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Abbr" title="Template:Abbr">abbr</a>}}</code> template.</li> 
       <li>Normalize archaic glyphs and ligatures in English that are unnecessary to the meaning. Examples include <i><a href="/wiki/%C3%86" title=""></a></i>?<i>ae</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/%C5%92" title=""></a></i>?<i>oe</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Long_s" title="Long s">?</a></i>?<i>s</i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Thorn_(letter)#Abbreviations" title="Thorn (letter)"><sup>e</sup></a></i>?<i>the</i>. 
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(See also <a href="#Ampersand">&nbsp;Ampersand</a>.)</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Titles#Typographic_conformity" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Titles">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Titles &nbsp;Typographic conformity</a> for special considerations in normalizing the typography of titles of works.</span> </p>
      <p>However, national varieties should not be changed, as these may involve changes in vocabulary. For example, a quotation from a British source should retain British spelling, even in an article that otherwise uses American spelling. 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(See <a href="#Consistency_within_articles">&nbsp;Consistency within articles</a>.)</span> Numbers also usually <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Quotations,_titles,_etc." title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">should not be reformatted</a>. </p>
      <p>Direct quotation should not be used to preserve the formatting preferred by an external publisher (especially when the material would otherwise be unchanged), as this tends to have the effect of "<a href="/wiki/Scare_quotes" title="Scare quotes">scare-quoting</a>": </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><em>Acceptable</em>: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The animal is listed as endangered on the IUCN Red List of Threatened Species.</span></li> 
       <li><em>Unacceptable</em>: <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">The animal is listed as "Endangered" on the IUCN Red List of Threatened Species.</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Italics can be used to mark a particular usage as a <a href="/wiki/Term_of_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Term of art">term of art</a> (a case of "<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Text_formatting#Words_as_words" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting">words as words</a>"), especially when it is unfamiliar or should not be reworded by a non-expert: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><em>Permissible</em>: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The animal is listed as <i>critically endangered</i> on the IUCN Red List of Threatened Species.</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>When quoting a complete sentence, it is usually recommended to keep the first word capitalized. However, if the quoted passage has been integrated into the surrounding sentence (for example, with an introduction such as "<var style="padding-right: 1px;">X</var> said that"), the original capital letter may be lower-cased. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">LaVesque's report stated: "The equipment was selected for its low price. This is the primary reason for criticism of the program."</span></li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">LaVesque's report said that "the equipment was selected for its low price".</span></li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The program was criticized primarily because "the equipment was selected for its low price", according to LaVesque.</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>It is not normally necessary to explicitly note changes in capitalization. However, for more precision, the altered letter may be put inside square brackets: "The" ? "[t]he". </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The program was criticized primarily because "[t]he equipment was selected for its low price", according to LaVesque.</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Attribution">Attribution</span></h3> 
      <p>The reader must be able to determine the source of any quotation, at the very least via a footnote. The source must be named <em>in article text</em> if the quotation is an opinion 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view#Attributing_and_specifying_biased_statements" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">Wikipedia:Neutral point of view &nbsp;Attributing and specifying biased statements</a>)</span>. When attributing a quotation, avoid <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Words_to_avoid#Synonyms_for_said" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Words to avoid">characterizing it in a biased manner</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Quotations_within_quotations">Quotations within quotations</span></h3> 
      <p>See <a href="#For_a_quotation_within_a_quotation">&nbsp;For a quotation within a quotation</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Linking">Linking</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:LINKQUOTE"></span><span id="MOS:LWQ"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:LINKQUOTE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:LINKQUOTE</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:LWQ&amp;redirect=no">MOS:LWQ</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>Be conservative when linking within quotations: link only to targets that correspond to the meaning clearly intended by the quote's author. Where possible, link from text outside of the quotation instead  either before it or soon after. (If quoting <a href="/wiki/Hypertext" title="Hypertext">hypertext</a>, add an editorial note, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">[link in original]</span> or <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">[link added]</span>, as appropriate, to avoid ambiguity as to whether the link was made by the original author.) </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Block_quotations">Block quotations</span></h3> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Block_quotations"></span><span class="anchor" id="Block_quotes"></span> </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:BQ"></span><span id="MOS:BLOCKQUOTE"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:BQ&amp;redirect=no">MOS:BQ</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:BLOCKQUOTE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:BLOCKQUOTE</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>Format a long quote (more than about forty words or a few hundred characters, or consisting of more than one paragraph, regardless of length) as a <a href="/wiki/Block_quotation" title="Block quotation">block quotation</a>, indented on both sides. Block quotations should be enclosed in <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Blockquote" title="Template:Blockquote">blockquote</a>}}</code> (a wrapper for the <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;blockquote&gt;...&lt;/blockquote&gt;</code> HTML element). </p>
      <p>Do not enclose block quotations in quotation marks (and especially avoid large, decorative quotation marks; those provided by the <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Cquote" title="Template:Cquote">cquote</a>}}</code> template have been disabled in mainspace). Block quotations using a colored background are also discouraged. </p>
      <p>Use <code>{{blockquote}}</code> (or <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;blockquote&gt;</code> or any other template using it) only for actual quotations; <a href="#Indentation">indentation for other purposes</a> is done differently. </p>
      <p>Citations do not belong within the text of block quotations because they are not part of the quoted material. It is conventional to precede a block quotation with an introductory sentence (or sentence fragment) and append the source citation to that line. Alternatively, the <code>{{blockquote}}</code> template provides parameters for attribution and citation, which will appear below the quotation. 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(For use of dashes with attributions, see <a href="#Other_uses_(em_dash_only)">&nbsp;Other uses (em dash only)</a>.)</span> If a citation is used inside the <code>{{blockquote}}</code> template, then it must go in those citation parameters. This after-quotation attribution style is not typical in articles, and is intended for famous quotations. For most block quotations, follow the instruction above to put the citation between the attributive introduction and the quotation. A purported quotation that has no cited source should be flagged with <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Quote_without_source" title="Template:Quote without source">quote without source</a>}}</code>, or deleted. </p>
      <p>Line breaks and indentation inside a <code>{{blockquote}}</code> or <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;blockquote&gt;</code> are generally ignored; use <code class="nowrap">&lt;<a href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/Extension:Poem" class="extiw" title="mw:Extension:Poem">poem</a>&gt;</code> or <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Poem_quote" title="Template:Poem quote">poem quote</a>}}</code> for poetry, lyrics, and similar material: </p> 
      <div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-moin mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">
       <pre><span></span>{{blockquote|&lt;poem&gt;
What this grim, ungainly, ghastly, gaunt, and ominous bird of yore
            Meant in croaking "Nevermore."
&lt;/poem&gt;}}
</pre>
      </div> 
      <p>This gives: </p> <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style>
       <blockquote class="templatequote">
        <div class="poem"> 
         <p>What this grim, ungainly, ghastly, gaunt, and ominous bird of yore<br> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Meant in croaking "Nevermore." </p> 
        </div>
       </blockquote></span> 
      <p>Or quote such material inline, with line breaks indicated by <code>{{nbsp}}/</code>, and paragraph or stanza breaks by <code>{{nbsp}}//</code>. </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:PQ"></span><span id="MOS:PULLQUOTE"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:PQ&amp;redirect=no">MOS:PQ</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:PULLQUOTE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:PULLQUOTE</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Pull_quotes"></span><span class="anchor" id="Pull_quote"></span><span class="anchor" id="Pull_quotations"></span><span class="anchor" id="nocquote"></span> <a href="/wiki/Pull_quote" title="Pull quote">Pull quotes</a> do not belong in Wikipedia articles. These are the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:What_Wikipedia_is_not#Wikipedia_is_not_news" title="Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not">news and magazine style</a> of "pulling" material already in the article to reuse it in attention-grabbing decorative quotations. This unencyclopedic approach is a form of <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Editorializing" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">editorializing</a>, produces <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Provide_context_for_the_reader" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles">out-of-context</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view#Due_and_undue_weight" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">undue emphasis</a>, and may <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research">lead the reader to conclusions</a> not supported in the material. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign-language_quotations">Foreign-language quotations</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:FOREIGNQUOTE"></span><span id="MOS:QUOTEFOREIGN"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:FOREIGNQUOTE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:FOREIGNQUOTE</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:QUOTEFOREIGN&amp;redirect=no">MOS:QUOTEFOREIGN</a></span></li>
       </ul>
