      </div> 
      <p>Quotations from foreign-language sources should appear with a translation into English, preferably a modern<sup id="cite_ref-recent_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recent-11">[f]</a></sup> one. Quotations that are translations should be explicitly distinguished from those that are not. Indicate the original source of a translation (if it is available, and not first published within Wikipedia), and the original language (if that is not clear from the context). </p>
      <p>If the original, untranslated text is available, provide a reference for it or include it, as appropriate. </p>
      <p>When editors themselves translate foreign text into English, care must always be taken to include the original text, <em>in italics</em> (except for non-Latin-based writing systems), and to use actual and (if at all possible) common English words in the translation. Unless you are certain of your competency to translate something, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Translation" title="Wikipedia:Translation">Wikipedia:Translation</a> for assistance. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Punctuation">Punctuation</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For a brief guide to how some punctuation marks are used in Wikipedia for special purposes such as <i>italicizing text</i>, see <a href="/wiki/Help:Punctuation" title="Help:Punctuation">Help:Punctuation</a>.
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:PUNCT"></span><span id="MOS:&amp;#039;"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:PUNCT&amp;redirect=no">MOS:PUNCT</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:%27&amp;redirect=no">MOS:'</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Apostrophes">Apostrophes</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="WP:&amp;#039;"></span><span id="MOS:APOSTROPHE"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikipedia:%27&amp;redirect=no">WP:'</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:APOSTROPHE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:APOSTROPHE</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Foreign_characters_that_resemble_apostrophes"></span> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Use straight apostrophes (<span style="font-size: 120%;"><span class="example monospaced example-mono" style="font-family: monospace, monospace; color: #006400;">'</span></span>), not curly apostrophes (<span style="font-size: 120%;"><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad monospaced example-mono" style="font-family: monospace, monospace; color: #8B0000;"></span></span>).<sup id="cite_ref-curlyq_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-curlyq-7">[c]</a></sup> Do not use accent marks or backticks (<span style="font-size: 120%;"><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad monospaced example-mono" style="font-family: monospace, monospace; color: #8B0000;">`</span></span>) as apostrophes.</li> 
       <li>Templates such as <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:%27" title="Template:'">'</a>}}</code> and <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:%27s" title="Template:'s">'s</a>}}</code> are helpful when an apostrophe (or single quote) appears at the beginning or end of text in italics or bold, because italics and bold are themselves indicated by sequences of single quotes. Example: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Dynasty</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> first season</span> (markup: <span class="nowrap"><code>''Dynasty''{{'s}} first season</code></span>).</li> 
       <li>Letters resembling apostrophes, such as <a href="/wiki/%CA%BBokina" class="mw-redirect" title="?okina">?okina</a> (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 120%;">?</span>&nbsp;</span>&nbsp; <i>markup:</i> <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Okina" title="Template:Okina">okina</a>}}</code>), <a href="/wiki/Saltillo_(linguistics)" title="Saltillo (linguistics)">saltillo</a> (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 120%;">?</span>&nbsp;</span>&nbsp; <i>markup:</i> <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Saltillo" title="Template:Saltillo">saltillo</a>}}</code>), Hebrew <a href="/wiki/Ayin" title="Ayin">ayin</a> (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 120%;">?</span>&nbsp;</span>&nbsp; <i>markup:</i> <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Ayin" title="Template:Ayin">ayin</a>}}</code>) and Arabic <a href="/wiki/Hamza" title="Hamza">hamza</a> (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 120%;">?</span>&nbsp;</span>&nbsp; <i>markup:</i><code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Hamza" title="Template:Hamza">hamza</a>}}</code>), should be represented by those templates or by their <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> values. (Templates cannot be used in article titles; 
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">see also <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Hawaii-related_articles#Orthography,_spelling_and_formatting" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Hawaii-related articles">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Hawaii-related articles &nbsp;Orthography, spelling and formatting</a></span>.)</li> 
       <li>For <a href="/wiki/Wade%E2%80%93Giles" title="WadeGiles">WadeGiles</a> romanizations of Mandarin Chinese, use <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Asper" title="Template:Asper">asper</a>}}</code>, which makes a <a href="/wiki/Spiritus_asper" class="mw-redirect" title="Spiritus asper">spiritus asper</a> (<big>?</big>).</li> 
       <li>For languages with <a href="/wiki/Ejective_consonants" class="mw-redirect" title="Ejective consonants">ejective consonants</a>, use <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Hamza" title="Template:Hamza">hamza</a>}}</code>.</li> 
       <li>For usage of the possessive apostrophe, see <a href="#Possessives">&nbsp;Possessives</a>.</li> 
       <li>For further treatment of apostrophe usage (possessive, elision, formation of certain plurals, foreign-language issues) see the article <a href="/wiki/Apostrophe" title="Apostrophe">Apostrophe</a>.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Quotation_marks">Quotation marks</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:QUOTEMARKS"></span><span id="MOS:&amp;quot;"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:QUOTEMARKS&amp;redirect=no">MOS:QUOTEMARKS</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:%22&amp;redirect=no">MOS:"</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style#Quotations" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style">Wikipedia:Manual of Style &nbsp;Quotations</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In the material below, the term "quotation" includes conventional uses of quotation marks such as for titles of songs, chapters, episodes, and so on. Quotation marks are also used in other contexts, such as in <a href="#Animals,_plants,_and_other_organisms">cultivar names</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Quotation_characters">Quotation characters</span></h4> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:CURLY"></span><span id="MOS:CQ"></span><span id="MOS:STRAIGHT"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:CURLY&amp;redirect=no">MOS:CURLY</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:CQ&amp;redirect=no">MOS:CQ</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:STRAIGHT&amp;redirect=no">MOS:STRAIGHT</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>Use <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><span style="font-size: 120%;"><b>"</b></span>straight<span style="font-size: 120%;"><b>"</b></span></span> quotation marks, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;"><span style="font-size: 120%;"><b></b></span>curly<span style="font-size: 120%;"><b></b></span></span> ones. (For single apostrophe quotes: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><span style="font-size: 120%;"><b>'</b></span>straight<span style="font-size: 120%;"><b>'</b></span></span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;"><span style="font-size: 120%;"><b></b></span>curly<span style="font-size: 120%;"><b></b></span></span>.)<sup id="cite_ref-curlyq_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-curlyq-7">[c]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Do not use accent marks, backticks (<span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;"><span style="font-size: 120%;"><b>`</b></span>text<span style="font-size: 120%;"><b></b></span></span>), low-high (<span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">&nbsp;</span>) or <a href="/wiki/Guillemet" title="Guillemet">guillemet</a> (<span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">&nbsp;</span>) marks as quotation marks (except when such marks are <em>internal</em> to quoted non-English text&nbsp; see <a href="/wiki/MOS:CONFORM" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:CONFORM">MOS:CONFORM</a>). The symbols <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">?</span> and <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">?</span> seen in edit window dropdowns are <a href="/wiki/Prime_(symbol)" title="Prime (symbol)">prime</a> and double-prime; these are used to indicate subdivisions of the <a href="/wiki/Degree_(angle)" title="Degree (angle)">degree</a>, but not as apostrophes or quote marks.</li> 
       <li>Quotation marks and apostrophes in imported material should be changed if necessary.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Double_or_single"><span id="Double_or_single_quotation_marks"></span>Double or single</span></h4> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:DOUBLE"></span><span id="MOS:SINGLE"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:DOUBLE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:DOUBLE</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:SINGLE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:SINGLE</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>Most quotations take double quotation marks (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Bob said: "Jim ate the apple."</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[j]</a></sup> Exceptions: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Plant cultivars take <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1023754711">.mw-parser-output .vanchor>:target~.vanchor-text{background-color:#b1d2ff}</style><span class="vanchor"><span id="single_quotation_marks"></span><span id="Single_quotation_marks"></span><span class="vanchor-text">single quotation marks</span></span> (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Malus domestica</i> 'Golden Delicious'</span>; see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(flora)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (flora)">Wikipedia:Naming conventions (flora)</a>).</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Gloss_(annotation)#In_linguistics" title="Gloss (annotation)">Simple glosses</a> that translate or define unfamiliar terms take single quotes, with no comma before the definition (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Cossack</i> comes from Turkic <i lang="trk" title="Turkic languages collective text">qazaq</i> 'freebooter'</span>).</li>
      </ul> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="For_a_quotation_within_a_quotation">For a quotation within a quotation</span></h4> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:QWQ"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:QWQ&amp;redirect=no">MOS:QWQ</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>For a quotation within a quotation, use single quotes: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Bob asked: "Did Jim say 'I ate the apple' before he left?"</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>For deeper nesting, alternate between single and double quotes: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">He said, "That book asserts, 'Confucius said "Everything has beauty, but not everyone sees it.<span style="padding-right:.15em;">"</span>'<span style="padding-left:.15em;">"</span></span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>For quote marks in immediate succession, add a sliver of space by using <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:%22_%27" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:&quot; '">" '</a>}}</code>, <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:%27_%22" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:' &quot;">' "</a>}}</code>, or (as in the example just given) <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:%22_%27_%22" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:&quot; ' &quot;">" ' "</a>}}</code>: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">He announced, "The answer was 'Yes!<span style="padding-right:.15em;">'</span>"</span> Markup: <code>He announced, "The answer was 'Yes!{{<a href="/wiki/Template:%27_%22" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:' &quot;">' "</a>}}</code></li> 
       <li><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">He announced, "The answer was 'Yes!'"</span> (simply jamming ' and " together)</li>
      </ul> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Article_openings"><span id="Quotation_marks_in_article_openings"></span>Article openings</span></h4> 
      <p>In the bolded text typically appearing at the opening of an article: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Any quotation marks that are part of the title should be in bold just like the rest of the title (from <i><a href="/wiki/%22A%22_Is_for_Alibi" title="&quot;A&quot; Is for Alibi">"A" Is for Alibi</a></i>: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i><b>"A" Is for Alibi</b></i> is a mystery novel&nbsp;...</span>).</li> 
       <li>Quotation marks <i>not</i> part of the article title should not be bolded (from the article <a href="/wiki/Jabberwocky" title="Jabberwocky">Jabberwocky</a>: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">"<b>Jabberwocky</b>" is a nonsense poem&nbsp;...</span>; from <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bill" title="Buffalo Bill">Buffalo Bill</a>: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><b>William Frederick</b> "<b>Buffalo Bill</b>" <b>Cody</b> was an American soldier, bison hunter, and showman&nbsp;...</span>).</li>
      </ul> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Punctuation_before_quotations">Punctuation before quotations</span></h4> 
      <p>If a non-quoted but otherwise identical construction would work grammatically without a comma, using a comma before a quotation embedded within a sentence is optional: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The report stated "There was a 45% reduction in transmission rate."</span> (<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cf." class="extiw" title="wikt:cf.">Cf.</a> the non-quotation <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The report stated there was a 45% reduction in transmission rate.</span>)</li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The report stated, "There was a 45% reduction in transmission rate."</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>The comma-free approach is often used with partial quotations: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The report observed "a 45% reduction in transmission rate".</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Commas are usually used with interrupted quotations: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">"Life", Anas Nin wrote, "shrinks or expands in proportion to one's courage."</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>A comma is required when it would be present in the same construction if none of the material were a quotation: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">In Margaret Mead's view, "we must recognize the whole gamut of human potentialities" to enrich our culture.</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Do not insert a comma if it would confuse or alter the meaning: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Caitlyn Jenner expressed concerns about children "who are coming to terms with being true to who they are".</span> (Accurate quote of a statement about <em>some</em> children&nbsp; specifically those children "who are coming to terms<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>...")</li> 
       <li><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Caitlyn Jenner expressed concerns about children, "who are coming to terms with being true to who they are".</span> (Changes the meaning to imply Jenner was expressing concern about <em>all</em> children, while separately observing that children, in general, "are coming to terms<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>...")</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>It is clearer to use a colon to introduce a quotation if it forms a complete sentence, and this should always be done for multi-sentence quotations: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The report stated: "There was a 45% reduction in transmission rate."</span></li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Albert Einstein wrote: "Logic will get you from A to B. Imagination will take you everywhere."</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>No additional punctuation is necessary for an explicit <a href="#Words_as_words">words-as-words</a> scenario: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The message was unintelligible except for the fragments "help soon" and "how much longer before".</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Names_and_titles"><span id="Quotation_marks_with_names_and_titles"></span>Names and titles</span></h4> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Quotation_marks-Titles"></span> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For complete guidance on the handling of titles of works, see (until the material is better consolidated): 
       <ul>
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Titles" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Titles">WP:Manual of Style/Titles</a> (overview and details)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style#Titles_of_works" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style">WP:Manual of Style &nbsp;Titles of works</a> (which summarizes the key points)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style#Titles" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style">WP:Manual of Style ?Italics ?Titles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Text_formatting#Names_and_titles" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting">WP:Manual of Style/Text formatting &nbsp;Names and titles</a> (both summarize details at WP:Manual of Style/Titles)</li> 
        <li>the section you are reading now</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Lists_of_works" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Lists of works">WP:Manual of Style/Lists of works</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Music#Capitalization" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Music">WP:Manual of Style/Music &nbsp;Capitalization</a></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>Quotation marks should be used for the following names and titles: </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716">
      <div class="div-col" style="column-width: 30em;"> 
       <ul>
        <li>Articles and chapters (books and periodicals italicized)</li> 
        <li>Sections of musical pieces (pieces italicized)</li> 
        <li>Individual strips from comics and webcomics (comics italicized)</li> 
        <li>Poems (long or epic poems italicized)</li> 
        <li>Songs (albums, song cycles, operas, operettas, and oratorios italicized)</li> 
        <li>Individual episodes of television and radio series and <a href="/wiki/Serial_(radio_and_television)" title="Serial (radio and television)">serials</a> (series title italicized)<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[k]</a></sup></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>For example: The song "<a href="/wiki/Lucy_in_the_Sky_with_Diamonds" title="Lucy in the Sky with Diamonds">Lucy in the Sky with Diamonds</a>" from the album <i><a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band" title="Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band">Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band</a></i> by the band <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a>. </p>
      <p>Do not use quotation marks or italics for: </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716">
      <div class="div-col" style="column-width: 15em;"> 
       <ul>
        <li>Ancient writings</li> 
        <li>Concert tours</li> 
        <li>Locations</li> 
        <li>Myths and epics</li> 
        <li>Prayers</li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>Many, but not all, of the above items should also be in <a href="#Titles_of_works">title case</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Punctuation_inside_or_outside">Punctuation inside or outside<span id="Punctuation_inside_or_outside_quotation_marks"></span></span></h4> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="LP"></span><span class="anchor" id="LQ"></span><span class="anchor" id="TQ"></span><span class="anchor" id="logical_quotes"></span>
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855"></p>
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:LQ"></span><span id="MOS:LQUOTE"></span><span id="MOS:INOROUT"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:LQ&amp;redirect=no">MOS:LQ</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:LQUOTE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:LQUOTE</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:INOROUT&amp;redirect=no">MOS:INOROUT</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Logical_quotation_on_Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia:Logical quotation on Wikipedia">Wikipedia:Logical quotation on Wikipedia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>On the English Wikipedia, use the "<a href="/wiki/Quotation_marks_in_English#British_practice" title="Quotation marks in English">logical quotation</a>" style in all articles, regardless of the variety of English in which they are written. Include terminal punctuation within the quotation marks only if it was present in the original material, and otherwise place it after the closing quotation mark. For the most part, this means treating periods and commas in the same way as question marks: keep them inside the quotation marks if they apply only to the quoted material and outside if they apply to the whole sentence. Examples are given below. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Did Darla say, "There I am"?</span> (mark applies to whole sentence)</li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">No, she said, "Where am I?"</span> (mark applies to quoted material only)</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>If the quotation is a single word or a sentence fragment, place the terminal punctuation outside the closing quotation mark. When quoting a full sentence, the end of which coincides with the end of the sentence containing it, place terminal punctuation inside the closing quotation mark. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Marlin needed, he said, "to find Nemo".</span></li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Marlin said: "I need to find Nemo."</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>If the quoted sentence has been broken up with an editorial insertion, still include the terminal punctuation inside the closing quotation mark. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">"I need", said Marlin, "to find Nemo."</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>If the quoted sentence is followed by a <a href="/wiki/Clause" title="Clause">clause</a> that should be preceded by a comma, omit the <a href="/wiki/Full_stop" title="Full stop">full stop</a> (period)  but other terminal punctuation, such as a question mark or exclamation mark, may be retained. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Dory said, "Yes, I can read", which gave Marlin an idea.</span></li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Dory said, "Yes, I can read!", which gave Marlin an idea.</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>If the quoted sentence is followed by a clause identifying the speaker, use a comma outside the quotation mark instead of a full stop inside it, but retain any other terminal punctuation, such as question marks. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">"Why are you sleeping?", asked Darla.</span></li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">"Fish are friends, not food", said Bruce.</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Do not follow quoted words or fragments with commas inside the quotation marks, except where a longer quotation has been broken up and the comma is part of the full quotation. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">"Fish are friends," said Bruce, "not food."</span></li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">"Why", asked Darla, "are you sleeping?"</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brackets_and_parentheses">Brackets and parentheses</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:B&amp;amp;P"></span><span id="MOS:BRACKET"></span><span id="MOS:PAREN"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:B%26P&amp;redirect=no">MOS:B&amp;P</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:BRACKET&amp;redirect=no">MOS:BRACKET</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:PAREN&amp;redirect=no">MOS:PAREN</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>This section applies to both round brackets <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">(&nbsp;)</span>, often called <a href="/wiki/Bracket" title="Bracket">parentheses</a>, and square brackets <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">[&nbsp;]</span>. </p>
      <p>If a sentence contains a bracketed phrase, place the sentence punctuation outside the brackets <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">(as shown here).</span> However, where one or more sentences are wholly inside brackets, place their punctuation inside the brackets. There should be no space next to the inner side of a bracket. An opening bracket should usually be preceded by a space. This may not be the case if it is preceded by an opening quotation mark, another opening bracket, or a portion of a word: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">He rose to address the meeting: "(Ahem)&nbsp;... Ladies and gentlemen, welcome!"</span></li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Only the royal characters in the play ([Prince] Hamlet and his family) habitually speak in blank verse.</span></li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">We journeyed on the Inter[continental].</span></li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Most people are right-handed. (Some people are left-handed, but that does not make right-handed people "better" than left-handed people.)</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>There should be a space after a closing bracket, except where a punctuation mark follows (though a spaced dash would still be spaced after a closing bracket) and in unusual cases similar to those listed for opening brackets. </p>
      <p>Avoid adjacent sets of brackets. Either put the parenthetic phrases in one set separated by commas, or rewrite: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><em>Avoid</em>: <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Nikifor Grigoriev (c. 18851919) (also known as Matviy Hryhoriyiv) was a Ukrainian insurgent leader.</span></li> 
       <li><em>Better</em>: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Nikifor Grigoriev (c. 18851919, also known as Matviy Hryhoriyiv) was a Ukrainian insurgent leader.</span></li> 
       <li><em>Better</em>: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Nikifor Grigoriev (c. 18851919) was a Ukrainian insurgent leader. He was also known as Matviy Hryhoriyiv.</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Square brackets are used to indicate editorial replacements and insertions within quotations, though this should never alter the intended meaning. They serve three main purposes: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>To clarify: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">She attended [secondary] school</span>, where this was the intended meaning, but the type of school was unstated in the original sentence.</li> 
       <li>To reduce the size of a quotation: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">X contains Y, and under certain circumstances, X may contain Z as well</span> may be reduced to <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">X contains Y [and sometimes Z]</span>. When an ellipsis (...) is used to indicate that material is removed from a direct quotation, it should not normally be bracketed 
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="#Ellipses">&nbsp;Ellipses</a>)</span>.</li> 
       <li>To make the grammar work: Referring to someone's statement <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">"I hate to do laundry"</span>, one could properly write <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">She "hate[s] to do laundry"</span>.</li>
      </ul>
      <p> If a sentence includes subsidiary material enclosed in square or round brackets, it must still carry terminal punctuation <em>after</em> those brackets, regardless of any punctuation within the brackets. 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996643573"></p>
      <div class="block-indent">
       <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">She refused all requests (except for basics such as food, medicine, etc.).</span>
      </div>
      <p> However, if the entire sentence is within brackets, the closing punctuation falls within the brackets. <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">(This sentence is an example.)</span> </p>
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Brackets_and_linking">Brackets and linking</span></h4> 
      <p>Square brackets inside of links must be <a href="/wiki/Escape_character" title="Escape character">escaped</a>: </p> 
      <table class="wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td>He said, "<code><span class="example monospaced example-mono" style="font-family: monospace, monospace; color: #006400;">[[John Doe|John &amp;#91;Doe&amp;#93;]]</span></code> answered."</td> 
         <td> <p>He said, "<a href="/wiki/John_Doe" title="John Doe">John [Doe]</a> answered." </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>He said, "<code><span class="example monospaced example-mono" style="font-family: monospace, monospace; color: #006400;">[[John Doe|John {{bracket|Doe}}]]</span></code> answered."</td> 
         <td> <p>He said, "<a href="/wiki/John_Doe" title="John Doe">John [Doe]</a> answered." </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code><span class="example monospaced example-mono" style="font-family: monospace, monospace; color: #006400;">[https://example.com On the first day &amp;#91;etc.&amp;#93;]</span></code></td> 
         <td> <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://example.com">On the first day [etc.]</a> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code><span class="example monospaced example-mono" style="font-family: monospace, monospace; color: #006400;">[https://example.com On the first day {{bracket|etc.}}]</span></code></td> 
         <td> <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://example.com">On the first day [etc.]</a> </p> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The <code class="nowrap">&lt;<a href="/wiki/Help:Nowiki" class="mw-redirect" title="Help:Nowiki">nowiki</a>&gt;</code> markup can also be used: <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;nowiki&gt;[Doe]&lt;/nowiki&gt;</code> or <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;nowiki&gt;[etc.]&lt;/nowiki&gt;</code>. </p>
      <p>If a URL itself contains square brackets, the wiki-text should use the <a href="/wiki/URL_encoding" class="mw-redirect" title="URL encoding">URL-encoded</a> form <code>https://example.com/foo.php?query=<span class="example example-bold" style="font-weight: bold; color: #006400;">%5B</span>xxx<span class="example example-bold" style="font-weight: bold; color: #006400;">%5D</span>yyy</code>, rather than ...<code>query=<span class="example deprecated-content example-bad example-bold" style="font-weight: bold; color: #8B0000;">[</span>xxx<span class="example deprecated-content example-bad example-bold" style="font-weight: bold; color: #8B0000;">]</span>yyy</code>. This will avoid truncation of the link after <code>xxx</code>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ellipses">Ellipses</span></h3> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Ellipsis"></span><span class="anchor" id="..."></span><span class="anchor" id="Ellipsis_style"></span><span class="anchor" id="Ellipsis_function_and_implementation"></span>
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855"></p>
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:ELLIPSIS"></span><span id="MOS:DOTDOTDOT"></span><span id="MOS:"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:ELLIPSIS&amp;redirect=no">MOS:ELLIPSIS</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:DOTDOTDOT&amp;redirect=no">MOS:DOTDOTDOT</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:%E2%80%A6&amp;redirect=no">MOS:</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>Use an <i><a href="/wiki/Ellipsis" title="Ellipsis">ellipsis</a></i> (plural <i>ellipses</i>) if material is omitted in the course of a quotation, unless square brackets are used to <a href="/wiki/Gloss_(annotation)" title="Gloss (annotation)">gloss</a> the quotation 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="#Brackets_and_parentheses">&nbsp;Brackets and parentheses</a>, and the points below)</span>. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Wikipedia's style for an ellipsis is three unspaced dots (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code>...</code></span>); do not use the precomposed ellipsis character (<span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;"><code></code></span>) or three dots separated by spaces <span class="nowrap">(<span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;"><code>. . .</code></span>)</span></li> 
       <li>Generally, use a non-breaking space before an ellipsis, and a regular space after it: <span class="nowrap"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code>"Alpha, Bravo,{{nbsp}}... Zulu"</code></span></span> 
        <ul>
         <li>But where an ellipsis is immediately followed by any of <code>.&nbsp;?&nbsp;!&nbsp;:&nbsp;; , ) ] }</code> or by a closing quotation mark (single or double), use a non-breaking space before the ellipsis, and no space after it: 
          <dl>
           <dd>
            <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code>Jones wrote, "These stories amaze me. The facts suffer so frightfully{{nbsp}}..."</code></span>
           </dd> 
           <dd>
            <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code>"But what of the other cities? London, Paris{{nbsp}}...?"</code></span> (Place terminal punctuation after an ellipsis only if it is textually important, as is often the case with exclamation marks and question marks but rarely with periods.)
           </dd>
          </dl></li> 
         <li>Or, if the ellipsis immediately follows a quotation mark, use no space before the ellipsis, and a non-breaking space after it: 
          <dl>
           <dd>
            <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code>He continued to pursue Smith ("...{{nbsp}}to the ends of the earth", he had sworn) until his own death.</code></span>
           </dd>
          </dl></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1023754711"><span class="vanchor"><span id="Pause_or_suspension_of_speech"></span><span class="vanchor-text">Pause or suspension of speech</span></span>
       </dt> 
       <dd>
        Three dots are occasionally used to represent a pause in or suspense of speech, in which case the punctuation is retained in its original form: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Virginia's startled reply was "Could he&nbsp;...? No, I can't believe it!"</span>. When it indicates an incomplete word, no space is used between the word fragment(s) and the ellipsis: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The garbled transmission ended with "We are stranded near San L...o", interpreted as a reference to either San Leandro or San Lorenzo.</span>
       </dd> 
       <dt>
        <span class="anchor" id="Ellipses_with_square_brackets"></span>With square brackets
       </dt> 
       <dd>
        Occasionally, square brackets are placed around an ellipsis to make clear that it isn't original to the material being quoted, for example if the quoted passage itself contains an ellipsis (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">She retorted: "How do I feel? How do you <em>think</em> I&nbsp;... This is too much!&nbsp;[...] Take me home!"</span>).
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Commas">Commas</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:COMMA"></span><span id="MOS:,"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:COMMA&amp;redirect=no">MOS:COMMA</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:,&amp;redirect=no">MOS:,</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <ul> 
       <li> A pair of <a href="/wiki/Comma" title="Comma">commas</a> can bracket an <a href="/wiki/Apposition" title="Apposition">appositive</a> (as can brackets or dashes, though with greater interruption of the sentence). For example: 
        <table role="presentation" style="background:transparent"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td><em>Correct</em>: </td> 
           <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">John Smith, Janet Cooper's son, is a well-known playwright.</span> </td>
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td><em>Correct</em>: </td> 
           <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Janet Cooper's son John Smith is a well-known playwright.</span> (when Janet has multiple sons) </td>
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td><em>Correct</em>: </td> 
           <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Janet Cooper's son, John Smith, is a well-known playwright.</span> (when Janet has only one son) </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table> <p>Always use a <i>pair</i> of commas for this, unless another punctuation mark takes the place of the second comma: </p> 
        <table role="presentation" style="background:transparent"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td><em>Incorrect</em>: </td> 
           <td><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">The newest member, John Smith was blunt.</span> </td>
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td><em>Correct</em>: </td> 
           <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Blunt comments came from the newest member, John Smith.</span> </td>
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td><em>Correct</em>: </td> 
           <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The newest member, John Smith&nbsp; himself a retired teacher&nbsp; was blunt.</span> </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table> </li> 
       <li> Don't let other punctuation distract you from the need for a comma, especially when the comma collides with a bracket or parenthesis: 
        <table role="presentation" style="background:transparent"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td><em>Correct</em>: </td> 
           <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Burke and Wills, fed by locals (on beans, fish, and <i>ngardu</i>), survived for a few months.</span> </td>
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td><em>Incorrect</em>: </td> 
           <td><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Burke and Wills, fed by locals (on beans, fish, and <i>ngardu</i>) survived for a few months.</span> </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table> </li> 
       <li><span class="anchor" id="fewer_commas"></span> Modern<sup id="cite_ref-recent_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recent-11">[f]</a></sup> writing uses fewer commas; there are usually ways to simplify a sentence so that fewer are needed. 
        <table role="presentation" style="background:transparent"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td><em>Clear</em>: </td> 
           <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Schubert's heroes included Mozart, Beethoven, and Joseph and Michael Haydn.</span> </td>
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td><em>Awkward</em>: </td> 
           <td><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Mozart was, along with the Haydns, both Joseph and Michael, and also Beethoven, one of Schubert's heroes.</span> </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table> </li> 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
       <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
        <span id="MOS:GEOCOMMA"></span>
       </div>
       <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
        <div class="module-shortcutlist">
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
        </div>
        <ul>
         <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:GEOCOMMA&amp;redirect=no">MOS:GEOCOMMA</a></span></li>
        </ul>
       </div> 
       <li><span class="anchor" id="Geographical_references"></span> In geographical references that include multiple levels of subordinate divisions (e.g., city, state/province, country), a comma separates each element and follows the last element unless followed by other punctuation. 
        <table role="presentation" style="background:transparent"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td><em>Correct</em>: </td> 
           <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">He set October 1, 2011, as the deadline for Chattanooga, Oklahoma, to meet his demands.</span> </td>
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td><em>Incorrect</em>: </td> 
           <td><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">He set October 1, 2011, as the deadline for Chattanooga, Oklahoma to meet his demands.</span> </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table> </li> 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
       <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
        <span id="MOS:DATECOMMA"></span>
       </div>
       <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
        <div class="module-shortcutlist">
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
        </div>
        <ul>
         <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:DATECOMMA&amp;redirect=no">MOS:DATECOMMA</a></span></li>
        </ul>
       </div> 
       <li><span class="anchor" id="Date_commas"></span> <a href="/wiki/MOS:DATEFORMAT" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:DATEFORMAT">Dates</a> in monthdayyear format require a comma after the day, as well as after the year, unless followed by other punctuation. In both cases, the last element is treated as <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Basic_copyediting#Parenthetical_comma" title="Wikipedia:Basic copyediting">parenthetical</a>. 
        <table role="presentation" style="background:transparent"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td><em>Correct</em>: </td> 
           <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">He set October 1, 2011, as the deadline for Chattanooga, Oklahoma, to meet his demands.</span> </td>
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td><em>Incorrect</em>: </td> 
           <td><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">He set October 1, 2011 as the deadline for Chattanooga, Oklahoma, to meet his demands.</span> </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table> </li> 
       <li> Place quotation marks by following <a href="#Punctuation_inside_or_outside">&nbsp;Punctuation inside or outside</a>. This is called "logical quotation". 
        <table role="presentation" style="background:transparent"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td><em>Correct</em>: </td> 
           <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">She said, "Punctuation styles on Wikipedia change too often", and made other complaints.</span> </td>
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td><em>Incorrect</em>: </td> 
           <td><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">She said, "Punctuation styles on Wikipedia change too often," and made other complaints.</span> </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table> </li> 
       <li> A comma may be included before a quotation embedded within a sentence 
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="#Quotation_marks">&nbsp;Quotation marks</a>)</span>. </li> 
      </ul> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Serial_commas">Serial commas</span></h4> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Serial_comma"></span><span class="anchor" id="Oxford_comma"></span><span class="anchor" id="Oxford_commas"></span><span class="anchor" id="Harvard_comma"></span><span class="anchor" id="Harvard_commas"></span> </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:SERIAL"></span><span id="MOS:OXFORD"></span><span id="MOS:HARVARD"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:SERIAL&amp;redirect=no">MOS:SERIAL</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:OXFORD&amp;redirect=no">MOS:OXFORD</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:HARVARD&amp;redirect=no">MOS:HARVARD</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "MOS:OXFORD" redirects here. For Oxford spelling, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Spelling#British_English_with_&quot;-ize&quot;_(Oxford_spelling)" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Spelling">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Spelling &nbsp;British English with "-ize" (Oxford spelling)</a>.
      </div> 
      <p>A <a href="/wiki/Serial_comma" title="Serial comma">serial comma</a> (sometimes also called an <i>Oxford comma</i> or <i>Harvard comma</i>) is a comma used immediately before a conjunction (<i>and</i>, <i>or</i>, <i>nor</i>) in a list of three or more items. </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996643573">
      <div class="block-indent">
       <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">ham, chips, and eggs</span> &nbsp; serial comma
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996643573">
      <div class="block-indent">
       <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">ham, chips and eggs</span> &nbsp; no serial comma
      </div> 
      <p>Editors may use either convention so long as each article is internally consistent. Serial commas are more helpful the more complex the material, such as a list with multi-word items (especially if one contains its own <i>and</i>), or a series of probably unfamiliar terms. </p>
      <p>However, there are cases in which either omitting or including the serial comma results in ambiguity: </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996643573">
      <div class="block-indent">
       <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">The author thanked her friends, Sinad O'Connor and Bob Marley</span> &nbsp; which may list either four or more people (the friends and the two people named), or two people (O'Connor and Marley, who are the friends).
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996643573">
      <div class="block-indent">
       <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">The author thanked a friend, Sinad O'Connor, and Bob Marley</span> &nbsp; which may list either two people (O'Connor, who is the friend, and Marley), or three people (the first being the friend, the second O'Connor, and the third Marley).
      </div> 
      <p>In such cases of ambiguity, clarify one of three ways: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Add or remove the serial comma.</li> 
       <li>Use separate sentences, bullet lists, or some other structural change to clarify.</li> 
       <li>Recast the sentence ("friends" case): 
        <ul>
         <li>To list two people: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The author thanked her friends Sinad O'Connor and Bob Marley.</span> 
          <ul>
           <li>Clearer: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The author thanked two friends  Sinad O'Connor and Bob Marley.</span></li>
          </ul></li> 
         <li>To list several people: 
          <dl>
           <dd>
            <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The author thanked Sinad O'Connor, Bob Marley and her friends</span>, or
           </dd> 
           <dd>
            <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The author thanked Sinad O'Connor, Bob Marley, and her friends</span>.
           </dd>
          </dl> 
          <ul>
           <li>But not: <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">The author thanked Bob Marley, Sinad O'Connor[,] and her friends</span> &nbsp; introduces ambiguity about <i>her</i>.</li>
          </ul></li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li>Recast the sentence ("friend" case): 
        <ul>
         <li>To list two people: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The author thanked Bob Marley and her friend, Sinad O'Connor.</span> 
          <ul>
           <li>Or be more specific when possible (the commas here set off non-restrictive <a href="/wiki/Apposition" title="Apposition">appositives</a>): <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The author thanked her childhood friend, Sinad O'Connor, and her mentor, Bob Marley.</span></li>
          </ul></li> 
         <li>To list three people: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The author thanked Bob Marley, Sinad O'Connor, and a friend.</span> 
          <ul>
           <li>Clarity with gender-specific terms such as <i>mother</i> can be tricky; <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">The author thanked her mother, Kim Thayil, and Sinad O'Connor</span> is unclear because readers may not know <a href="/wiki/Kim_Thayil" title="Kim Thayil">Kim Thayil</a> is male and wouldn't be the same person as the mother.</li> 
           <li>Clearer: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The author thanked Kim Thayil, Sinad O'Connor, and her own mother</span> or <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The author thanked her mother and musicians Kim Thayil and Sinad O'Connor</span> .</li>
          </ul></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colons">Colons</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:COLON"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:COLON&amp;redirect=no">MOS:COLON</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For the "colon trick" (for linking to a category, image, or interwiki link without adding the page to the category, displaying the image, or adding the interwiki link), see <a href="/wiki/Help:Colon_trick" title="Help:Colon trick">Help:Colon trick</a>.
      </div> 
      <p>A <a href="/wiki/Colon_(punctuation)" title="Colon (punctuation)">colon</a> (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">:</span>) introduces something which demonstrates, explains, or modifies what has come before, or is a list of items that has just been introduced. The items in such a list may be separated by commas; or, if they are more complex and perhaps themselves contain commas, the items should be separated by semicolons or arranged in a bulleted list. </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996643573">
      <div class="block-indent">
       <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">We visited several tourist attractions: the Leaning Tower of Pisa, which I thought could fall at any moment; the Bridge of Sighs; the supposed birthplace of Petrarch, or at least the first known house in which he lived; and so many more.</span>
      </div> 
      <p>A colon may also be used to introduce <a href="/wiki/Quotation_marks_in_English#Quotations_and_speech" title="Quotation marks in English">direct speech</a> enclosed within quotation marks 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="#Quotation_marks">&nbsp;Quotation marks</a>)</span>. </p>
      <p>In most cases a colon works best with a complete grammatical sentence before it. When what follows the colon is also a complete sentence, start it with a capital letter, but otherwise do not capitalize after a colon except where doing so is needed for another reason, as for a proper name. Except in technical usage (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">a 3:1 ratio</span>), no sentence should contain multiple colons, no space precedes a colon, and a space (but never a hyphen or dash) follows a colon. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Semicolons">Semicolons</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:SEMICOLON"></span><span id="MOS:COMMASPLICE"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:SEMICOLON&amp;redirect=no">MOS:SEMICOLON</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:COMMASPLICE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:COMMASPLICE</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For usage in marking up description (definition) lists, see <a href="/wiki/Help:List#Description_lists" title="Help:List">Help:List &nbsp;Description lists</a>.
      </div> 
      <p>A <a href="/wiki/Semicolon" title="Semicolon">semicolon</a> (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">;</span>) is sometimes an alternative to a full stop (period), enabling related material to be kept in the same sentence; it marks a more decisive division in a sentence than a comma. If the semicolon separates clauses, normally each clause must be independent (meaning that it could stand on its own as a sentence). In many cases, only a comma or only a semicolon will be correct in a given sentence. </p> 
      <table role="presentation" style="margin:0.2em 0 0.5em 1.6em; background:transparent"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td style="padding-right:1em"><em>Correct</em>: </td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Though he had been here before, I did not recognize him.</span> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="padding-right:1em"><em>Incorrect</em>: </td> 
         <td><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Though he had been here before; I did not recognize him.</span> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Above, "Though he had been here before" cannot stand on its own as a sentence, and therefore is not an independent clause. </p> 
      <table role="presentation" style="margin:0.2em 0 0.5em 1.6em; background:transparent"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td style="padding-right:1em"><em>Correct</em>: </td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Oranges are an acidic fruit; bananas are classified as alkaline.</span> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="padding-right:1em"><em>Incorrect</em>: </td> 
         <td><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Oranges are an acidic fruit, bananas are classified as alkaline.</span> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>This incorrect use of a comma between two independent clauses is known as a <a href="/wiki/Comma_splice" title="Comma splice">comma splice</a>; however, in certain kinds of cases a comma may be used where a semicolon would seem to be called for: </p> 
      <table role="presentation" style="margin:0.2em 0 0.5em 1.6em; background:transparent"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td><em>Accepted</em>:</td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">"Life is short, art is long."</span> (two brief clauses in an <a href="/wiki/Aphorism" title="Aphorism">aphorism</a>; see <i><a href="/wiki/Ars_longa,_vita_brevis" title="Ars longa, vita brevis">Ars longa, vita brevis</a></i>) </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><em>Accepted</em>:</td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">"I have studied it, you have not."</span> (reporting brisk conversation, such as this reply of <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Newton</a>'s) </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>A sentence may contain several semicolons, especially when the clauses are parallel in construction and meaning; multiple unrelated semicolons are often signs that the sentence should be divided into shorter sentences or otherwise refashioned. </p> 
      <table role="presentation" style="margin:0.2em 0 0.5em 1.6em; background:transparent"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td style="padding-right:1em"><em>Unwieldy</em>: </td> 
         <td><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Oranges are an acidic fruit; bananas are classified as alkaline; pears are close to neutral; these distinctions are rarely discussed.</span> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="padding-right:1em"><em>One better way</em>: </td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Oranges are an acidic fruit, bananas are alkaline, and pears are close to neutral; these distinctions are rarely discussed.</span> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Semicolons are used in addition to commas to separate items in a listing, when commas alone would result in confusion. </p> 
      <table role="presentation" style="margin:0.2em 0 0.5em 1.6em; background:transparent"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td style="padding-right:1em"><em>Confusing</em>: </td> 
         <td><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Sales offices are located in Boston, Massachusetts, San Francisco, California, Singapore, and Millbank, London, England.</span> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="padding-right:1em"><em>Clear</em>: </td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Sales offices are located in Boston, Massachusetts; San Francisco, California; Singapore; and Millbank, London, England.</span> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h4><span id="Semicolon_before_.22however.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Semicolon_before_&quot;however&quot;">Semicolon before "however"</span></h4> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:HOWEVER"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:HOWEVER&amp;redirect=no">MOS:HOWEVER</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>The meaning of a sentence containing a trailing clause that starts with the word <i>however</i> depends on the punctuation preceding that word. A common error is to use the wrong punctuation, thereby changing the meaning to one not intended. </p>
      <p>When the word <i>however</i> is an adverb meaning "nevertheless", it should be preceded by a semicolon and followed by a comma. Example: </p> 
      <table role="presentation" style="margin:0.2em 0 0.5em 1.6em; background:transparent"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td></td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">It was obvious they could not convert these people; however, they tried.</span> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><em>Meaning</em>:</td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">It was obvious they could not convert these people; nevertheless, they tried.</span> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>When the word <i>however</i> is a conjunction meaning "in whatever manner", or "regardless of how", it may be preceded by a comma but not by a semicolon, and should not be followed by punctuation. Example: </p> 
      <table role="presentation" style="margin:0.2em 0 0.5em 1.6em; background:transparent"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td></td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">It was obvious they could not convert these people, however they tried.</span> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><em>Meaning</em>:</td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">It was obvious they could not convert these people, regardless of how they tried.</span> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>In the first case, the clause that starts with "however" cannot be swapped with the first clause; in the second case this can be done without change of meaning: </p> 
      <table role="presentation" style="margin:0.2em 0 0.5em 1.6em; background:transparent"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td></td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">However they tried, it was obvious they could not convert these people.</span> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><em>Meaning</em>:</td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Regardless of how they tried, it was obvious they could not convert these people.</span> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>If the two clauses cannot be swapped, a semicolon is required. </p>
      <p>A sentence or clause can also contain the word <i>however</i> in the middle, if it is an adverb meaning "although" that could have been placed at the beginning but does not start a new clause in mid-sentence. In this use, the word may be enclosed between commas. Example: </p> 
      <table role="presentation" style="margin:0.2em 0 0.5em 1.6em; background:transparent"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td></td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">He did not know, however, that the venue had been changed at the last minute.</span> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><em>Meaning</em>:</td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">However, he did not know that the venue had been changed at the last minute.</span> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hyphens">Hyphens</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:HYPHEN"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:HYPHEN&amp;redirect=no">MOS:HYPHEN</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Hyphen" title="Hyphen">Hyphens</a> (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">-</span>) indicate conjunction. There are three main uses: </p> 
      <ol>
       <li>In hyphenated personal names: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">John Lennard-Jones</span>.</li> 
       <li>To link <a href="/wiki/Prefix" title="Prefix">prefixes</a> with their main terms in certain constructions (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">quasi-scientific</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">pseudo-Apollodorus</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">ultra-nationalistic</span>). 
        <ul>
         <li>A hyphen may be used to distinguish between <a href="/wiki/Homograph" title="Homograph">homographs</a> (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">re-dress</span> means <i>dress again</i>, but <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">redress</span> means <i>remedy</i> or <i>set right</i>).</li> 
         <li>There is a clear trend to join both elements in all varieties of English (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">subsection</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">nonlinear</span>). Hyphenation clarifies when the letters brought into contact are the same (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">non-negotiable</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">sub-basement</span>) or are vowels (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">pre-industrial</span>), or where a word is uncommon (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">co-proposed</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">re-target</span>) or may be misread (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">sub-era</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">subera</span>).
