      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:CONSECUTIVE"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:CONSECUTIVE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:CONSECUTIVE</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>Where a word or phrase that includes terminal punctuation ends a sentence, do not add a second terminal punctuation mark. If a quoted phrase or title ends in a question mark or exclamation mark, it may confuse readers as to the nature of the article sentence containing it, and so is usually better reworded to be mid-sentence. Where such a word or phrase occurs mid-sentence, new terminal punctuation (usually a period) must be added at the end. </p> 
      <table role="presentation" style="margin:0.2em 0 0.5em 1.6em; background:transparent"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td><em>Incorrect</em>:</td> 
         <td><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Slovak returned to the Red Hot Chili Peppers in 1985 after growing tired of What Is This?.</span> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><em>Acceptable</em>:</td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Slovak returned to the Red Hot Chili Peppers in 1985 after growing tired of What Is This?</span> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><em>Better</em>:</td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Slovak, having grown tired of What Is This?, returned to the Red Hot Chili Peppers in 1985.</span> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><em>Incorrect</em>:</td> 
         <td><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">He made several films with Sammy Davis Jr..</span> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><em>Correct</em>:</td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">He made several films with Sammy Davis Jr.</span> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Punctuation_and_footnotes">Punctuation and footnotes</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:CITEPUNCT"></span><span id="MOS:PUNCTFOOT"></span><span id="MOS:REFPUNCT"></span><span id="MOS:PUNCTREF"></span><span id="MOS:REFSPACE"></span><span id="MOS:PF"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:CITEPUNCT&amp;redirect=no">MOS:CITEPUNCT</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:PUNCTFOOT&amp;redirect=no">MOS:PUNCTFOOT</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:REFPUNCT&amp;redirect=no">MOS:REFPUNCT</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:PUNCTREF&amp;redirect=no">MOS:PUNCTREF</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:REFSPACE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:REFSPACE</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:PF&amp;redirect=no">MOS:PF</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">Wikipedia:Citing sources</a>
      </div> 
      <p><b>Ref tags</b> (<code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;ref&gt;...&lt;/ref&gt;</code>) are used to create <i><a href="/wiki/Help:Footnotes" title="Help:Footnotes">footnotes</a></i> (sometimes called <i>endnotes</i> or just <i>notes</i>), as <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Inline_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citation footnotes</a> and sometimes <a href="/wiki/Help:Explanatory_notes" title="Help:Explanatory notes">explanatory notes</a>. All ref tags should <em>immediately</em> follow the text to which the footnote applies, with no intervening space<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[o]</a></sup>), and are placed <em>after</em> adjacent punctuation, not before (apart from the exceptions below). Adjacent ref tags should have no space between them, nor should there be any between ref tags and <a href="/wiki/Category:Inline_templates" title="Category:Inline templates">inline dispute/cleanup templates</a>. </p>
      <p>When ref tags are used, a <a href="/wiki/Help:Footnotes#Creating_the_footnote_list" title="Help:Footnotes">footnote list</a> must be added, and this is usually placed in the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Layout#Notes_and_references" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Layout">References</a> section, near the end of the article in the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:APPENDIX" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:APPENDIX">standard appendices and footers</a>. </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Note: In the examples below, the superscript callouts (for example here?<sup class="reference nowrap ltr" style="color:#002bb8;">[10]</sup>) are dummies and are not clickable.
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li><em>Example</em>: <a href="/wiki/Flightless_bird" title="Flightless bird">Flightless birds</a> have a reduced <a href="/wiki/Keel_(bird_anatomy)" title="Keel (bird anatomy)">keel</a>,<sup class="reference nowrap ltr" style="color:#002bb8;">[10]</sup> and they also have smaller wing bones than flying birds of similar size.<sup class="reference nowrap ltr" style="color:#002bb8;">[11]</sup><sup class="reference nowrap ltr" style="color:#002bb8;">[12]</sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Exceptions: Ref tags are placed <em>before</em> dashes, not after. Where a footnote applies only to material within parentheses, the ref tags belong just before the closing parenthesis. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><em>Example</em>: Paris is not the capital city of England&nbsp; the capital of which is London?<sup class="reference nowrap ltr" style="color:#002bb8;">[10]</sup>&nbsp; but that of France,<sup class="reference nowrap ltr" style="color:#002bb8;">[11]</sup> and it is widely known as a beautiful city.<sup class="reference nowrap ltr" style="color:#002bb8;">[12]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources.">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li> 
       <li><em>Example</em>: Kim Jong-un (Korean: ???;<sup class="reference nowrap ltr" style="color:#002bb8;">[10]</sup> Hanja: ???<sup class="reference nowrap ltr" style="color:#002bb8;">[11]</sup>) is the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Leader_(North_Korean_title)" title="Supreme Leader (North Korean title)">Supreme Leader of North Korea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Workers%27_Party_of_Korea" title="General Secretary of the Workers' Party of Korea">leader</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Party_of_Korea" title="Workers' Party of Korea">Workers' Party of Korea</a>.<sup class="reference nowrap ltr" style="color:#002bb8;">[a]</sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Punctuation_after_formulae">Punctuation after formulae</span></h3> 
      <p>A sentence that ends with a formula should have terminal punctuation (period, exclamation mark, or question mark) after the formula. Within a sentence, place other punctuation (such as commas or colons) after the formula just as if the text were not a formula. See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Mathematics#Punctuation_after_formulae" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Mathematics">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Mathematics &nbsp;Punctuation after formulae</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dates_and_time">Dates and time</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers &nbsp;Chronological items</a>
      </div> 
      <p>For ranges of dates and times, see <a href="#En_dashes:_other_uses">&nbsp;En dashes: other uses</a>. </p>
      <p>Dates should be <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Linking" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Linking">linked</a> only when they are germane and topical to the subject, as discussed at <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Linking#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Linking">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Linking &nbsp;Chronological items</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Time_of_day">Time of day</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/MOS:TIME" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:TIME">MOS:TIME</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Time of day is normally expressed in figures rather than being spelled out. Use context to determine whether to use the <a href="/wiki/12-hour_clock" title="12-hour clock">12-</a> or <a href="/wiki/24-hour_clock" title="24-hour clock">24-hour</a>. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Twelve-hour clock times are written in one of two forms: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">11:15&nbsp;a.m.</span> and <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">2:30&nbsp;p.m.</span>, or <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">11:15&nbsp;am</span> and <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">2:30&nbsp;pm</span>. Include a <a href="#Non-breaking_spaces">non-breaking space</a>. Use <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">noon</span> and <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">midnight</span> rather than <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">12&nbsp;pm</span> and <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">12&nbsp;am</span>; it may need to be specified whether <i>midnight</i> refers to the start or end of a date.</li> 
       <li>Twenty-four-hour clock times are written in the form <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">08:15</span> and <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">22:55</span>, with no suffix. Midnight written as <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">00:00</span> begins the day; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">24:00</span> ends it.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dates"><span id="Choice_of_format"></span><span id="Days"></span>Dates</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/MOS:DATEFORMAT" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:DATEFORMAT">MOS:DATEFORMAT</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Full dates are formatted <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><span class="nowrap">10 June 1921</span></span> or <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><span class="nowrap">June 10, 1921</span></span>; or where the year is omitted, use <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><span class="nowrap">10 June</span></span> or <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><span class="nowrap">June 10</span></span>. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>The dates in the <i>text</i> of any one article should all have the same format (day-first or month-first). 
        <ul>
         <li>For date formats in citations, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Citation_style" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">Wikipedia:Citing sources &nbsp;Citation style</a>.</li> 
         <li>Dates in quotations and titles are always left as-is.</li> 
         <li>If a numerical format is required (e.g., for conciseness in lists and tables), use the YYYY-MM-DD format: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><span class="nowrap">2005-04-03</span></span>.</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li>Articles on topics with strong ties to a particular English-speaking country should generally use the more common date format for that country (month-first for the US, except in military usage; day-first for most others; articles related to Canada may use either consistently). Otherwise, do not change an article from one date format to the other without good reason.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Months">Months</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/MOS:MONTH" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:MONTH">MOS:MONTH</a>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>For month and year, write <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">June 1921</span>, with no comma.</li> 
       <li>Abbreviations for months, such as <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Feb</span>, are used only where space is extremely limited. Such abbreviations should use three letters only, and should not be followed by a period (full point) except at the end of a sentence.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Seasons">Seasons</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/MOS:SEASON" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:SEASON">MOS:SEASON</a>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>Avoid ambiguous references to <a href="/wiki/Seasons" class="mw-redirect" title="Seasons">seasons</a>, which are different in the southern and northern hemispheres.</li> 
       <li>Names of seasons may be used when there is a logical connection to the event they are describing (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the autumn harvest</span>) or when referring to a phase of a natural yearly cycle (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">migration typically starts in mid-spring</span>). Otherwise, neutral wording is usually preferable (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">He was elected in November 1992</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">He was elected in the fall of 1992</span>).</li> 
       <li>Journals and other publications that are issued seasonally (e.g., "Summer 2005") should be dated as such in citations 
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(for more information, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Seasonal_publication_dates_and_differing_calendar_systems" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">Wikipedia:Citing sources &nbsp;Seasonal publication dates and differing calendar systems</a>)</span>.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Years_and_longer_periods">Years and longer periods</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/MOS:DECADE" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:DECADE">MOS:DECADE</a>, <a href="/wiki/MOS:CENTURY" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:CENTURY">MOS:CENTURY</a>, and <a href="/wiki/MOS:ERA" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:ERA">MOS:ERA</a>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>Do not use <i>the year</i> before the digits (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">1995</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">the year 1995</span>), unless the meaning would otherwise be unclear.</li> 
       <li>Decades are written in the format <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the 1980s</span>, with no apostrophe. Use the two-digit form ('80s) only with an established social or cultural meaning. Avoid forms such as <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">the 1700s</span> that could refer to ten or a hundred years.</li> 
       <li>Years are denoted by <a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">AD and BC</a> or, equivalently, <a href="/wiki/Common_Era" title="Common Era">CE and BCE</a>. Use only one system within an article, and do not change from one system to the other without good reason. The abbreviations are written without periods, and with a <a href="#Non-breaking_spaces">non-breaking space</a>, as in <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">5&nbsp;BC</span>. Omit AD or CE unless omitting it would cause ambiguity.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>More information on all the above topics can be found at <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers &nbsp;Chronological items</a>, including the handling of dates expressed in different calendars, and times corresponding to different time zones. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current">Current</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:As_of" title="Wikipedia:As of">Wikipedia:As of</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Relative_time_references" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch &nbsp;Relative time references</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The term "current"<sup id="cite_ref-recent_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recent-11">[f]</a></sup> should be avoided. What is current today may not be tomorrow; situations change over time. Instead, use date- and time-specific text. To help keep information updated use the <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:As_of" title="Template:As of">as of</a>}}</code> template. </p> 
      <table role="presentation" style="margin:0.2em 0 0.5em 1.6em; background:transparent"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td><em>Incorrect</em>:</td> 
         <td><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">He is the current ambassador to ...</span> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><em>Correct</em>:</td> 
         <td><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">As of March 2011, he is the ambassador to ...</span> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Numbers"><span id="Spelling_out_numbers"></span>Numbers</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers &nbsp;Numbers</a>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>Integers from zero to nine are spelled out in words. Integers greater than nine <em>expressible in one or two words</em> may be expressed either in numerals or in words. Other numbers are given in numerals or in forms such as <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">21<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>million</span>. See <a href="/wiki/MOS:NUM#Numbers_as_figures_or_words" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:NUM">MOS:NUM &nbsp;Numbers as figures or words</a>.</li> 
       <li>In general, use a comma in numbers with five or more digits to the left of the decimal point. Numbers with four digits are at the editor's discretion: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">12,345</span>, but either <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">1,000</span> or <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">1000</span>. See <a href="/wiki/MOS:NUM#Grouping_of_digits" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:NUM">MOS:NUM &nbsp;Grouping of digits</a>.</li> 
       <li>In general, use decimals rather than fractions for measurements, but fractions are sometimes used with <a href="/wiki/Imperial_units" title="Imperial units">imperial</a> and <a href="/wiki/U.S._customary_units" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. customary units">U.S. customary</a> units. Keep articles internally consistent.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Scientific_notation" title="Scientific notation">Scientific notation</a> (e.g., <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7007580000000000000?"></span>5.8<span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;"></span>10<sup>7</sup>&nbsp;kg</span></span>) is preferred in scientific contexts. Markup: <code>{{val|5.8|e=7|u=kg}}</code>.</li> 
       <li>Write out "million" and "billion" on the first use. After that, unspaced "M" can be used for millions and "bn" for billions: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">70M</span> and <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">25bn</span>. See <a href="/wiki/MOS:NUM#Numbers_as_figures_or_words" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:NUM">MOS:NUM &nbsp;Numbers as figures or words</a> for similar words.</li> 
       <li>Write <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">3%</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">three percent</span>, or <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">three per cent</span>, but not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">3<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>%</span> (with a space) or <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">three<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>%</span>. "Percent" is American usage, and "per cent" is British usage 
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="#National_varieties_of_English">&nbsp;National varieties of English</a>)</span>. In ranges of percentages written with an en dash, write only a single percent sign: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">314%</span>.</li> 
       <li>Indicate uncertainties as e.g., <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7023153400000000000?"></span>(1.534<span style="margin-left:0.3em;margin-right:0.15em;"></span>0.35)<span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;"></span>10<sup>23</sup>&nbsp;m</span></span>. Markup: <code>{{val|1.534|0.35|e=23|u=m}}</code>. See <a href="/wiki/MOS:NUM#Uncertainty_and_rounding" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:NUM">MOS:NUM &nbsp;Uncertainty and rounding</a> for other formats.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Currencies">Currencies</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Currencies_and_monetary_values" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers &nbsp;Currencies and monetary values</a>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>Use the full abbreviation on first use (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">US$</span> for the US dollar and <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">A$</span> for the Australian dollar), <em>unless the currency is already clear from context</em>. For example, the government of the United States always spends money in American dollars, and never in Canadian or Australian dollars.</li> 
       <li>Use only one symbol with ranges, as in <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">$250300</span>.</li> 
       <li>In articles that are not specific to a country, express amounts of money in <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollars" class="mw-redirect" title="United States dollars">United States dollars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Euros" class="mw-redirect" title="Euros">euros</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Pounds_sterling" class="mw-redirect" title="Pounds sterling">pounds sterling</a>. Do not link the names or symbols of currencies that are commonly known to English-speakers (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">$</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"></span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"></span>), unless there is a particular reason to do so; do not use potentially ambiguous currency symbols, unless the meaning is clear in the context.</li> 
       <li>In country-specific articles, use the currency of the country. On first occurrence, consider including conversion to US dollars, euros, or pounds sterling, at a rate appropriate to the context. For example, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Since 2001 the grant has been 10,000,000 <a href="/wiki/Swedish_krona" title="Swedish krona">Swedish kronor</a> (1.0M as of August 2009)</span>. Wording such as "approx." is not appropriate for simple rounding-off of the converted amount.</li> 
       <li>Generally, use the full name of a currency, and link it on its first appearance if English-speakers are likely to be unfamiliar with it (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">52 <a href="/wiki/Nepalese_rupee" title="Nepalese rupee">Nepalese rupees</a></span>); subsequent occurrences can use the currency sign (just <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">88 Rs</span>).</li> 
       <li>Most currency symbols are placed <em>before</em> the number, and unspaced <span class="nowrap">(<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">$123</span> not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">$ 123</span>).</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Units_of_measurement">Units of measurement</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Units_of_measurement" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers &nbsp;Units of measurement</a>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>The main unit in which a quantity is expressed should generally be an <a href="/wiki/International_System_of_Units" title="International System of Units">SI</a> unit or <a href="/wiki/Non-SI_units_mentioned_in_the_SI" title="Non-SI units mentioned in the SI">non-SI unit officially accepted for use with the SI</a>. However, 
        <ul>
         <li>Scientific articles may also use specialist units appropriate for the branch of science in question.</li> 
         <li>In non-scientific articles with strong ties to the United States, the main unit is generally a U.S. customary unit (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">22 pounds (10 kg)</span>).</li> 
         <li>In non-scientific articles with strong ties to the United Kingdom, although the main unit is generally a metric unit (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">10 kilograms (22 lb)</span>), imperial units are still used as the main units in some contexts (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">7 miles (11 km) by road</span>).</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li>Where English-speaking countries use different units for the same measurement, provide a conversion in parentheses. Examples: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Mississippi River is 2,320 miles (3,734&nbsp;km) long</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the Murray River is 2,375 kilometres (1,476&nbsp;mi) long</span>. The <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Convert" title="Template:Convert">convert</a>}}</code> template is useful for producing such expressions.</li> 
       <li>In a direct quotation, always retain the source's units. Any conversion should follow in square brackets (or, an obscure use of units can be explained in a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Footnotes" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Footnotes">footnote</a>).</li> 
       <li>Where space is limited (such as tables, infoboxes, parenthetical notes, and mathematical formulas) unit symbols are preferred. In prose, unit names should be given in full if used only a few times but symbols may be used when a unit (especially one with a long name) is used repeatedly after spelling out the first use (e.g., <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Up to 15 kilograms of filler is used for a batch of 250<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>kg</span>), except for unit names that are hardly ever spelled out (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">C</span> rather than <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">degrees Celsius</span>).</li> 
       <li>Most unit names are not capitalized. (For spelling differences, follow <a href="#National_varieties_of_English">&nbsp;National varieties of English</a>.)</li> 
       <li>Use "per" when writing out a unit, rather than a slash: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">metre per second</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">metre/second</span>.</li> 
       <li>Units unfamiliar to general readers should be presented as a namesymbol pair on first use, linking the unit name (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Energies were originally 2.3 <a href="/wiki/Megaelectronvolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Megaelectronvolt">megaelectronvolts</a> (MeV), but were eventually 6<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>MeV</span>).</li> 
       <li>For ranges, see <a href="#En_dashes:_other_uses">&nbsp;En dashes: other uses</a>, and MOS:NUM, at &nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Date_ranges" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">Date ranges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Percentages" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">Percentages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Unit_names_and_symbols" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">Unit names and symbols</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Formatting_of_monetary_values" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">Formatting of monetary values</a>.</li> 
       <li>Unit symbols are preceded by figures, not by spelled-out numbers. Values and unit symbols are separated by a <a href="/wiki/Non-breaking_space" title="Non-breaking space">non-breaking space</a>. For example, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">5&nbsp;min</span>. The percent sign and units of degrees, minutes, and seconds <em>for angles and coordinates</em> are unspaced.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Common_mathematical_symbols">Common mathematical symbols</span></h2> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:COMMONMATH"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:COMMONMATH&amp;redirect=no">MOS:COMMONMATH</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Mathematics" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Mathematics">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Mathematics</a>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>For a negative sign or subtraction operator, use a minus sign (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">?</span>, Unicode character U+2212 <small>MINUS SIGN</small>). Input by clicking on it in the insert box beneath the edit window or by typing <code>&amp;minus;</code>.</li> 
       <li>For multiplication, use a multiplication sign (<span class="nowrap">
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734"><span class="monospaced">U+00D7</span> </span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em"></span> <span style="font-size:85%;">MULTIPLICATION SIGN</span>) or a dot (<span class="nowrap">
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734"><span class="monospaced">U+22C5</span> </span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em">?</span> <span style="font-size:85%;">DOT OPERATOR</span>), which are input by clicking on them in the edit toolbox under the edit window or by entering <code>&amp;times;</code> or <code>&amp;sdot;</code>. Care should be taken not to confuse the dot operator (in the "Math and logic" section of the edit toolbox) with an interpunct (in the "Insert" section of the edit toolbox) or a bullet. The letter <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">x</span> should not be used to indicate multiplication, but it is used (unspaced) as the substitute for "by" in terms such as <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><a href="/wiki/4x4" class="mw-redirect" title="4x4">4x4</a></span>.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Exponentiation" title="Exponentiation">Exponentiation</a> is indicated by a superscript, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>a</i><sup><i>n</i></sup></span> (typed as <code>''a''&lt;sup&gt;''n''&lt;/sup&gt;</code>.</li> 
       <li>Do not use programming language notation outside computer program text. In most programming languages, subtraction, multiplication, and exponentiation are represented by the <a href="/wiki/Hyphen-minus" title="Hyphen-minus">hyphen-minus</a> <code>-</code>, the <a href="/wiki/Asterisk" title="Asterisk">asterisk</a> <code>*</code>, and either the <a href="/wiki/Caret" title="Caret">caret</a> <code>^</code> or the double asterisk <code>**</code>; <a href="/wiki/Scientific_notation" title="Scientific notation">scientific notation</a> is replaced by <a href="/wiki/E_notation" class="mw-redirect" title="E notation">E notation</a>.</li> 
       <li>Symbols for <a href="/wiki/Binary_operator" class="mw-redirect" title="Binary operator">binary operators</a> and <a href="/wiki/Binary_relation" title="Binary relation">relations</a> are usually spaced on both sides: 
        <ul>
         <li>plus, minus, and plus-or-minus (as binary operators): <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">+</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">?</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"></span> (as in <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">5&nbsp;?&nbsp;3</span>);</li> 
         <li>multiplication and division: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"></span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"></span>;</li> 
         <li>equals, does not equal, equals approximately: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">=</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">?</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">?</span>;</li> 
         <li>is less than, is less than or equal to, is greater than, is greater than or equal to: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">&lt;</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">?</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">&gt;</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">?</span>.</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li>Symbols for <a href="/wiki/Unary_operator" class="mw-redirect" title="Unary operator">unary operators</a> are closed-up to their operand: 
        <ul>
         <li>positive, negative, and positive-or-negative signs: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">+</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">?</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"></span> (as in <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">?3</span>);</li> 
         <li>other unary operators, such as the exclamation mark as a <a href="/wiki/Factorial" title="Factorial">factorial</a> sign (as in <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">5!</span>).</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li>Variables are italicized, but digits and punctuation are not; only <i>x</i> and <i>y</i> are italicized in <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">2(5<i>x</i>&nbsp;+&nbsp;<i>y</i>)<sup>2</sup></span>.</li> 
       <li>The <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Math" title="Template:Math">math</a>}}</code> template can be used to style formulas in a serif font to help distinguish them from surrounding text. For single variables, <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Mvar" title="Template:Mvar">mvar</a>}}</code> is also available.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar_and_usage">Grammar and usage</span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Possessives">Possessives</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:POSS"></span><span id="MOS:&amp;#039;S"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:POSS&amp;redirect=no">MOS:POSS</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:%27S&amp;redirect=no">MOS:'S</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For the apostrophe character, see <a href="#Apostrophes">&nbsp;Apostrophes</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For thorough treatment of the English possessive, see <a href="/wiki/Apostrophe" title="Apostrophe">Apostrophe</a>.
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Singular_nouns">Singular nouns</span></h4> 
      <p>For the possessive of singular nouns, including proper names and words ending in <i>s</i>, add <i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s</i> (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">my daughter's achievement</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">my niece's wedding</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Cortez's men</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the boss's office</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Illinois's largest employer</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Descartes's philosophy</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Verreaux's eagle</span>). Exception: abstract nouns ending with an /s/ sound, when followed by <i>sake</i> (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">for goodness' sake</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">for his conscience' sake</span>). If a name ending in <i>s</i> or <i>z</i> would be difficult to pronounce with <i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s</i> added (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Jesus's teachings</span>), consider rewording (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the teachings of Jesus</span>). </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Plural_nouns">Plural nouns</span></h4> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:PLURALNOUN"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:PLURALNOUN&amp;redirect=no">MOS:PLURALNOUN</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>For a normal plural noun, ending with a pronounced <i>s</i>, form the possessive by adding just an apostrophe (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">my sons' wives</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">my nieces' weddings</span>).</li> 
       <li>For a plural noun <em>not</em> ending with a pronounced <i>s</i>, add <i>'s</i> (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">women's careers</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">people's habits</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">mice's whiskers</span>; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The two Dumas's careers were controversial</span>, but where rewording is an option, this may be better: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The career of each Dumas was controversial</span>).</li>
      </ul> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_names">Official names</span></h4> 
      <p>Official names (of companies, organizations, or places) should not be altered. (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><a href="/wiki/St_Thomas%27_Hospital" title="St Thomas' Hospital">St Thomas' Hospital</a></span> should therefore <em>not</em> be rendered as <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">St Thomas's Hospital</span> or <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">St. Thomas Hospital</span>, even for consistency.) </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First-person_pronouns">First-person pronouns<span class="anchor" id="First-person_pronouns"></span></span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:I"></span><span id="MOS:OUR"></span><span id="MOS:PERSON"></span><span id="MOS:WE"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:I&amp;redirect=no">MOS:I</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:OUR&amp;redirect=no">MOS:OUR</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:PERSON&amp;redirect=no">MOS:PERSON</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:WE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:WE</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Use_of_pronouns" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles">Wikipedia:Writing better articles &nbsp;Use of pronouns</a>
      </div> 
      <p>To maintain an objective and impersonal encyclopedic voice, an article should never refer to its editors or readers using <i>I</i>, <i>my</i>, <i>we</i>, <i>us</i>, or similar forms: <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">We note that some have argued against our proposal</span>. But some such forms are acceptable in certain figurative uses. For example: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>In historical articles to mean the modern world as a whole: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Only portions of <i>De re publica</i> have come down to us.</span></li> 
       <li>The <a href="/wiki/Author%27s_we" class="mw-redirect" title="Author's we">author's <i>we</i></a> found in scientific writing (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">We construct <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">S</span> as follows</span>), though rephrasing to use <a href="/wiki/English_passive_voice" title="English passive voice">passive voice</a> may be preferable (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">S</span> is constructed as follows</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-passive_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-passive-23">[p]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second-person_pronouns">Second-person pronouns<span class="anchor" id="Second-person_pronouns"></span></span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:YOU"></span><span id="MOS:BAIT"></span><span id="MOS:PEDAGOGY"></span><span id="MOS:SOCRATIC"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:YOU&amp;redirect=no">MOS:YOU</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:BAIT&amp;redirect=no">MOS:BAIT</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:PEDAGOGY&amp;redirect=no">MOS:PEDAGOGY</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:SOCRATIC&amp;redirect=no">MOS:SOCRATIC</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "WP:YOU" redirects here. For "Wikipedia is not about <em>you</em>", see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTYOU" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTYOU">WP:NOTYOU</a>.
      </div> 
      <p>Avoid addressing the reader using <i>you</i> or <i>your</i>, which sets an inappropriate tone 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see also <a href="#Instructional_and_presumptuous_language">&nbsp;Instructional and presumptuous language</a>)</span>. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Use a noun or a third-person pronoun: instead of <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">When you move past "Go", you collect $200</span>, use <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">A player passing "Go" collects $200</span>, or <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">When a player passes "Go", they collect $200</span>.</li> 
       <li>If a person cannot be specified, or when implying "anyone" as a subject, the pronoun <i><a href="/wiki/One_(pronoun)" title="One (pronoun)">one</a></i> may be used: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">a sense that one is being watched</span>. Other constructions may be preferable if <i>one</i> seems stilted: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">a person's sense of being watched</span>.</li> 
       <li>The <a href="/wiki/English_passive_voice" title="English passive voice">passive voice</a> may sometimes be used instead:<sup id="cite_ref-passive_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-passive-23">[p]</a></sup> <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Impurities are removed before bottling</span>.</li> 
       <li>Do not bait links, e.g., "<span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Click here for more information</span>"; let the browser's normal highlighting invite a click. ("<span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Click here</span>" also makes no sense to someone reading on paper.)</li> 
       <li>Likewise, "See: (reference)" or "Consider ..." are milder second-person baits, common in academic writing (<a href="/wiki/Pedagogy" title="Pedagogy">pedagogy</a>). This interactive personality is inconsistent with an encyclopedia's passive presentation of objective matter. 
        <ul>
         <li>"See" and the like can be used to internally cross-reference other Wikipedia material. Do not italicize words like "see". Such a cross reference should be parenthetical, so the article text stands alone if the parenthetical is removed. The <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Cross_reference" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Cross reference">Cross reference</a>}}</code> template can be used for this: <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Cross_reference" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Cross reference">Cross reference</a>|(see [[Chicken]])}}</code>, <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Cross_reference" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Cross reference">Cross reference</a>|(See [[Dacian language]] for details.)}}</code> It is usually better to rewrite the material to integrate these links contextually rather than use <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Self-references_to_avoid" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Self-references to avoid">explicit Wikipedia self-references</a>.</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li>Do not address the reader with the <a href="/wiki/Socratic_method" title="Socratic method">Socratic method</a> by asking and answering questions. <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Did <a href="/wiki/Francis_Bacon" title="Francis Bacon">Bacon</a> write <a href="/wiki/Shakespeare" class="mw-redirect" title="Shakespeare">Shakespeare</a>? Then who wrote Bacon?</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plurals">Plurals</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:PLURALS"></span><span id="MOS:SINGULAR"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:PLURALS&amp;redirect=no">MOS:PLURALS</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:SINGULAR&amp;redirect=no">MOS:SINGULAR</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/English_plurals" title="English plurals">English plurals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Collective_noun" title="Collective noun">Collective noun</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For the article title guideline, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(plurals)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (plurals)">Wikipedia:Naming conventions (plurals)</a>.
      </div> 
      <p>Use the appropriate plural; allow for cases (such as <i><a href="/wiki/Excursus" title="Excursus">excursus</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Hanif" title="Hanif">hanif</a></i>) in which a word is now listed in major English dictionaries, and normally takes an <i>s</i> or <i>es</i> plural, not its original plural: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">two excursuses</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">two <i><i lang="la" title="Latin-language text">excursus</i></i></span> as in Latin; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">two hanifs</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">two <i>hunafa</i></span> as in Arabic. </p>
      <p>Some <a href="/wiki/Collective_noun" title="Collective noun">collective nouns</a>&nbsp; such as <i>team</i> (and proper names of them), <i>army</i>, <i>company</i>, <i>crowd</i>, <i>fleet</i>, <i>government</i>, <i>majority</i>, <i>mess</i>, <i>number</i>, <i>pack</i>, and <i>party</i>&nbsp; may refer either to a single entity or to the members that compose it. In British English, such words are sometimes treated as singular, but more often treated as plural, according to context. Exceptionally, names of towns and countries usually take singular verbs (unless they are being used to refer to a team or company by that name, or when discussing actions of that entity's government). For example, in <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> are playing <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> tonight</span>, <i>England</i> refers to a <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> team; but in <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">England is the most populous country of the United Kingdom</span>, it refers to the country. In North American English, these words (and <i>the United States</i>, for historical reasons) are almost invariably treated as singular; the major exception is when sports teams are referred to by nicknames, plural verbs are commonly used to match e.g., <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Heat" title="Miami Heat">Heat</a> are playing the Lakers</span>. See also <a href="#National_varieties_of_English">&nbsp;National varieties of English</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb_tense">Verb tense</span></h3> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Tense"></span><span class="anchor" id="TENSE"></span><span class="anchor" id="VERBTENSE"></span>
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855"></p>
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:TENSE"></span><span id="MOS:VERB"></span><span id="WP:WAS"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:TENSE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:TENSE</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:VERB&amp;redirect=no">MOS:VERB</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikipedia:WAS&amp;redirect=no">WP:WAS</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "MOS:PRESENT" redirects here. For the guideline on words such as "currently", "soon", and "recently", see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Statements_likely_to_become_outdated" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers &nbsp;Statements likely to become outdated</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Biography#Tense" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Biography">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Biography &nbsp;Tense</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Relative_time_references" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch &nbsp;Relative time references</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Tense_in_fiction" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles">Wikipedia:Writing better articles &nbsp;Tense in fiction</a>
      </div> 
      <p>By default, write articles in the present tense, including those covering works of fiction 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Tense_in_fiction" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles">Wikipedia:Writing better articles &nbsp;Tense in fiction</a>)</span> and products or works that have been discontinued. However, articles about periodicals that are no longer being produced should normally, and with commonsense exceptions, use the past tense. Generally, do not use past tense except for past events, subjects that are dead or no longer meaningfully exist, or periodicals and similar written material that are no longer being produced. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The PDP-10 is a mainframe computer family manufactured by Digital Equipment Corporation from 1966 into the 1980s.</span></li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Earth: Final Conflict</i> is a Canadian science fiction television series that ran for five seasons between October 6, 1997, and May 20, 2002.</span></li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The Gordon Riots of 1780 were<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>...</span></li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The Beatles were an English rock band that formed in Liverpool in 1960.</span></li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Barack Obama is a former president of the United States</span> (not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Barack Obama was a president of the United States</span>).</li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Jumbo Comics was an adventure anthology comic book published by Fiction House from 1938 to 1953</span></li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>A Prairie Home Companion</i> is a radio show that aired live from 1974 to 2016</span> (not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;"><i>A Prairie Home Companion</i> was a radio show</span>).</li> 
       <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>Flappy Bird</i> is a mobile game developed by Vietnamese video game artist and programmer Dong Nguyen</span> (not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;"><i>Flappy Bird</i> was a mobile game</span>)</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Tense can be used to distinguish between current and former status of a subject: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Dn Aonghasa <strong>is</strong> the ruin of a prehistoric Irish cliff fort. Its original shape <strong>was</strong> presumably oval or D-shaped, but parts of the cliff and fort have since collapsed into the sea.</span> (Emphasis added to distinguish the different tense usages; Dn Aonghasa is a structure that was later damaged by an event.) </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">Vocabulary</span></h2> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="VOCAB"></span><span class="anchor" id="VOCABULARY"></span> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contractions">Contractions</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:CONTRACTIONS"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:CONTRACTIONS&amp;redirect=no">MOS:CONTRACTIONS</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Abbreviations#Contractions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Abbreviations">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Abbreviations &nbsp;Contractions</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Avoid <a href="/wiki/Contraction_(grammar)" title="Contraction (grammar)">contractions</a>, which have little place in formal writing. For example, write <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i>do not</i></span> instead of <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;"><i>don't</i></span>. Use of <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">o'clock</span> is an exception. Contracted titles such as <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Dr.</span> and <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">St</span> generally should not be used but may apply in some contexts (e.g., quoted material, place names, titles of works). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gender-neutral_language">Gender-neutral language</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "MOS:GENDER" redirects here. For the style guideline regarding pronoun usage for individuals whose gender might be questioned, see <a href="/wiki/MOS:GENDERID" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:GENDERID">MOS:GENDERID</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For an essay with suggestions and sample usage, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Gender-neutral_language" title="Wikipedia:Gender-neutral language">Wikipedia:Gender-neutral language</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_about_women" title="Wikipedia:Writing about women">Wikipedia:Writing about women</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:GNL"></span><span id="MOS:S/HE"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:GNL&amp;redirect=no">MOS:GNL</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:S/HE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:S/HE</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>Use <a href="/wiki/Gender-neutral_language" title="Gender-neutral language">gender-neutral language</a>  avoiding the <a href="/wiki/Generic_he" class="mw-redirect" title="Generic he">generic <i>he</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/Generic_she" class="mw-redirect" title="Generic she">generic <i>she</i></a>, for example  where this can be done with clarity and precision. This does not apply to direct quotations or the titles of works (<i><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The Ascent of Man</span></i>), which should not be altered, or to wording about one-gender contexts, such as an all-female school (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">When any student breaks that rule, she loses privileges</span>). </p>
      <p>References to space programs, past, present and future, should use gender-neutral phrasing: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">human spaceflight</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">robotic probe</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">uncrewed mission</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">crewed spacecraft</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">piloted</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">unpiloted</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">astronaut</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">cosmonaut</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">manned</span> or <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">unmanned</span>. Direct quotations and proper nouns that use gendered words should not be changed, like <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Manned Maneuvering Unit</span>. </p>
      <p>Ships may be referred to using either neuter forms ("it", "its") or feminine forms ("she", "her", "hers"). Either usage is acceptable, but each article should be internally consistent and employ one or the other exclusively. As with all optional styles, articles should not be changed from one style to another unless there is a substantial reason to do so. See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Military_history#Pronouns" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Military history">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Military history &nbsp;Pronouns</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contested_vocabulary">Contested vocabulary</span></h3> 
      <p>Avoid words and phrases that give the impression of straining for formality, that are unnecessarily regional, or that are not widely accepted. See <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_words_with_disputed_usage" title="List of English words with disputed usage">List of English words with disputed usage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:List_of_commonly_misused_English_words" title="Wikipedia:List of commonly misused English words">Wikipedia:List of commonly misused English words</a>; see also <a href="#Identity">&nbsp;Identity</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Instructional_and_presumptuous_language">Instructional and presumptuous language</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:INSTRUCT"></span><span id="MOS:NOTE"></span><span id="MOS:NOTED"></span><span id="MOS:PRESUME"></span><span id="MOS:QUESTION"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:INSTRUCT&amp;redirect=no">MOS:INSTRUCT</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:NOTE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:NOTE</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:NOTED&amp;redirect=no">MOS:NOTED</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:PRESUME&amp;redirect=no">MOS:PRESUME</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:QUESTION&amp;redirect=no">MOS:QUESTION</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "MOS:NOTE" redirects here. For footnotes, see <a href="/wiki/Help:Footnotes" title="Help:Footnotes">Help:Footnotes</a>. For hatnotes, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Hatnote" title="Wikipedia:Hatnote">Wikipedia:Hatnote</a>. For musical notes, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Music#Images_and_notation" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Music">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Music &nbsp;Images and notation</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Editorializing" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch &nbsp;Editorializing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Information_style_and_tone" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles">Wikipedia:Writing better articles &nbsp;Information style and tone</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Self-references_to_avoid#Note_that_..." title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Self-references to avoid">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Self-references to avoid &nbsp;Note that ...</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Avoid such phrases as <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">remember that</span> and <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">note that</span>, which <a href="/wiki/Imperative_mood" title="Imperative mood">address readers directly</a> in an <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Tone" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles">unencyclopedic tone</a> and lean toward <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:What_Wikipedia_is_not#Wikipedia_is_not_a_manual,_guidebook,_textbook,_or_scientific_journal" title="Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not">instructional</a>. They are a subtle form of <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Self-references_to_avoid" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Self-references to avoid">Wikipedia self-reference</a>, "breaking the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_wall" title="Fourth wall">fourth wall</a>". Similarly, phrases such as <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">of course</span>, <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">naturally</span>, <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">obviously</span>, <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">clearly</span>, and <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">actually</span> make presumptions about readers' knowledge, may <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">express a viewpoint</a>, and may call into question the reason for including the information in the first place. Do not <em>tell</em> readers that something is ironic, surprising, unexpected, amusing, coincidental, etc. Simply state the sourced facts and allow readers to draw their own conclusions. Such constructions can usually just be deleted, leaving behind proper sentences with a more academic and less pushy tone: <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Note that this was naturally subject to controversy in more conservative newspapers.</span> becomes <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">This was subject to controversy in more conservative newspapers.</span> </p>
      <p>Avoid rhetorical questions, especially <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style#Section_headings" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style">in headings</a>. Use a heading of <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Active listening</span> and text such as <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The term <i>active listening</i>, coined in&nbsp;...</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">What is <i>active listening</i>?</span>. </p>
      <p>A neutral <a href="/wiki/Template:Crossreference" title="Template:Crossreference">cross-reference</a> is permissible&nbsp; e.g., <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see also <a href="/wiki/Bulverism" title="Bulverism">Bulverism</a></span>)</span>&nbsp; but it is usually better recast as a sentence with a link. <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><a href="/wiki/Bulverism" title="Bulverism">Bulverism</a>, also known as the psychogenetic fallacy, is a related logic flaw.</span> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subset_terms">Subset terms</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:SUBSET"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
