        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:SUBSET&amp;redirect=no">MOS:SUBSET</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>A <i>subset term</i> identifies a set of members of a larger class. Common subset terms are <i>including</i>, <i>among</i>, and <i>etc.</i> Avoid redundant subset terms (e.g., mis-constructions like <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;"><strong>Among</strong> the most well-known members of the fraternity are <strong>included</strong> two members of the Onassis family</span> or <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">The elements in stars <strong>include</strong> hydrogen, helium, <strong>etc.</strong></span>). The word <i>including</i> does not introduce a complete list; instead, use <i>consisting of</i>, or <i>composed of</i>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Identity">Identity</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:IDENTITY"></span><span id="MOS:ID"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:IDENTITY&amp;redirect=no">MOS:IDENTITY</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:ID&amp;redirect=no">MOS:ID</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Biographies#Child_named_for_parent_or_predecessor" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Biographies">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Biographies &nbsp;Child named for parent or predecessor</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Self-published_or_questionable_sources_as_sources_on_themselves" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">Wikipedia:Verifiability &nbsp;Self-published or questionable sources as sources on themselves</a>
      </div> 
      <p>When there is a discrepancy between the term most commonly used by reliable sources for a person or group and the term that person or group uses for themselves, use the term that is most commonly used by recent<sup id="cite_ref-recent_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recent-11">[f]</a></sup> reliable sources. If it is unclear which is most used, use the term that the person or group uses. </p>
      <p>Disputes over how to refer to a person or group are addressed by Wikipedia <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Content_policies" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Content policies">content policies</a>, such as those on <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verifiability</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">neutral point of view</a> (and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Article_titles" title="Wikipedia:Article titles">article titles</a> when the term appears in the title of an article). </p>
      <p>Use specific terminology. For example, it is often more appropriate for people or things from Ethiopia (a country in Africa) to be described as <i>Ethiopian</i>, not carelessly (with the risk of <a href="/wiki/Stereotyping" class="mw-redirect" title="Stereotyping">stereotyping</a>) as <i>African</i>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gender_identity">Gender identity</span></h4> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="GENDERID"></span> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Biography#Gender_identity" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Biography">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Biography &nbsp;Gender identity</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Biography#Gender_identity" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Biography">Specific guidelines apply</a> to any person whose gender might be questioned, and any living transgender or non-binary person. In summary: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Use gendered words only if they reflect the person's latest self-identification as reported in recent sources.</li> 
       <li>If the person is living and was not notable yet when a former name was in use, that name should not be included in any Wikipedia page, even in quotations, as a privacy matter. Exception: Do not expunge or replace names in source citations (whether as authors or mentioned in work titles).</li> 
       <li>Former names under which a living person was notable should be introduced with "born" or "formerly" in the lead sentence of their main biographical article. Name and gender matters should be explained at first appearance in that article, without overemphasis. In articles on works or other activities of such a person, use their current name by default, and give another name associated with that context in a parenthetical or footnote, only if they were notable under that name. In other articles, do not go into detail about such a person's name or gender except when directly relevant to the context.</li> 
       <li>Avoid confusing constructions by rewriting. Paraphrase, elide, or use square brackets to replace portions of quotations as needed to avoid confusion, former names, and mismatching gendered words.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference selfref">For examples and finer points, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Biography#Gender_identity" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Biography">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Biography &nbsp;Gender identity</a>.</span> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_terms">Foreign terms</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:FOREIGN"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:FOREIGN&amp;redirect=no">MOS:FOREIGN</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Accessibility#Other_languages" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility &nbsp;Other languages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Wikipedia_Manual_of_Style_(regional)" title="Category:Wikipedia Manual of Style (regional)">Category:Wikipedia Manual of Style (regional)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Help:Interlanguage_links" title="Help:Interlanguage links">Help:Interlanguage links</a>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="No_common_usage_in_English">No common usage in English</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Text_formatting#Foreign_terms" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting &nbsp;Foreign terms</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Foreign terms should be used sparingly. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Text_formatting#Foreign_terms" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting">Use italics</a> for phrases in other languages and for isolated foreign words that are not current in English. Where possible, this is best done with the <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Lang" title="Template:Lang">lang</a>}}</code> template using the appropriate <a href="/wiki/ISO_language_code" class="mw-redirect" title="ISO language code">ISO language code</a>, e.g., <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Lang" title="Template:Lang">lang</a>|es|casa}}</code>. There are alternatives to the <code>{{lang}}</code> template which also provide additional information about a foreign word or phrase, such as a link to the language name; 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference selfref">see <a href="/wiki/Category:Wikipedia_multilingual_support_templates" title="Category:Wikipedia multilingual support templates">Category:Wikipedia multilingual support templates</a></span>. The <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Lang" title="Template:Lang">lang</a>}}</code> template and related templates automatically italicize text for Latin-alphabet scripts, so do not add separate italics markup around or within them. Non-Latin-based scripts like Chinese should not be italicized, since it is already obvious the material cannot be English, and some such scripts do not support italicization. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Common_usage_in_English">Common usage in English</span></h4> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">Loanwords</a> and borrowed phrases that have common usage in English&nbsp; <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Gestapo</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">samurai</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">vice versa</span>&nbsp; do not require italics. A rule of thumb is to not italicize words that appear unitalicized in major general-purpose English-language dictionaries. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Spelling_and_romanization">Spelling and romanization</span></h4> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:ROMANIZATION"></span><span id="MOS:ROMANISATION"></span><span id="MOS:DIACRITICS"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:ROMANIZATION&amp;redirect=no">MOS:ROMANIZATION</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:ROMANISATION&amp;redirect=no">MOS:ROMANISATION</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:DIACRITICS&amp;redirect=no">MOS:DIACRITICS</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(use_English)#Modified_letters" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (use English)">Wikipedia:Naming conventions (use English) &nbsp;Modified letters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Romanization" title="Wikipedia:Romanization">Wikipedia:Romanization</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Category:Romanization" title="Category:Romanization">Category:Romanization</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Names not originally written in one of the <a href="/wiki/Latin-script_alphabets" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin-script alphabets">Latin-script alphabets</a> (written for example in Greek, Cyrillic, or Chinese scripts) must be given a <a href="/wiki/Romanization" title="Romanization">romanized</a> form for use in English. Use a systematically <a href="/wiki/Transliteration" title="Transliteration">transliterated</a> or otherwise romanized name (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Aleksandr Tymoczko</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Wang Yanhong</span>); but if there is a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Article_titles#Use_commonly_recognizable_names" title="Wikipedia:Article titles">more common</a> English form of the name (<span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Tchaikovsky</span>, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Chiang Kai-shek</span>), use that form instead. </p>
      <p>The use of <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">diacritics</a> (such as accent marks) for foreign words is neither encouraged nor discouraged; their usage depends on whether they appear in <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verifiable reliable sources</a> in English, and on the constraints imposed by specialized Wikipedia guidelines. Provide <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Redirect#Alternative_names_and_languages" title="Wikipedia:Redirect">redirects</a> from alternative forms that use or exclude diacritics. </p>
      <p>Proper names in languages which use the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabet</a> can include characters with <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">diacritics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Typographic_ligature" class="mw-redirect" title="Typographic ligature">ligatures</a>, and others that are not commonly used in present-day English. Wikipedia normally retains these special characters, except where there is a well-established English spelling that replaces them with English standard letters. Examples: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>The name of the article on Hungarian mathematician <a href="/wiki/Paul_Erd%C5%91s" title="Paul Erd?s">Paul Erd?s</a> is spelt with the <a href="/wiki/Double_acute_accent" title="Double acute accent">double acute accent</a>, and the alternative spellings <i>Paul Erdos</i> and <i>Paul Erds</i> redirect to that article.</li> 
       <li>Similarly, the name of the article on the Nordic god <a href="/wiki/%C3%86gir" title="gir">gir</a> is so spelt, with redirects from the ligature-free form <a href="/wiki/Aegir" class="mw-redirect" title="Aegir">Aegir</a> and the Swedish spelling <a href="/wiki/%C3%84gir" class="mw-redirect" title="gir">gir</a>.</li> 
       <li>However, the Spanish region named <i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">Aragn</i> in Spanish and <i lang="ca" title="Catalan-language text">Arag</i> in Catalan is given as <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">Aragon</a>, without the accent, as this is the established English name (the non-English names appear, with their diacritics, in its lead section).</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Such matters are determined on an topic-by-topic basis; <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Consensus#Levels_of_consensus" title="Wikipedia:Consensus">a small group of editors</a> cannot "prohibit" or "require" diacritics across a category of articles.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[q]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Spell a name consistently in the title and the text of an article. 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(Relevant policy: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Article_titles" title="Wikipedia:Article titles">Wikipedia:Article titles</a>; see also <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(use_English)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (use English)">Wikipedia:Naming conventions (use English)</a>.)</span> For a foreign name, phrase, or word, adopt the spelling most commonly used in English-language <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">reliable sources</a>, including but not limited to those already cited in the article.<sup id="cite_ref-GScholar_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GScholar-25">[r]</a></sup> For punctuation of compounded forms, see relevant guidelines in <a href="#Punctuation">&nbsp;Punctuation</a>. </p>
      <p>A non-English <a href="/wiki/Proper_and_common_nouns" title="Proper and common nouns">proper name</a> should generally not be italicized, unless it would be for some other reason; this is most commonly when it is the <a href="/wiki/MOS:FOREIGNTITLE" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:FOREIGNTITLE">title of a major published work</a>, as in <a href="/wiki/Les_Liaisons_dangereuses" title="Les Liaisons dangereuses"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Les Liaisons dangereuses</i></span></a>; or when it is being compared in a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Text_formatting#Words_as_words" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting">words-as-words</a> manner to another name for the same subject, e.g., <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><b>Nuremberg</b> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <i lang="de">Nrnberg</i>)</span>. When the name should not be italicized, language markup can still be used to ensure proper pronunciation in screen readers, with the <code class="nowrap" style="">|italic=unset</code> parameter: <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Lang" title="Template:Lang">lang</a>|de|italic=unset|Nrnberg}}</code>. </p>
      <p>Sometimes usage will be influenced by other guidelines, such as <a href="#National_varieties_of_English">&nbsp;National varieties of English</a>, which may lead to different choices in different articles. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_non-English_concerns">Other non-English concerns</span></h4> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Other_concerns"></span> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>For non-English vernacular names of species, see <a href="#Animals,_plants,_and_other_organisms">&nbsp;Animals, plants, and other organisms</a>.</li> 
       <li>For handling of foreign-language quotations, see <a href="#Foreign-language_quotations">&nbsp;Foreign-language quotations</a>.</li> 
       <li>For non-English characters that resemble single quotation marks and apostrophes, see <a href="#Foreign_characters_that_resemble_apostrophes">&nbsp;Foreign characters that resemble apostrophes</a>.</li> 
       <li>For actual non-English quotation characters, see <a href="#Quotation_characters">&nbsp;Quotation characters</a>.</li> 
       <li>For capitalization in foreign-language work titles, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Titles#Capitalization_in_foreign-language_titles" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Titles">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Titles &nbsp;Capitalization in foreign-language titles</a>.</li> 
       <li>For <a href="/wiki/Interlinear_gloss" title="Interlinear gloss">interlinear glosses</a> and their particular uses of small-caps (and italics and single quotes), see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Text_formatting#All_caps_and_small_caps" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting &nbsp;All caps and small caps</a>.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technical_language">Technical language<span id="JARGON"></span></span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:JARGON"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:JARGON&amp;redirect=no">MOS:JARGON</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "Wikipedia:Jargon" redirects here. For an explanation of jargon used on Wikipedia, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Glossary" title="Wikipedia:Glossary">Wikipedia:Glossary</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:What_Wikipedia_is_not#Wikipedia_is_not_a_manual,_guidebook,_textbook,_or_scientific_journal" title="Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not">Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not &nbsp;Wikipedia is not a manual, guidebook, textbook, or scientific journal</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Make_technical_articles_understandable" title="Wikipedia:Make technical articles understandable">Wikipedia:Make technical articles understandable</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Some topics are intrinsically technical, but editors should try to make them understandable to as many readers as possible. Minimize <a href="/wiki/Jargon" title="Jargon">jargon</a>, or at least explain it or tag it using <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Technical" title="Template:Technical">Technical</a>}}</code> or <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Technical-statement" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Technical-statement">Technical-statement</a>}}</code> for other editors to fix. For unavoidably technical articles, a separate introductory article (like <a href="/wiki/Introduction_to_general_relativity" title="Introduction to general relativity">Introduction to general relativity</a>) may be the best solution. Avoid excessive <i>wikilinking</i> (linking within Wikipedia) as a substitute for parenthetic explanations such as the one in this sentence. Do not introduce new and specialized words simply to teach them to the reader when more common alternatives will do. When the notions named by jargon are too complex to explain concisely in a few parenthetical words, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Make_technical_articles_understandable#Write_one_level_down" title="Wikipedia:Make technical articles understandable">write one level down</a>. For example, consider adding a brief background section with <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Main" title="Template:Main">main</a>}}</code> tags pointing to the full treatment article(s) of the prerequisite notions; this approach is practical only when the prerequisite concepts are central to the exposition of the article's main topic and when such prerequisites are not too numerous. Short articles, such as <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Stub" title="Wikipedia:Stub">stubs</a>, generally do not have such sections. </p>
      <p>
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference selfref">For italicization and other markup of introduced terms, see: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Text_formatting#Words_as_words" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting &nbsp;Words as words</a>.</span> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographical_items">Geographical items</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:GEO"></span><span id="MOS:PLACE"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:GEO&amp;redirect=no">MOS:GEO</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:PLACE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:PLACE</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-Merge_from plainlinks ombox ombox-move" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mergefrom.svg/50px-Mergefrom.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mergefrom.svg/75px-Mergefrom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mergefrom.svg/100px-Mergefrom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="50" data-file-height="20"></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">It has been suggested that <i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Capital_letters#Place_names" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters#Place names</a></i> be <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Merging" title="Wikipedia:Merging">merged</a> into this section. (<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia_talk:Manual_of_Style/Capital_letters#Irrelevant_text_in_Personal_names_and_Place_names_sections" title="Wikipedia talk:Manual of Style/Capital letters">Discuss</a>)<small><i> Proposed since April 2021.</i></small></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(geographic_names)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (geographic names)">Wikipedia:Naming conventions (geographic names)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Abbreviations#Special_considerations" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Abbreviations">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Abbreviations &nbsp;Special considerations</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Places should generally be referred to consistently by the same name as in the title of their article 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(geographic_names)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (geographic names)">Wikipedia:Naming conventions (geographic names)</a>)</span>. Exceptions are made if there is a widely accepted historical English name appropriate to the given context. In cases where such a historical name is used, it should be followed by the modern<sup id="cite_ref-recent_11-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recent-11">[f]</a></sup> name in round brackets (parentheses) on the first occurrence of the name in applicable sections of the article. This resembles linking; it should not be done to the detriment of style. On the other hand, it is probably better to provide such a variant too often than too rarely. If more than one historical name is applicable for a given context, the other names should be added after the modern English name, that is: "historical name (modern name, other historical names)". </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_files">Media files</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Creation_and_usage_of_media_files" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Creation and usage of media files">Wikipedia:Creation and usage of media files</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Images">Images</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:IM"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:IM&amp;redirect=no">MOS:IM</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Images" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Images">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Images</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Accessibility#Images" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility &nbsp;Images</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Image_use_policy" title="Wikipedia:Image use policy">Wikipedia:Image use policy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Picture_tutorial" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Picture tutorial">Wikipedia:Picture tutorial</a>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>Each image should be inside the level<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>2 section to which it relates, within the section defined by the most recent <code>==Heading==</code> delimited by two equal signs, or at the top of the lead section. Do not place images immediately above section headings.</li> 
       <li>Avoid <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Sandwich" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Sandwich">sandwiching text</a> horizontally between two images that face each other, and between an image and an infobox or similar.</li> 
       <li>It is often preferable to place images of people so they "look" toward the text. Do not achieve this by reversing the image.</li> 
       <li>Any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Picture_tutorial#Galleries" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Picture tutorial">galleries</a> should comply with <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Image_use_policy#Image_galleries" title="Wikipedia:Image use policy">Wikipedia:Image use policy &nbsp;Image galleries</a>. Consider <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Wikimedia_sister_projects#Where_to_place_links" title="Wikipedia:Wikimedia sister projects">linking to additional images on Commons</a> instead.</li> 
       <li>Avoid referring to images as being to the left, the right, above or below, because image placement varies with platform, and is meaningless to people using screen readers; instead, use captions to identify images.</li> 
       <li>An image's <code class="nowrap" style="">|alt=</code> text takes the image's place for those who are unable to see the image. See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Accessibility/Alternative_text_for_images" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility/Alternative text for images">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility/Alternative text for images</a>.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_media_files">Other media files</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Videos" title="Wikipedia:Videos">Wikipedia:Videos</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Other media files include video and audio files. Style recommendations for such files largely follow recommendations for image files (as far as applicable). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Avoid_using_images_to_convey_text"><span id="Avoid_entering_textual_information_as_images"></span>Avoid using images to convey text</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Accessibility#Text" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility &nbsp;Text</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:TEXTASIMAGES"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:TEXTASIMAGES&amp;redirect=no">MOS:TEXTASIMAGES</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>Textual information should almost always be entered as text rather than as an image. True text can be colored and adjusted with <a href="/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets" class="mw-redirect" title="Cascading Style Sheets">CSS</a> tags and templates, but text in images cannot be. Images are not searchable, are slower to download, and are unlikely to be read as text by devices for the visually impaired. Any important textual information in an image should also appear in the image's alt text, caption, or other nearby text. </p>
      <p>For entering textual information as audio, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Spoken_Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Spoken Wikipedia">Wikipedia:WikiProject Spoken Wikipedia</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Captions">Captions</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:CAPTION"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:CAPTION&amp;redirect=no">MOS:CAPTION</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Captions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Captions">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Captions</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Photographs and other graphics should have captions, unless they are unambiguous depictions of the subject of the article or when they are "self-captioning" images (such as reproductions of album or book covers). In a biography article no caption is necessary for a portrait of the subject pictured alone, but one might be used to give the year, the subject's age, or other circumstances of the portrait along with the name of the subject. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Formatting_of_captions">Formatting of captions</span></h4> 
      <ul>
       <li>Captions normally start with a capital letter.<sup id="cite_ref-Sentence_case_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sentence_case-5">[a]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Most captions are not complete sentences but merely <a href="/wiki/Sentence_fragment" class="mw-redirect" title="Sentence fragment">sentence fragments</a> which should not end with a period. However, if any complete sentence occurs in a caption, then every sentence and every sentence fragment in that caption should end with a period.</li> 
       <li>The text of captions should not be specially formatted, except in ways that would apply if it occurred in the main text (e.g., italics for the Latin name of a species).</li> 
       <li>Captions should be succinct; more information can be included on its description page, or in the main text.</li> 
       <li>Captions for technical charts and diagrams may need to be substantially longer than usual; they should fully describe all elements of the image and indicate its significance.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bulleted_and_numbered_lists">Bulleted and numbered lists</span></h2> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:LISTBULLET"></span><span id="MOS:LISTNUMBERED"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:LISTBULLET&amp;redirect=no">MOS:LISTBULLET</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:LISTNUMBERED&amp;redirect=no">MOS:LISTNUMBERED</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main pages: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Lists" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Lists">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Lists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Embedded_lists" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Embedded lists">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Embedded lists</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Help:List" title="Help:List">Help:List</a>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>Do not use lists if a passage is read easily as plain paragraphs.</li> 
       <li>Use proper wikimarkup- or template-based list code 
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Lists" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Lists">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Lists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Help:List" title="Help:List">Help:List</a>)</span>.</li> 
       <li>Do not leave blank lines between items in a bulleted or numbered list unless there is a reason to do so, since this causes the Wiki software to interpret each item as beginning a new list. 
        <ul>
         <li>Indents (such as this) are permitted if the elements are <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Embedded_lists#&quot;Children&quot;_(i.e.,_indentation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Embedded lists">"child" items</a>.</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li>Use numbers rather than bullets only if: 
        <ul>
         <li>a need to refer to the elements by number may arise;</li> 
         <li>the sequence of the items is critical; or</li> 
         <li>the numbering has some independent meaning, for example in a listing of musical tracks.</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li>Use the same grammatical form for all elements in a list, and do not mix sentences and sentence fragments as elements, for example when the elements are: 
        <ul>
         <li><b>complete sentences</b>  each one is formatted with sentence case (its first letter is capitalized) and a final period (full point);</li> 
         <li><b>sentence fragments</b>  the list is typically introduced by an introductory fragment ending with a colon;</li> 
         <li><b>titles of works</b>  they retain the original capitalization of the titles;</li> 
         <li><b>other elements</b>  they are formatted consistently in either sentence case or lower case.</li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Links">Links</span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wikilinks">Wikilinks</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Linking" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Linking">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Linking</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Help:Link" title="Help:Link">Help:Link</a>
      </div> 
      <p><b>Make <a href="/wiki/Help:Link" title="Help:Link">links</a> only where they are relevant and helpful in the context</b>: Excessive use of hyperlinks can be distracting and may slow the reader down. Redundant links (like the one in <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">the tallest people on <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a></span>) clutter the page and make future maintenance harder. High-value links that <em>are</em> worth pursuing should stand out clearly. </p>
      <p><b>Linking to sections</b>: A hash sign&nbsp;(<code>#</code>) followed by the appropriate heading will lead to a relevant part of a page. For example, <code>[[Apostrophe#Use in non-English names]]</code> links to a particular section of the article <a href="/wiki/Apostrophe" title="Apostrophe">Apostrophe</a>. </p>
      <p><b>Initial capitalization</b>: Wikipedia's <a href="/wiki/MediaWiki" title="MediaWiki">MediaWiki</a> software does not require that wikilinks begin with an upper-case character. Capitalize the first letter only where this is naturally called for, or when specifically referring to the linked article by its name: <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><a href="/wiki/Snake" title="Snake">Snakes</a> are often <a href="/wiki/Venomous" class="mw-redirect" title="Venomous">venomous</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Lizard" title="Lizard">lizards</a> only rarely 
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="/wiki/Poison" title="Poison">Poison</a>)</span>.</span> </p>
      <p><b>Check links</b>: Ensure the destination is the intended one; many dictionary words lead to disambiguation pages and not to complete or well-chosen articles. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="External_links">External links</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:External_links" title="Wikipedia:External links">Wikipedia:External links</a>
      </div> 
      <p>External links should not normally be used in the body of an article. Instead, articles can include an <i>External links</i> section at the end, pointing to further information outside Wikipedia as distinct from citing sources. The standard format is a primary heading, <code>==External links==</code>, followed by a bulleted list of links. Identify the link and briefly indicate its relevance to the article. For example: </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996643573">
      <div class="block-indent">
       <div class="plainlist"> 
        <ul>
         <li><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-tid mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><span class="k">*</span> [<span class="na">https://history.nih.gov/exhibits/history/index.html</span> History of NIH]</code></li> 
         <li><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-tid mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><span class="k">*</span> [<span class="na">https://nih.gov/</span> National Institutes of Health homepage]</code></li>
        </ul> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>These will appear as: </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996643573">
      <div class="block-indent"> 
       <ul>
        <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://history.nih.gov/exhibits/history/index.html">History of NIH</a></li> 
        <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://nih.gov/">National Institutes of Health homepage</a></li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <p>Where appropriate, use <a href="/wiki/Category:External_link_templates" title="Category:External link templates">external link templates</a> such as <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Official_website" title="Template:Official website">Official website</a>}}</code> and <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:URL" title="Template:URL">URL</a>}}</code>. </p>
      <p>Add external links with discretion; Wikipedia is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTLINK" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTLINK">not a link repository</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Miscellaneous">Miscellaneous</span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Keep_markup_simple">Keep markup simple</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:MARKUP"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:MARKUP&amp;redirect=no">MOS:MARKUP</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>Other things being equal, keep <a href="/wiki/Help:Wiki_markup" class="mw-redirect" title="Help:Wiki markup">markup</a> simple. This makes wikitext easier to understand and edit, and the results seen by the reader more predictable. Use HTML and CSS markup sparingly. </p>
      <p>In general, wikitext formatting is considered easier to use than HTML and wikitext is preferred if there are equivalents; see <a href="/wiki/Help:HTML_in_wikitext" title="Help:HTML in wikitext">Help:HTML in wikitext</a>. <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:HTML_5#Obsolete_elements_and_attributes" title="Wikipedia:HTML 5">Obsolete elements and attributes</a> should be updated or removed. There are many templates that allow HTML markup to be used without putting it in articles directly, such as {{<a href="/wiki/Template:Em" title="Template:Em">em</a>}} (see <a href="/wiki/MOS:EMPHASIS" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:EMPHASIS">MOS:EMPHASIS</a>) and {{<a href="/wiki/Template:Strong" title="Template:Strong">strong</a>}} (see <a href="/wiki/MOS:BOLD" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS:BOLD">MOS:BOLD</a>). </p>
      <p>An <a href="/wiki/Character_entity_reference" class="mw-redirect" title="Character entity reference">HTML character entity</a> is sometimes better than the equivalent Unicode character, which may be difficult to identify in edit mode; for example, <code>&amp;Alpha;</code> is explicit whereas <code>?</code> (the upper-case form of Greek <code>?</code>) may be misidentified as the Latin <code>A</code>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formatting_issues">Formatting issues</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Text_formatting" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Modifications in font size, blank space, and color 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see <a href="#Color_coding">&nbsp;Color coding</a>)</span> are an issue for the Wikipedia site-wide <a href="/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets" class="mw-redirect" title="Cascading Style Sheets">style sheet</a> and should be reserved for special cases only. </p>
      <p>Typically, the use of custom font styles will: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>reduce consistency, since the text will no longer look uniform;</li> 
       <li>reduce usability, since it might be impossible for people with custom style sheets (for accessibility reasons, for example) to override it, and it might clash with a different <a href="/wiki/Skin_(computing)" title="Skin (computing)">skin</a> or inconvenience people with color blindness 
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(see below)</span>; and</li> 
       <li>cause disputes, since other editors may disagree aesthetically with the choice of style.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Specify font sizes <em>relatively</em> (for example with <code>font-size: 85%</code>) rather than <em>absolutely</em> (like <code>font-size: 8pt</code>). The resulting font size of any text should not drop below 85% of the page's default font size. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Color_coding">Color coding</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Accessibility#Color" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility &nbsp;Color</a>
      </div>
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:COLORCODING"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:COLORCODING&amp;redirect=no">MOS:COLORCODING</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>Do not use color <em>alone</em> to mark differences in text: they may be invisible to people with <a href="/wiki/Color_blindness" title="Color blindness">color blindness</a> and useless in black-and-white printouts or displays. </p>
      <p>Choose colors that are distinguishable by readers with the most common form of colorblindness, such as <a href="/wiki/Maroon_(color)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maroon (color)"><span style="background: white; color: maroon">maroon</span></a> and <a href="/wiki/Teal" title="Teal"><span style="background: white; color: teal">teal</span></a>, and <em>additionally</em> mark the differences with change of font or some other means (<a href="/wiki/Maroon_(color)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maroon (color)"><span style="background: white; font-family: Georgia, serif; color: maroon; font face: Times New Roman">maroon and alternative font face</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Teal" title="Teal"><span style="background: white; color: teal">teal</span></a>). Avoid low contrast between text and background colors. See also <a href="/wiki/Color_coding" class="mw-redirect" title="Color coding">color coding</a>. </p>
      <p>Even for readers with unimpaired color vision, excessive background shading of table entries impedes readability and recognition of Wikilinks. Background color should be used only as a <em>supplementary</em> visual cue and should be subtle (consider using lighter, less-dominant <a href="/wiki/Pastel_(color)" title="Pastel (color)">pastel</a> hues) rather than glaring. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Indentation">Indentation</span></h4> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="INDENT"></span><span class="anchor" id="Indent"></span><span class="anchor" id="indenting"></span>
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855"></p>
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:INDENT"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:INDENT&amp;redirect=no">MOS:INDENT</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Accessibility#Indentation" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility &nbsp;Indentation</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Do not abuse block quotation markup to indent non-quotations. Various templates are available for indentation, including <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Block_indent" title="Template:Block indent">block indent</a>}}</code> and (for inline use) <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:In5" title="Template:In5">in5</a>}}</code>. </p>
      <p>Avoid <code>:</code> (<a href="/wiki/Description_list" class="mw-redirect" title="Description list">description list</a> markup) for simple visual indentation in articles (common as it may be on talk pages). It causes accessibility problems and outputs invalid HTML. 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Accessibility#Indentation" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility &nbsp;Indentation</a> for alternatives.</span> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controlling_line_breaks"><span id="Non-breaking_spaces"></span>Controlling line breaks</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:NBSP"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:NBSP&amp;redirect=no">MOS:NBSP</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Help:Line-break_handling" title="Help:Line-break handling">Help:Line-break handling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Template:Spaces" title="Template:Spaces">Template:Spaces</a>
      </div> 
      <p>It is sometimes desirable to force a text segment to appear entirely on a single line??that is, to prevent a line break (line wrap) from occurring anywhere within it. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>A <b><a href="/wiki/Non-breaking_space" title="Non-breaking space">non-breaking space</a></b> (or <b>hard space</b>) will never be used as a line-break point. Markup: for <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">19<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>kg</span>, code <code>19&amp;nbsp;kg</code> <em>or</em> <code>19{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nbsp" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nbsp">nbsp</a>}}kg</code>.</li> 
       <li>Or use <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nowrap" title="Template:Nowrap">nowrap</a>}}</code>, <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nobreak" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nobreak">nobreak</a>}}</code>, or <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nobr" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nobr">nobr</a>}}</code> (all equivalent). Markup: for <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><span class="nowrap">5 24? N</span></span> code <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nobr" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nobr">nobr</a>|5 24? N}}</code>.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>It is desirable to prevent line breaks where breaking across lines might be confusing or awkward. For example: </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716">
      <div class="div-col" style="column-width: 15em;"> 
       <ul>
        <li><code>17{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nbsp" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nbsp">nbsp</a>}}kg</code></li> 
        <li><code>AD{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nbsp" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nbsp">nbsp</a>}}565</code></li> 
        <li><code>2:50{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nbsp" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nbsp">nbsp</a>}}pm</code></li> 
        <li><code>11{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nbsp" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nbsp">nbsp</a>}}billion</code></li> 
        <li><code>May{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nbsp" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nbsp">nbsp</a>}}2014</code></li> 
        <li><code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nobr" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nobr">nobr</a>|5 24? 21? N}}</code></li> 
        <li><code>Boeing{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nbsp" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nbsp">nbsp</a>}}747</code></li> 
        <li><code>123{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nbsp" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nbsp">nbsp</a>}}Elm Street</code></li> 
        <li><code>World War{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nbsp" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nbsp">nbsp</a>}}II</code></li> 
        <li><code>Pope Paul{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nbsp" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nbsp">nbsp</a>}}VI</code></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>Whether a non-breaking space is appropriate depends on context: whereas it is appropriate to use <code>12{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nbsp" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nbsp">nbsp</a>}}MB</code> in prose, it may be counterproductive in a table (where an unattractive break may be acceptable to conserve precious horizontal space) and unnecessary in a short parameter value in an infobox (where a break would never occur anyway). </p>
      <p>A line break may occur at a <b>thin space</b> (<code>&amp;thinsp;</code>, or <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Thinsp" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Thinsp">thinsp</a>}}</code>), which is sometimes used to correct too-close placement of adjacent characters. To prevent this, consider using <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nobr" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nobr">nobr</a>}}</code>. </p>
      <p>Insert non-breaking and thin spaces as <a href="/wiki/Named_character_reference" class="mw-redirect" title="Named character reference">named character reference</a> (<code>&amp;nbsp;</code> or <code>&amp;thinsp;</code>), or as templates that generate these (<code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nbsp" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nbsp">nbsp</a>}}</code>, <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Thinsp" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Thinsp">thinsp</a>}}</code>), and never by entering them directly into the edit window from the keyboard&nbsp; they are visually indistinguishable from regular spaces, and later editors will be unable to see what they are. Inside wikilinks, a construction such as <span class="nowrap"><code>[[World War&amp;nbsp;II]]</code></span> works but <span class="nowrap"><code>[[World War{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Nbsp" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Nbsp">nbsp</a>}}II]]</code></span> doesn't. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scrolling_lists_and_collapsible_content">Scrolling lists and collapsible content</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="WP:DONTHIDE"></span><span id="MOS:SCROLL"></span><span id="MOS:COLLAPSE"></span><span id="MOS:DONTHIDE"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcuts</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikipedia:DONTHIDE&amp;redirect=no">WP:DONTHIDE</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:SCROLL&amp;redirect=no">MOS:SCROLL</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:COLLAPSE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:COLLAPSE</a></span></li>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:DONTHIDE&amp;redirect=no">MOS:DONTHIDE</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "WP:COLLAPSE" redirects here. For the guideline on collapsing off-topic talk page discussions, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:TALKOFFTOPIC" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:TALKOFFTOPIC">WP:TALKOFFTOPIC</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Accessibility#Users_with_limited_CSS_or_JavaScript_support" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility &nbsp;Users with limited CSS or JavaScript support</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Help:Scrolling_list" title="Help:Scrolling list">Scrolling lists</a>, and collapsible templates that toggle text display between <i>hide</i> and <i>show</i>, can interfere with readers' ability to access our content. Such mechanisms are <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Spoiler" title="Wikipedia:Spoiler">not to be used to conceal "spoiler" information</a>. Templates are <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Template_namespace#Guidelines" title="Wikipedia:Template namespace">not normally used to store article text</a> at all, as it interferes with editors' ability to find and edit it. </p>
      <p>When such features are used, take care that the content will still be <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Accessibility#Users_with_limited_CSS_or_JavaScript_support" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Accessibility">accessible on devices that do not support JavaScript or CSS</a>, and to the greater than 60% of Wikipedia readers who use the <a href="/wiki/Help:Mobile_access" title="Help:Mobile access">mobile version of the site</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[s]</a></sup> which has a limited set of features. Mobile ability to access the content in question is easy to test with the "Mobile view" link at the bottom of each page.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[t]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><strong>Collapsible templates should not conceal article content by default upon page loading.</strong> This includes <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Footnotes" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">reference lists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Tables" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Tables">tables</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Embedded_lists" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Embedded lists">lists</a> of article content, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Image_use_policy#Image_galleries" title="Wikipedia:Image use policy">image galleries</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Captions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Captions">image captions</a>. In particular, while some templates support a <code>collapsible</code> parameter or manually-added CSS class, and this is permissible, the <code>collapsed</code>, <code>mw-collapsed</code>, and <code>autocollapse</code> states <em>should not be used in articles</em> to pre-emptively force the closure of these elements, except as noted below. Any information hidden in this way when the page loads will be irreversibly invisible to the aforementioned classes of users, as well as a growing number of low-bandwidth users in Asia who reach a Wikipedia article via Google.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[u]</a></sup> Several other CSS classes, used manually or by templates, will render content inaccessible to mobile users.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[v]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Collapsed or auto-collapsing <i>cells</i> or <i>sections</i> may be used with tables if it simply repeats information covered in the main text (or is purely supplementary, e.g., several past years of statistics in collapsed tables for comparison with a table of uncollapsed current stats). Auto-collapsing is often a feature of <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Categories,_lists,_and_navigation_templates#Navigation_templates" title="Wikipedia:Categories, lists, and navigation templates">navboxes</a>. A few <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Infobox" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Infobox">infoboxes</a> also use pre-collapsed sections for infrequently accessed details. If information in a list, infobox, or other non-navigational content seems extraneous or trivial enough to inspire pre-collapsing it, consider raising a discussion on the article (or template) talk page about whether it should be <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:What_Wikipedia_is_not#Wikipedia_is_not_an_indiscriminate_collection_of_information" title="Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not">included at all</a>. If the information is important and the concern is article density or length, consider <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Layout#Body_sections" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Layout">dividing the article into more sections</a>, integrating <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Trivia_sections" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Trivia sections">unnecessarily list-formatted information</a> into the article prose, or <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Summary_style" title="Wikipedia:Summary style">splitting the article</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Invisible_comments">Invisible comments</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:COMMENT"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:COMMENT&amp;redirect=no">MOS:COMMENT</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "WP:COMMENT" redirects here. For the expression of personal opinions in articles, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:What_Wikipedia_is_not#Wikipedia_is_not_a_publisher_of_original_thought" title="Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not">Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not &nbsp;Wikipedia is not a publisher of original thought</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For invisible control characters, see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Text_formatting#Private_Use_Area_and_invisible_formatting_characters" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Text formatting &nbsp;Private Use Area and invisible formatting characters</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Hidden_text" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Hidden text">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Hidden text</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Editors use "invisible" comments&nbsp; not shown in the rendered page seen by readers of the article, but visible in the wiki source when an editor opens the article for editing&nbsp; to communicate with one another. </p>
      <p>Invisible comments are useful for alerting other editors to issues such as common mistakes that regularly occur in the article, a section title's being the target of an incoming link, or pointing to a discussion that established a consensus relating to the article. They should not be used to instruct other editors not to perform certain edits, although where existing local consensus is against making such an edit, they may usefully draw the editor's attention to that. Avoid adding too many invisible comments because they can clutter the wiki source for other editors. Check that your invisible comment does not change the formatting, for example by introducing unwanted white space in the rendered page. </p>
      <p>To leave an invisible comment, enclose the text you intend to be read only by editors between <code>&lt;!--</code> and <code>--&gt;</code>. For example: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><code class="wrap" style="">&lt;!--&nbsp;If you change this section title, also change the links to it on the pages ....&nbsp;--&gt;</code></li> 
       <li><code class="wrap" style="">&lt;!--&nbsp;When adding table entries, remember to update the total given in the text.&nbsp;--&gt;</code></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>This notation can be inserted with a single click in <a href="/wiki/Help:Wiki_markup" class="mw-redirect" title="Help:Wiki markup">wiki markup</a>, just under the edit pane in edit mode. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pronunciation">Pronunciation</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Pronunciation" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Pronunciation">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Pronunciation</a>
      </div> 
      <p><b>Pronunciation</b> in Wikipedia is indicated in the <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">International Phonetic Alphabet</a> (IPA). In most situations, for ease of understanding by the majority of readers and across variants of the language, <a href="/wiki/Phonetic_transcription#Narrow_versus_broad_transcription" title="Phonetic transcription">quite broad</a> IPA transcriptions are best for English pronunciations. See <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">Help:IPA/English</a> and <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">Help:IPA</a> (general) for keys, and <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:IPA" title="Template:IPA">IPA</a>}}</code> for templates that link to these keys. For English pronunciations, <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key">pronunciation respellings</a> may be used <em>in addition to</em> the IPA. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Editing_policy" title="Wikipedia:Editing policy">Editing policy</a>  explains Wikipedia's general philosophy of editing</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:What_Wikipedia_is_not#Wikipedia_is_not_a_manual,_guidebook,_textbook,_or_scientific_journal" title="Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not">Wikipedia is not a manual, guidebook, textbook, or scientific journal</a>&nbsp; we write for a general, not technical, readership as much as we can</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_the_Manual_of_Style" class="mw-redirect" title="Help:Introduction to the Manual of Style">Manual of Style tutorial</a>&nbsp; a quick introduction to the style guide for articles</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_the_Manual_of_Style/Manual_of_Style_quiz" title="Help:Introduction to the Manual of Style/Manual of Style quiz">Manual of Style quiz</a>&nbsp; test your Manual of Style knowledge</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Styletips" title="Wikipedia:Styletips">Styletips</a>  a list of advice for editors on writing style and formatting</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Contents" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Contents">Manual of Style Contents</a>  guidelines for film, novels, biographies, military history, etc.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_and_using_style_guides" title="Wikipedia:Identifying and using style guides">Identifying and using style guides</a>&nbsp; an essay providing a summary of off-site style guides' influences on MoS and their uses as sources in Wikipedia articles</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:If_MOS_doesn%27t_need_a_rule_on_something,_then_it_needs_to_not_have_a_rule_on_that_thing" title="Wikipedia:If MOS doesn't need a rule on something, then it needs to not have a rule on that thing">Wikipedia:If MOS doesn't need a rule on something, then it needs to not have a rule on that thing</a>&nbsp; Resisting MOSBLOAT.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guidance">Guidance</span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Annotated_article" title="Wikipedia:Annotated article">Annotated article</a>  is a well-constructed sample article, with annotations</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:DEVELOP" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:DEVELOP">Article development</a>  lists the ways in which you can help an article grow 
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Basic_copyediting" title="Wikipedia:Basic copyediting">Basic copyediting</a>  gives helpful advice on copy-editing</li> 
         <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles">Better articles</a>  guidance on how to make articles better</li> 
         <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:The_perfect_article" title="Wikipedia:The perfect article">Perfect article</a>  point-by-point guidance on what makes a great article</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoiding_common_mistakes" title="Wikipedia:Avoiding common mistakes">Avoiding common mistakes</a>  gives a list of common mistakes and how to avoid them</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Be_bold" title="Wikipedia:Be bold">Be bold</a>  suggests a bold attitude toward page updates</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">Citing sources</a>  explains process and standards for citing references</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Help:Editing" title="Help:Editing">Editing</a>  is a short primer on editing pages</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Style_guide" title="Style guide">Style guide</a>  contains links to the style guides of some magazines and newspapers</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Help:Wiki_markup" class="mw-redirect" title="Help:Wiki markup">Wiki markup</a>  explains the codes and resources available for editing a page</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:In_versus_of" title="Wikipedia:In versus of">Wikipedia:<i>In</i> versus <i>of</i></a>  a supplement on prepositions</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tools">Tools</span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/User_talk:GregU/dashes.js" class="mw-redirect" title="User talk:GregU/dashes.js">User:GregU's dashes script</a>  a script that will fix dashes in articles in accordance with MOS:DASH</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/User:Ohconfucius/script/MOSNUM_dates" title="User:Ohconfucius/script/MOSNUM dates">User:Ohconfucius MOSDATE script</a>  a script that will unify dates in articles in accordance with MOS:DATEFORMAT</li>
      </ul>
