      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guidelines_within_the_Manual_of_Style">Guidelines within the Manual of Style</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For the major parts of the Manual of Style, see the sidebar at top right of this page (visible only in desktop view, not in <a class="external text" href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style">mobile view</a>)
      </div> 
      <p>(Links to policy and guidelines on specific questions) </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Names">Names</span></h4> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1007196855">
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="MOS:ORGNAME"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MOS:ORGNAME&amp;redirect=no">MOS:ORGNAME</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>Proper names: 
        <ul>
         <li>Generally (dedicated MOS page): <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Proper_names" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Proper names">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Proper names</a></li> 
         <li>Place names: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Proper_names#Place_names" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Proper names">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Proper names &nbsp;Place names</a></li> 
         <li>Diacritical marks in names: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Proper_names#Diacritics" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Proper names">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Proper names &nbsp;Diacritics</a></li> 
         <li>Peoples and languages that share the same name: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Proper_names#Peoples_and_their_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Proper names">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Proper names &nbsp;Peoples and their languages</a></li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li>Naming and identifying individuals and peoples: 
        <ul>
         <li>Generally: <a href="#Identity">&nbsp;Identity</a></li> 
         <li>Specifically (for individuals): <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Biographies#Names" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Biographies">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Biographies &nbsp;Names</a></li> 
         <li>Opening paragraph of biographies: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Biographies#Opening_paragraph" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Biographies">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Biographies &nbsp;Opening paragraph</a></li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li>Names of organizations: 
        <ul>
         <li>Generally (has application beyond the topic guideline in which it is currently located): <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Cue_sports#Respect_for_official_organization_names" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Cue sports">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Cue sports &nbsp;Respect for official organization names</a></li> 
         <li>Names that are also trademarks (dedicated MOS page): <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Trademarks" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Trademarks">Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Trademarks</a></li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li>Names of animal and plant species, etc. (in article titles): <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(fauna)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (fauna)">Wikipedia:Naming conventions (fauna)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(flora)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (flora)">Wikipedia:Naming conventions (flora)</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style>
      <div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-Sentence_case-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Sentence_case_5-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Sentence_case_5-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Sentence_case_5-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Sentence_case_5-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Wikipedia uses <a href="/wiki/Sentence_case" class="mw-redirect" title="Sentence case">sentence case</a> for sentences, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Article_titles" title="Wikipedia:Article titles">article titles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Layout" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Layout">section titles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Tables" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Tables">table headers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Images" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Images">image captions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Lists" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Lists">list entries</a> (in most cases), and entries in <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Infobox" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Infobox">infoboxes</a> and similar templates, among other things. Any MoS guidance about the start of a sentence applies to items using sentence case.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Phrases such as <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">In early life</span> are acceptable (though not required) as section headings. They are also used frequently as part of longer article titles <a href="/wiki/Piracy_in_the_Caribbean" title="Piracy in the Caribbean"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Piracy in the Caribbean</span></a>, especially when a shorter construction (<span class="example example-neutral" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: initial;">Caribbean piracy</span>) may have ambiguity issues.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-curlyq-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-curlyq_7-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-curlyq_7-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-curlyq_7-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Curly quotation marks and apostrophes are deprecated on the English Wikipedia because: 
           <ul>
            <li><b>Consistency keeps searches predictable.</b> Though most browsers treat curly and straight quotation marks interchangeably, Internet Explorer does not (as of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Manual_of_Style&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>), so a search for <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Alzheimer's disease</span> will fail to find <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Alzheimers disease</span> and vice versa.</li> 
            <li><b>Straight quotation marks and apostrophes</b> are easier to type reliably on most platforms.</li>
           </ul> </span></li> 
         <li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The top-level heading is used only in the auto-generated page title.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A comment outside the <code>==&nbsp;==</code> but on the same line may cause the section-editing link to fail to appear at all; in other browsers, it may appear, but using it will cause the section heading to not automatically be added to the edit summary.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-recent-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-recent_11-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-recent_11-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-recent_11-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-recent_11-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-recent_11-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-recent_11-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-recent_11-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">In MoS's own wording, "recent", "current", "modern", and "contemporary" in reference to sources and usage should usually be interpreted as referring to reliable material published within the last forty years or so. In the consideration of name changes of persons and organizations, focus on sources from the last few years. For broader English-language usage matters, about forty years is typical. While style guides with fewer than five years in print have not been in publication long enough to have had as much real-world impact as those from around 20002015 (on which MoS is primarily based), the corpora used for <a href="/wiki/Google_ngrams" class="mw-redirect" title="Google ngrams">Google <var style="padding-right: 1px;">n</var>grams</a> are updated through 2019, and we frequently <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Search_engine_test#Some_search_engine_tests" title="Wikipedia:Search engine test">rely on</a> what they indicate from the late 20th century and onward.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-eponyms-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-eponyms_12-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">There are some rare additional exceptions to capitalization of eponyms, in which a term has been strongly conventionalized in lower-case, i.e., is preferred that way in a majority of major English-language dictionaries. For example, <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">parkinsonian</span> describes a patient exhibiting symptoms of <a href="/wiki/Parkinson%27s_disease" title="Parkinson's disease"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Parkinson's disease</span></a>. Linguistics/orthography use of the terms <a href="/w/index.php?title=Linguistic_latinisation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Linguistic latinisation (page does not exist)"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">latinize</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Romanisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanisation"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">romanize</span></a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anglicization" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglicization"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">anglicize</span></a> <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Capital_letters#Anglo-_and_similar_prefixes" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Capital letters">are increasingly lower-case</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Italic_type" title="Italic type"><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">italic[s]</span></a> in typography always is.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-Standardized_breeds-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Standardized_breeds_13-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Breeds guideline added per a <span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=&amp;diff=prev&amp;oldid=881140543#RfC_on_capitalization_of_the_names_of_standardized_breeds">December 2018 RfC</a></span>. "Standardized breed" doesn't have a perfectly clear meaning, but does encompass any breed subject to the <a href="/wiki/Breed_standard" title="Breed standard">breed standard</a> or <a href="/wiki/Studbook" class="mw-redirect" title="Studbook">studbook</a> of a notable breeder/fancier organization. Various other groupings of domesticated animals are not standardized breeds: ancient historical varieties, breed groups, feral populations, landraces, and <a href="/wiki/Crossbreed" title="Crossbreed">crossbreeds</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_(biology)" title="Hybrid (biology)">hybrids</a> that no major organizations recognize as breeds. Many often are not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Notability" title="Wikipedia:Notability">notable</a> anyway.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Quoted text" for typographic conformity and many other purposes includes titles of works, names of organizations, and other strings that are, in essence, quoted. Example: things like "Mexican-American War" are routinely corrected to "MexicanAmerican War" on Wikipedia, including in titles of cited sources. This has no effect on searching for the works we have cited, since all major search engines disregard punctuation marks.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Double quotation marks are preferred to single because: 
           <ul>
            <li>They are immediately distinguishable from apostrophes: 
             <ul>
              <li><span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">She wrote that 'Cleanthes' differs from the others', but neither opinion may represent Hume's'</span> (slows the reader down).</li> 
              <li><span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">She wrote that "Cleanthes' differs from the others', but neither opinion may represent Hume's"</span> (clearer).</li>
             </ul></li> 
            <li>Most browsers distinguish single and double quotation marks. Searches for <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">"must see" attractions</span> may fail to find <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">'must see' attractions</span>.</li>
           </ul> </span></li> 
         <li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Series title italicized" is using <i>series</i> to mean the entire show as a whole. A season (also called a <i>series</i> in British English) with its own title uses quotation marks for that title, as a sub-work.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Specifically, compound <a href="/wiki/Attributive" class="mw-redirect" title="Attributive">attributives</a>, which are modifiers of a noun that occur within the <a href="/wiki/Noun_phrase" title="Noun phrase">noun phrase</a>. 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1015928993"><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference">(See <a href="/wiki/English_compound#Hyphenated_compound_modifiers" title="English compound">English compound &nbsp;Hyphenated compound modifiers</a>.)</span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It is not logically possible to have a "<span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">1235 victory</span>", except in a game where a lower score is better. Otherwise, use a construction like <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Clovis beat Portales, 3512</span>, or <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Jameson lost the election, 2345 votes to 6789, to Garcia</span>, with parties, result, and number order in logical agreement.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-hairspace-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-hairspace_21-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/Hair_space" class="mw-redirect" title="Hair space">hair space</a> should be done as <span class="example monospaced example-mono" style="font-family: monospace, monospace; color: #006400;">{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Hair_space" title="Template:Hair space">hair space</a>}}</span> because the actual Unicode character (?) is almost invisible, the meaning of the numerical HTML entity (<span class="example deprecated-content example-bad monospaced example-mono" style="font-family: monospace, monospace; color: #8B0000;">&amp;#8202;</span>) is a bit obscure, and the named HTML entity "<span class="example deprecated-content example-bad monospaced example-mono" style="font-family: monospace, monospace; color: #8B0000;">&amp;hairsp;</span>" is not standard and not supported in many browsers.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;ref&gt;...&lt;/ref&gt;</code> tag can be spaced apart from the preceding content by a <a href="/wiki/Hair_space" class="mw-redirect" title="Hair space">hair space</a> in the unusual case that the results of not spacing could be visually confusing, such as when a citation immediately follows an exponent.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-passive-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-passive_23-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-passive_23-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="anchor" id="passive"></span><span class="anchor" id="Passive"></span><span class="anchor" id="PASSIVE"></span>The <a href="/wiki/English_passive_voice" title="English passive voice">passive voice</a> is often advised against in many forms of writing, but is used frequently in encyclopedic material, where its careful use avoids inappropriate first- and second-person constructions, as well as tone problems. Passive voice should still be avoided when it is not needed; write <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">Germany invaded Poland in 1939</span>, not <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Poland was invaded by Germany in 1939</span>. The most common uses of encyclopedic passive are to keep the focus on the subject instead of performing a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:What_Wikipedia_is_not#Wikipedia_is_not_news" title="Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not">news-style</a> shift to dwelling on a non-notable party; and to avoid leaping to certain-sounding conclusions from uncertain facts. Contrast <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">The break-in was reported to police the next morning</span>, versus <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">Assistant manager Peggy Plimpton-Chan reported the break-in to police the next morning</span>. Compare also <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;">There were no witnesses, but O'Neil was convicted of shooting the guard, and Sklarov of driving the getaway car</span>, and <span class="example deprecated-content example-bad" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #8B0000;">There were no witnesses, but O'Neil shot the guard, and Sklarov drove the getaway car</span>.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-24">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See: near-unanimous <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=User_talk:MakeSense64/Tennis_names&amp;oldid=496631631#RfC:_Can_a_wikiproject_require_no-diacritics_names,_based_on_an_organisation's_rule_or_commonness_in_English_press?">RfC</a>; repeated deletion at <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Miscellany_for_deletion" title="Wikipedia:Miscellany for deletion">Wikipedia:Miscellany for deletion</a> of an anti-diacritics "wikiproject", <a class="external autonumber" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikipedia:Miscellany_for_deletion/Wikipedia:Wikiproject_English&amp;oldid=664830645">[1]</a>; the policy <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Consensus#Levels_of_consensus" title="Wikipedia:Consensus">Wikipedia:Consensus &nbsp;Levels of consensus</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Arbitration_Committee" title="Wikipedia:Arbitration Committee">Wikipedia:Arbitration Committee</a>'s standardized <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Arbitration/Index/Principles_2#Levels_of_consensus" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Arbitration/Index/Principles 2"><i>statements of principles</i> on such matters</a>.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-GScholar-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-GScholar_25-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Reputable English-language encyclopedias and dictionaries in the aggregate are often helpful in <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(geographic_names)#Widely_accepted_name" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (geographic names)">determining the most widely accepted spelling</a> of a place name, loanwords, etc. It may also help (<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Google_test" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Google test">within limits</a>) to compare search results from the <a href="/wiki/Google_Scholar" title="Google Scholar">Google Scholar</a> journal index, for topics likely to be covered in peer-reviewed academic papers.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-26">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See <a href="/wiki/Template:Navbox_visibility" title="Template:Navbox visibility">Template:Navbox visibility</a>.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-27">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The "Mobile sidebar preview" tool near the bottom of <a href="/wiki/Special:Preferences#mw-prefsection-gadgets" title="Special:Preferences">Special:Preferences#mw-prefsection-gadgets</a> permits live preview. The "Mobile view" page-bottom feature shows the article only as it currently exists; if using that, and considering a change that could have mobile accessibility implications, please save the change first in a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:User_pages#Subpages" title="Wikipedia:User pages">user sandbox</a> and test the mobile version of that. A page's mobile version can also be accessed by changing the <code>en.wikipedia.org</code> in the address bar to <code>en.m.wikipedia.org</code> and loading that version of the URL. Note also that viewing the normal "desktop" version of the website on a mobile device is not viewing the <em>mobile version</em> of the site, though (depending on mobile browser and what transcoding it is doing) this may be a worthwhile test for some broader accessibility matters, especially on tablets, which do not always use the mobile version of Wikipedia.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-29">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As noted, CSS and JavaScript support are required to operate the show/hide toggle. Moreover, hidden content is not available in the mobile version of Wikipedia even on devices that have that support, because the mobile version's servers strip that content out before sending the page. In 2016, Google launched a Google User Content service that, like the earlier Google Lite and Google Web Transcoder, strips hidden material from pages when they are accessed through Google searches, before content is delivered to users with slow connections. The service has already been deployed in India (where English is a major language) and Indonesia, with additional national markets planned for 2016 and forward. These services also completely strip out navboxes.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[8]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-30">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Applying, or using a template that applies, any of the following CSS classes will cause the affected content to be inaccessible to mobile users, and this list may not be exhaustive: <code>navbox</code>, <code>mbox-image</code>, <code>vertical-navbox</code>, <code>nomobile</code> are from <code><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://github.com/wikimedia/operations-mediawiki-config/blob/master/wmf-config/InitialiseSettings.php#L17056">wgMFRemovableClasses</a></code>. No top icons are displayed, so <code>topicon</code> is missing.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1011085734">
      <div class="reflist"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-CONLEVEL-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-CONLEVEL_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This is a matter of policy at <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Consensus#Level_of_consensus" title="Wikipedia:Consensus">Wikipedia:Consensus &nbsp;Level of consensus</a>: "Consensus among a limited group of editors, at one place and time, cannot override community consensus on a wider scale. For instance, unless they can convince the broader community that such action is right, participants in a wikiproject cannot decide that a Wikipedia policy or guideline does not apply to articles within its scope." And: "Wikipedia has a higher standard of participation and consensus for changes to policies and guidelines than to other types of pages." Subordinate pages include <a href="/wiki/Category:Wikipedia_Manual_of_Style" title="Category:Wikipedia Manual of Style">MoS detail pages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Council/Guide#Advice_pages" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Council/Guide">style essays</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Simplified_Manual_of_Style" title="Wikipedia:Simplified Manual of Style">Simplified Manual of Style</a>.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-ew-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-ew_2-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ew_2-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">These matters have been addressed in rulings of <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Arbitration_Committee" title="Wikipedia:Arbitration Committee">ArbCom</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Requests_for_arbitration/Jguk#Optional_styles" title="Wikipedia:Requests for arbitration/Jguk">2005</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Requests_for_arbitration/Sortan#Preferred_styles" title="Wikipedia:Requests for arbitration/Sortan">2006</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Requests_for_arbitration/Date_delinking#Optional_styles" title="Wikipedia:Requests for arbitration/Date delinking">2009</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Arbitration/Requests/Case/Infoboxes#Use_of_infoboxes" title="Wikipedia:Arbitration/Requests/Case/Infoboxes">2015</a>.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-ArbCom-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-ArbCom_3-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Arbitration_Committee" title="Wikipedia:Arbitration Committee">ArbCom</a> decisions in <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Requests_for_arbitration/Jguk#Principles" title="Wikipedia:Requests for arbitration/Jguk">June 2005</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Requests_for_arbitration/jguk_2#Principles" title="Wikipedia:Requests for arbitration/jguk 2">November 2005</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Requests_for_arbitration/Sortan#Principles" title="Wikipedia:Requests for arbitration/Sortan">2006</a></span> </li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="External_style_guides">External style guides</span></h3> 
      <p>Wikipedians are encouraged to familiarize themselves with modern editions of other guides to style and usage, which may cover details not included here. Those that have most influenced the Wikipedia Manual of Style are: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Chicago_Manual_of_Style" title="The Chicago Manual of Style">The Chicago Manual of Style</a></i> (University of Chicago Press). The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://faculty.cascadia.edu/cma/HIST148/cmscrib.pdf"><i>CMS Crib Sheet</i></a> is free online, and summarizes the main provisions.</li> 
       <li><i><a href="/wiki/Hart%27s_Rules" title="Hart's Rules">Oxford Guide to Style</a></i> (Oxford University Press). A compressed edition is available as <i>New Hart's Rules</i>. Available with its companion, the <i>Oxford Dictionary for Writers and Editors</i>, in one volume as <i>New Oxford Style Manual</i></li> 
       <li><i><a href="/wiki/Scientific_Style_and_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="Scientific Style and Format">Scientific Style and Format</a></i> (Council of Science Editors)</li> 
       <li><i><a href="/wiki/Garner%27s_Modern_English_Usage" title="Garner's Modern English Usage">Garner's Modern English Usage</a></i> (Oxford University Press)</li> 
       <li><i><a href="/wiki/Fowler%27s_Dictionary_of_Modern_English_Usage" class="mw-redirect" title="Fowler's Dictionary of Modern English Usage">Fowler's Dictionary of Modern English Usage</a></i> (Oxford University Press; primarily British English)</li> 
       <li><i><a href="/wiki/The_MLA_Style_Manual" class="mw-redirect" title="The MLA Style Manual">The MLA Style Manual</a></i> (Modern Language Association)</li> 
       <li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Elements_of_Style" title="The Elements of Style">The Elements of Style</a></i> by Strunk &amp; White</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>For additional reference works, see notable entries at <a href="/wiki/Style_guide" title="Style guide">Style guide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dictionary#Major_English_dictionaries" title="Dictionary">Dictionary &nbsp;Major English dictionaries</a>. </p>

          <th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="text-align: center;;width:6.9em;text-align:left;">Deletion&nbsp;<abbr title="explains the processes by which pages, revisions, and logs may be deleted">(?)</abbr></th>
          <td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;padding:0px">
           <div style="padding:0em 0.25em"></div>
           <table class="nowraplinks navbox-subgroup" style="border-spacing:0">
            <tbody>
             <tr>
              <th id="P" scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%;text-align:left; font-weight: normal;"><b><span style="color:#118811;"><abbr title="Policies"><span style="font-size:large">P</span></abbr></span></b></th>
              <td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
               <div style="padding:0em 0.25em"> 
                <ul>
                 <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Deletion_policy" title="Wikipedia:Deletion policy">Deletion policy</a></li> 
                 <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Proposed_deletion" title="Wikipedia:Proposed deletion">Proposed deletion</a> 
                  <ul>
